## Key Code

### PUC opcode contracts

`lopcodes.h` defines the relevant opcodes and notes:

```c
OP_GETTABLE,/* A B C R[A] := R[B][R[C]] */
OP_SETTABLE,/* A B C R[A][R[B]] := RK(C) */
OP_MMBIN,/* A B C call C metamethod over R[A] and R[B] */
OP_LEN,/* A B R[A] := #R[B] */
OP_CONCAT,/* A B R[A] := R[A].. ... ..R[A + B - 1] */
OP_CALL,/* A B C R[A], ... ,R[A+C-2] := R[A](...) */
OP_TAILCALL,/* A B C k return R[A](...) */
OP_RETURN,/* A B C k return R[A], ... ,R[A+B-2] */
OP_TFORPREP, OP_TFORCALL, OP_TFORLOOP
OP_SETLIST,/* A vB vC k R[A][vC+i] := R[A+i], 1 <= i <= vB */
OP_VARARG,/* A B C k R[A], ..., R[A+C-2] = varargs */
OP_GETVARG, /* A B C R[A] := R[B][R[C]], R[B] is vararg parameter */
OP_ERRNNIL,/* A Bx raise error if R[A] ~= nil ... */
```

Important notes in same file:

- CALL: `B == 0` uses previous `top`; `C == 0` sets `top` for next open instruction.
- VARARG: `C == 0` uses actual vararg count and sets top; `k` means vararg table in `R[B]`.
- RETURN: `B == 0` returns up to `top`.
- SETLIST: `B == 0` uses `top`; `k` extends `C` via following EXTRAARG.
- RETURN/TAILCALL `k` signals upvalue closing; `C > 0` signals hidden varargs.

### PUC arithmetic + MMBIN

`lcode.c` generates arithmetic op followed immediately by MMBIN companion:

```c
int pc = luaK_codeABCk(fs, op, 0, v1, v2, 0);
...
luaK_codeABCk(fs, mmop, v1, v2, cast_int(event), flip);  /* metamethod */
```

`lvm.c` fast arithmetic increments `pc` only on primitive success; otherwise dispatch falls through to next MMBIN. MMBIN then calls `luaT_trybinTM` and writes to original arithmetic result register:

```c
vmcase(OP_ADD) { op_arith(L, l_addi, luai_numadd); vmbreak; }

vmcase(OP_MMBIN) {
  Instruction pi = *(pc - 2);
  TValue *rb = vRB(i);
  TMS tm = (TMS)GETARG_C(i);
  StkId result = RA(pi);
  lua_assert(OP_ADD <= GET_OPCODE(pi) && GET_OPCODE(pi) <= OP_SHR);
  Protect(luaT_trybinTM(L, s2v(ra), rb, result, tm));
  vmbreak;
}
```

### PUC GETTABLE/SETTABLE

`lvm.c` fast path plus metamethod chain:

```c
vmcase(OP_GETTABLE) {
  TValue *rb = vRB(i);
  TValue *rc = vRC(i);
  if (ttisinteger(rc))
    luaV_fastgeti(rb, ivalue(rc), s2v(ra), tag);
  else
    luaV_fastget(rb, rc, s2v(ra), luaH_get, tag);
  if (tagisempty(tag))
    Protect(luaV_finishget(L, rb, rc, ra, tag));
}
```

`luaV_finishget`:
- non-table → `__index` or type error
- table miss without `__index` → nil
- function `__index` → call and place result
- table `__index` → repeat lookup with loop cap

SETTABLE similarly uses raw set/update, `__newindex` function/table chain, barrier, loop cap.

### PUC LEN/CONCAT

`luaV_objlen`:
- table without `__len` → `luaH_getn`
- strings → byte length
- otherwise `__len` or type error.

`luaV_concat`:
- converts convertible operands to strings
- invokes `__concat` when non-string/non-convertible
- handles yield continuation via `luaV_finishOp`.

### PUC CALL/TAILCALL/RETURN

`OP_CALL`:
```c
int b = GETARG_B(i);
int nresults = GETARG_C(i) - 1;
if (b != 0) L->top.p = ra + b;
if ((newci = luaD_precall(L, ra, nresults)) == NULL) ...
else goto startfunc;
```

`luaD_precall` retries through `tryfuncTM` for `__call`.

`OP_TAILCALL` computes vararg `delta`, closes upvalues when `k`, uses `luaD_pretailcall`.

`OP_RETURN` supports `B == 0` open return and `k` close path.

### PUC TFOR/SETLIST/VARARG/ERRNNIL

`OP_TFORPREP` swaps control/closing variables, creates TBC upvalue, jumps to TFORCALL.

`OP_TFORCALL` copies iterator/state/control into call slots and calls iterator.

`OP_TFORLOOP` continues if `R[A+3]` non-nil.

`OP_SETLIST`:
```c
n = GETARG_vB(i);
last = GETARG_vC(i);
if (n == 0) n = cast_uint(L->top.p - ra) - 1;
last += n;
if (TESTARG_k(i)) {
  last += GETARG_Ax(*pc) * (MAXARG_vC + 1);
  pc++;
}
for (; n > 0; n--) obj2arr(h, last - 1, val);
```

`OP_VARARG` calls `luaT_getvarargs`; `OP_GETVARG` calls `luaT_getvararg`.

`OP_ERRNNIL` in `.vendor/Lua/lvm.c`:
```c
if (!ttisnil(ra))
  halfProtect(luaG_errnnil(L, cl, GETARG_Bx(i)));
```

## Current repo/runtime facts

### Runtime op handlers

- `op/arithmetic.lua` implements numeric fast paths and skips MMBIN by `pc + 2`; on unsupported operand tags it records `frame.resume.a = a` and advances to MMBIN with `pc + 1`.
- `op_mmbin`, `op_mmbini`, `op_mmbink` currently `jump error(code = ERR_RUNTIME)`.
- `op/table.lua` GETTABLE/SETTABLE call `table_get/table_set`, which support table `__index`/`__newindex` chaining and callable metamethod exit through `prepare_call`.
- `op/misc.lua` LEN supports strings, table raw length with `__len`, and non-table `__len`. CONCAT currently calls `string_concat_range`, whose implementation only accepts already-string values and errors on non-string; `concat_mm` block currently errors.
- `op/call.lua` CALL/TAILCALL/RETURN use `prepare_call`, `adjust_results`, `return_from_lua`, `close_upvalues`, and `tbc_close_chain`.
- `op/loop.lua` TFORCALL is currently `ERR_RUNTIME`; TFORPREP only jumps; TFORLOOP checks `R[A+2]`, while PUC checks `R[A+3]` after TFORCALL layout.
- `op/closure.lua` fixed-count VARARG copies from explicit frame argument window; GETVARG is `ERR_RUNTIME`; VARARGPREP is no-op frame metadata.
- `op/misc.lua` ERRNNIL currently errors when value **is nil**, opposite of `.vendor/Lua/lvm.c` / `lopcodes.h` text.

### Runtime regions

- `regions_table.lua` table_get rejects non-table before metamethod lookup; PUC `luaV_finishget` checks `__index` on non-table via `luaT_gettmbyobj`.
- `regions_metamethod.lua` `get_metamethod` currently handles table metatables only; non-table type metatables are not represented there.
- `regions_string.lua` `string_concat_range` documents non-string conversion/metamethod selection as not pretending primitive success, but its `call_mm` continuation is never used; it errors on non-string.
- `regions_call.lua` `prepare_call` handles `__call` by shifting function/args and retrying classification.
- `regions_resume.lua` has explicit resume kinds for GETTABLE_MM, SETTABLE_MM, BINOP_MM, UNOP_MM, LEN_MM, CONCAT_MM, TFORLOOP_CALL, TBC_CLOSE, etc.
- `regions_error.lua` `tbc_close_chain` finds `__close` but currently errors instead of invoking it.

## Current LuaCompile facts

### ASDL vocabulary

`ssa_asdl/spongejit_lua_ssa.asdl` explicitly models:
- LuaSrc opcodes including MMBIN*, GETTABLE/SETTABLE, LEN, CONCAT, CALL/TAILCALL/RETURN, TFOR*, SETLIST, VARARG/GETVARG/ERRNNIL.
- LuaSem observations for protocol exits:
  - `CallProtocolObservation`
  - `CloseProtocolObservation`
  - `GenericForProtocolObservation`
  - `SetListProtocolObservation`
  - `GetVargProtocolObservation`
- LuaNF exits corresponding to those observations.
- MoonOut protocol tags: call, close, generic_for, setlist, getvarg.

### Source decode

`lua_src_from_puc_decode.lua` maps all PUC event names to LuaSrc. Important details:
- `CALL/TailCALL/RETURN` counts are passed through as `Count`.
- `RETURN` only captures `pc`, `a`, `b`; it does not preserve `C`/`k`.
- `SETLIST` decodes only `a`, `vb/b`, `vc/c`; does not preserve `k`/EXTRAARG in LuaSrc node.
- `ERRNNIL` decodes only `pc,a`; drops Bx/name index.
- MMBIN event mapping uses `c`/event → BinOp.

### Semantic lowering

`lua_src_to_lua_sem_lower.lua`:

- Arithmetic fast paths require evidence:
  - ADD/SUB require both source slots `IsI64`.
  - DIV/POW require `IsF64`.
  - K variants require const facts.
  - MOD/IDIV add non-zero divisor guard.
- MMBIN markers are semantic no-ops only if immediately preceded by an arithmetic opcode in the same lowered window; otherwise reject `UnsupportedSemanticCase`.
- GETTABLE/SETTABLE:
  - array path requires key slot `IsI64` and array payload/facts.
  - field path requires key const fact.
  - no generic table/metamethod semantic path.
- LEN:
  - requires `IsTable`, `ShapeEq`, `MetatableAbsent`, `ArrayLenOffset`, shape payload.
  - no string length or `__len` path in LuaCompile.
- CONCAT:
  - requires every source slot `IsString`.
  - no numeric-to-string conversion or `__concat` path.
- VARARG:
  - fixed count lowers to `VarargValue(base,index)`.
  - `nresults.value == 0` rejects.
- GETVARG:
  - lowers to `GetVargProtocolObservation`.
- VARARGPREP:
  - no effects; comment says frame setup is not hidden runtime action.
- RETURN:
  - `B=1` → Return0Observation.
  - `B=2` → one ReturnObservation.
  - all other counts, including `B=0`, reject.
- ERRNNIL:
  - accepts only if evidence proves slot is non-nil-like (`IsI64`, `IsF64`, table, closure, bool, true/false); otherwise missing fact.
- CALL/TAILCALL/CLOSE/TBC/TFOR*/SETLIST:
  - lower to protocol observations/exits, not full Lua semantics.

### MoonOut

- `moon_out_abi.lua` protocol tags:
  - call=6, close=7, generic_for=8, setlist=9, getvarg=10.
- `moon_out_emit.lua` emits:
  - CallProtocolExit → `out_tag=call`, `out_slot=base`, `out_narray=nargs`, `out_start=nresults`, `out_bool=tail`.
  - CloseProtocolExit → `out_tag=close`, `out_slot=slot`, `out_bool=tbc`.
  - GenericForProtocolExit → phase code in `out_event_kind`.
  - SetListProtocolExit → table slot, first value slot, narray, start.
  - GetVargProtocolExit → dst/base/index slots.
- `moon_out_validate.lua` treats these protocol exits as supported.

## Relationships

- `.vendor/Lua/lopcodes.h` + `lvm.c` define the semantic oracle.
- `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/src/constants.lua` mirrors opcode/TM order.
- `src/opcodes.lua` decodes instruction words and dispatches to `src/op/*.lua`.
- `src/op/*.lua` handlers call `regions_*` runtime fragments.
- SpongeJIT `lua_src_from_puc_decode.lua` maps PUC trace/event tables into ASDL `LuaSrc`.
- `lua_src_to_lua_sem_lower.lua` consumes LuaSrc + evidence and emits LuaSem effects/observations.
- `lua_sem_to_lua_nf_normalize.lua` turns observations into LuaNF protocol exits.
- `moon_out_emit.lua` turns LuaNF exits into typed MoonOut output protocol.

## Observations

- PUC arithmetic opcodes depend structurally on the immediately following MMBIN* companion. Runtime validation enforces this, and LuaCompile treats MMBIN* as no-op only after typed arithmetic lowered.
- Current LuaCompile “semantic” coverage can still reject valid generic Lua behavior because many decisions require evidence or only handle fast paths.
- `test_spongejit_lua_compile_completion.lua` explicitly marks generic ADD, GETTABLE, SETTABLE, LEN, CONCAT, variable VARARG, multivalue RETURN, and ERRNNIL as valid cases that must not reject.
- Several current MoonOut protocol exits are typed handoff records, not Lua semantic implementation: CALL/TAILCALL/CLOSE/TBC/TFOR*/SETLIST/GETVARG.
- `ERRNNIL` has a direct discrepancy: `.vendor/Lua` says/errors on `R[A] ~= nil`; current runtime/LuaCompile treat it as “must be non-nil” / error on nil or require non-nil proof.

## Knowledge-builder Output — 2026-06-02 10:02:32

### What Matters Most for This Problem

- **Semantic completeness vs protocol handoff**: valid Lua behavior cannot be counted as “compiled” if it exits to CALL/SETLIST/GETVARG/etc. protocols.
- **PVM discipline**: distinguish valid scalar phase boundaries from the PVM guide’s stronger flatten-early / uniform-command / for-loop execution target.
- **Obsolete test assumptions**: several tests encode rejected design choices as success criteria.
- **Information preservation**: current decode drops opcode bits needed for exact Lua semantics.
- **Semantic oracle alignment**: reset must align with PUC Lua semantics, not current runtime shortcuts.
- **Boundary clarity**: define what is a legitimate compiled exit, what is forbidden interpreter/protocol continuation, and what counts as rejection.

### Non-Obvious Observations

- Current scalar PVM phases are not themselves “wrong.” PVM explicitly allows scalar boundaries. The deeper conflict is that the scalar boundary returns large semantic objects that still contain nested NF/Contract structure, not an already-flattened command stream. Replacing scalar phases with handler phases would not by itself satisfy the PVM guide’s flatten-early discipline.

- `MoonOut.Kernel` is not really an output layer yet. It still carries `LuaNF.Program` and `LuaContract.Contract`, so MoonOut is closer to a wrapper around prior IR than a terminal representation. That means validation and emission are still structurally coupled to LuaNF variants.

- The current `out_tag` ABI is effectively a mini continuation protocol. Even though it is emitted as Moonlift source, tags such as `call`, `close`, `generic_for`, `setlist`, and `getvarg` encode “someone else must resume Lua semantics.” That conflicts with the rejected no-interpreter/protocol-handoff premise.

- The protocol exits are not isolated to MoonOut. They originate in LuaSem observations, become LuaNF exits, influence LuaContract derivation, affect foundry representative keys, are accepted by MoonOut validation, and are asserted by tests. Removing them is therefore not a local ABI cleanup; it invalidates a vertical assumption across the whole LuaCompile stack.

- Existing tests distinguish “no hidden helpers” for some cases, but still bless explicit protocol handoff for others. That creates an inconsistent safety bar: guard/truthiness paths are tested against fake boundaries, while CALL/SETLIST/GETVARG/etc. are allowed to be fake success.

- “All 85 opcode families are semantic” is misleading because rejection has moved inside semantic handlers. Opcode coverage currently measures handler presence, not semantic coverage. The completion gate is exposing that mismatch.

- `MissingFact` currently means “cannot specialize this valid Lua behavior,” but the rejected rejection-as-success model treated that as acceptable. Under a no-interpreter reset, facts must be separated conceptually from semantics: lack of evidence cannot automatically mean the operation is semantically unavailable.

- Generic Lua behavior and no-protocol-handoff are jointly stricter than either requirement alone. Generic ADD/GETTABLE/SETTABLE/LEN/CONCAT/CALL/VARARG/RETURN are not just missing fast paths; many require metamethod lookup, dynamic call behavior, open result counts, top handling, close chains, or resumable continuations.

- Current LuaSrc decoding loses information that becomes mandatory once there is no interpreter fallback:
  - `RETURN` drops `C` and `k`.
  - `SETLIST` drops `k` and EXTRAARG extension.
  - `ERRNNIL` drops Bx/name index.
  These losses were tolerable when cases could reject or protocol-exit, but not for exact compiled semantics.

- MMBIN is semantically tied to the immediately preceding arithmetic opcode. Treating MMBIN as a standalone no-op only works for primitive-specialized windows. Generic arithmetic needs the pair as one semantic unit, and window completeness becomes a hard invariant.

- `ERRNNIL` has an oracle-level contradiction: PUC says it errors on `R[A] ~= nil`, while current runtime/LuaCompile behave as if nil is the failing case / non-nil proof is success. Coding before resolving this risks baking in the wrong semantics.

- The current “MoonOut must not receive PUC opcode-shaped code” test is too weak. Absence of `LuaSrc.Op` constructors does not prove semantic lowering; NF exits can still encode opcode-shaped continuation behavior.

- The PVM guide’s uniform `Cmd` expectation implies a stronger invariant than “we have a list of steps.” Current NF has heterogeneous exit constructors and MoonOut emission dispatches by ASDL class. That remains variant-dispatch lowering, not uniform command execution.

- The current pointer-out ABI is also philosophically misaligned with Moonlift’s typed continuation/control model. It externalizes control as integers and mutable out-params rather than preserving explicit typed control edges.

- Foundry dedupe by `LuaNF + LuaContract` depends on the current meaning of exits and obligations. If protocol exits are no longer valid terminal semantics, representative keys may be deduping partial behaviors that should not be considered equivalent compiled kernels.

- Runtime interpreter modules contain more generic semantics than LuaCompile, but they are themselves interpreter/continuation machinery and contain known mismatches/incompleteness. Treating them as a semantic source without a clear boundary would reintroduce the rejected design in another form.

- CALL/RETURN/VARARG/SETLIST all depend on Lua’s dynamic `top` behavior. The current compiler often rejects open counts or turns them into protocol exits. A flat no-interpreter design must clarify how `top`-sensitive semantics are represented before any code changes.

### Knowledge Gaps

- What exits remain legitimate under “no interpreter”? Guard/deopt exits may be acceptable, but CALL/SETLIST/GETVARG-style semantic handoffs appear rejected. The boundary needs an explicit rule.

- Is the reset expected to support all valid generic Lua behavior now, or only stop calling rejection/protocol handoff “success”?

- What is the intended final PVM shape: scalar phase returning a flat ASDL command array, handler-form phases with installed methods, or something else?

- What is the stable semantic oracle for discrepancies between `.vendor/Lua` and `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/src`, especially `ERRNNIL`, TFOR layout, CONCAT, metamethods, and close behavior?

- Does the PUC event stream contain the opcode fields currently dropped by `lua_src_from_puc_decode.lua`? If not, exact lowering may be blocked at the input boundary.

## Approach-proposer Output — 2026-06-02 10:03:15

### Approach A: Honest Partial Flat Compiler
- **Core idea**: Keep LuaCompile conservative, but make success mean “fully compiled flat MoonOut commands,” never protocol handoff.
- **Key changes**:
  - Remove/ban `CallProtocolExit`, `CloseProtocolExit`, `GenericForProtocolExit`, `SetListProtocolExit`, `GetVargProtocolExit` as successful exits.
  - Add a terminal flat ASDL layer, e.g. `MoonOut.Cmd = (Kind kind, ...)`, and make `MoonOut.Kernel` carry `Cmd*` instead of `LuaNF.Program`.
  - Update `lua_sem_to_lua_nf_normalize.lua`, `lua_nf_to_moon_out_lower.lua`, `moon_out_validate.lua`, `moon_out_emit.lua`.
  - Rewrite tests that currently treat protocol exits or rejection as coverage.
- **Tradeoff**: Optimizes for architectural honesty and fast reset; sacrifices generic Lua completeness.
- **Risk**: The completion tests for valid generic Lua behavior will stay red until later semantic work exists.
- **Rough sketch**:
  - Define a whitelist of legitimate compiled exits: guard/deopt, return, jump/branch, hard error.
  - Change semantic lowering so protocol-only cases reject with explicit unsupported reasons.
  - Flatten accepted NF into uniform `MoonOut.Cmd*`.
  - Make MoonOut emission a simple `for _, cmd in ipairs(kernel.cmds)` dispatcher.
  - Foundry dedupes by flat command stream + contract, not protocol exits.

### Approach B: Full Semantic Microcode Layer
- **Core idea**: Replace protocol handoffs with a compiled Lua semantic microcode layer that can express generic table, metamethod, call, vararg, return, close, and loop behavior as flat commands.
- **Key changes**:
  - Add a new ASDL layer between `LuaNF` and `MoonOut`, e.g. `LuaExec.Cmd`.
  - Decode must preserve missing opcode fields: `RETURN C/k`, `SETLIST k/EXTRAARG`, `ERRNNIL Bx`.
  - Lower generic operations into explicit command sequences: metamethod lookup, table chains, `top` handling, `__call`, varargs, close chains.
  - MoonOut becomes a backend for `LuaExec.Cmd*`, not `LuaNF.Exit`.
- **Tradeoff**: Optimizes for semantic completeness under no-interpreter rules; sacrifices implementation size and migration speed.
- **Risk**: Reimplementing PUC semantics in compiler IR may duplicate or diverge from `.vendor/Lua`.
- **Rough sketch**:
  - Use `.vendor/Lua` as oracle and fix source decode information loss first.
  - Model runtime state explicitly in ASDL: stack, top, frame, constants, upvalues, table/value refs.
  - Define uniform command product: `Cmd(kind, dst, srcs, immediates, labels, obligations)`.
  - Lower each Lua semantic family into bounded command sequences or command-region loops.
  - Emit Moonlift from the flat command list with jump-first control and no out-tag continuation ABI.

### Approach C: Typed Region Target with Flat Emit Commands
- **Core idea**: Treat MoonOut as a flat list of commands that splice typed Moonlift regions, where generic Lua behavior is implemented as reusable compiled regions rather than external protocols.
- **Key changes**:
  - Introduce `MoonOut.Cmd` whose main operation is “emit this typed semantic region with these operands and continuations.”
  - Replace pointer/tag ABI with typed Moonlift continuations/unions.
  - Build a region library for generic semantics: table get/set, arithmetic metamethod, concat, len, call preparation, vararg adjustment, close chain.
  - `moon_out_emit.lua` emits region definitions/usages from flat commands.
- **Tradeoff**: Optimizes for reuse and Moonlift philosophy fit; sacrifices strict “all semantics visible as primitive commands” transparency.
- **Risk**: Region emits could become disguised helpers unless their contracts and continuation edges are fully typed and validated.
- **Rough sketch**:
  - Define flat `Cmd(kind, region, args, ok_cont, error_cont, guard_cont)` ASDL.
  - Convert protocol exits into internal typed regions only when the region fully implements the Lua semantics.
  - Validate that every region continuation is resolved inside the compiled kernel boundary.
  - Emit Moonlift `region`/`emit` code instead of integer `out_tag` protocols.
  - Keep PVM scalar phase boundaries, but make the final boundary return only flat `Cmd*`.

### Comparison

Pick **A** for a fast, honest reset that removes fake coverage first.  
Pick **B** if the goal is full Lua semantic compilation as explicit microcode.  
Pick **C** if the goal is full semantics while leaning into Moonlift’s typed region composition instead of a large primitive micro-op language.

## Critique Output — 2026-06-02 10:04:22

### Approach A: Honest Partial Flat Compiler

| Dimension | Score (1-5) | Rationale |
|-----------|-------------|-----------|
| **Coupling** | 2/5 | Lowers coupling by making `MoonOut.Kernel` stop carrying `LuaNF.Program` directly. Still requires vertical cleanup across LuaSem → LuaNF → Contract → Foundry → tests because protocol exits are embedded everywhere. |
| **Cohesion** | 4/5 | Clear responsibility split: semantic lowering may be partial, but MoonOut success means flat compiled output only. This makes “compiler output” cohesive again. |
| **Migration cost** | 3/5 | Non-trivial but bounded: remove/ban protocol exits as success, add flat `MoonOut.Cmd*`, update validation/emission/tests/foundry keys. Avoids implementing full Lua semantics immediately. |
| **Philosophy fit** | 5/5 | Best immediate fit with PVM_GUIDE flatten-early/uniform-Cmd expectations and Moonlift’s fail-fast/no-hidden-fallback principles. Scalar PVM phases can remain valid. |
| **Risk** | 2/5 | Main risk is political/test-expectation risk: completion remains red and coverage shrinks. Architecturally, risk of fake protocol handoff is lowest. |
| **Testability** | 5/5 | Highly testable incrementally: assert no protocol exits in accepted kernels, assert `MoonOut.Kernel` carries flat cmds only, rewrite fake-success tests, preserve scalar phase cache tests. |

**Verdict**: Strong yes  
**Key concern**: The boundary between legitimate compiled exits and forbidden semantic handoffs must be explicit and enforced, or the fake-success pattern will reappear under new names.

---

### Approach B: Full Semantic Microcode Layer

| Dimension | Score (1-5) | Rationale |
|-----------|-------------|-----------|
| **Coupling** | 4/5 | Decouples MoonOut from LuaNF, but tightly couples the compiler IR to detailed PUC runtime semantics: stack/top, metamethods, varargs, close chains, calls, table protocols, errors. |
| **Cohesion** | 3/5 | A `LuaExec.Cmd` layer has a coherent purpose, but the layer risks becoming a large embedded VM semantics model rather than a small compilation target. |
| **Migration cost** | 5/5 | Deep refactor. Requires decode fixes, new ASDL, new lowerings for generic Lua behavior, backend rewrite, contract/foundry changes, and test suite redefinition. |
| **Philosophy fit** | 4/5 | Strong on ASDL, flat commands, no out-tag continuation ABI, and no interpreter handoff. Weaker because it risks duplicating a VM inside compiler microcode. |
| **Risk** | 5/5 | Highest unknown-unknown risk. PUC semantics are subtle, current runtime has known discrepancies, and missing decoded fields block correctness unless resolved first. |
| **Testability** | 3/5 | Can be tested opcode-family by opcode-family, but cross-cutting semantics like CALL/RETURN/top/metamethod/yield/close interactions make incremental validation hard. |

**Verdict**: Significant concerns  
**Key concern**: Semantic divergence from `.vendor/Lua` is the critical danger; this approach can easily become a second, subtly wrong Lua implementation.

---

### Approach C: Typed Region Target with Flat Emit Commands

| Dimension | Score (1-5) | Rationale |
|-----------|-------------|-----------|
| **Coupling** | 3/5 | Better than protocol exits because continuations stay typed and internal, but MoonOut becomes coupled to a semantic region library and its contracts. |
| **Cohesion** | 4/5 | Cohesive if regions are true compiled semantic units and `MoonOut.Cmd` remains a flat emit-command layer. Less transparent than primitive microcode. |
| **Migration cost** | 4/5 | Requires replacing pointer/tag ABI, introducing flat region commands, building/validating region library, and changing emission/tests. Less exhaustive than B, more invasive than A. |
| **Philosophy fit** | 5/5 | Very strong Moonlift fit: typed continuations, regions, `emit`, no integer out-tag protocol, flat final command boundary. Also compatible with scalar PVM phases. |
| **Risk** | 4/5 | Main risk is disguised helper/protocol handoff: regions can become the same old interpreter boundary unless contracts prove all continuations resolve inside the compiled kernel. |
| **Testability** | 4/5 | Region contracts and continuation closure can be tested incrementally. Harder than A because “fully implements Lua semantics” is a semantic claim, not just a structural one. |

**Verdict**: Yes with caveats  
**Key concern**: Region emits must be compiled semantic splices, not opaque helper calls or external continuation protocols.

---

### Summary

- **Recommended**: **Approach A**. It best matches the immediate reset goal: stop calling protocol handoff or rejection “compiled success,” align MoonOut with flat command output, and avoid premature full-Lua implementation.
- **Dark horse**: **Approach C**. It has the most upside if the project wants fuller semantics while staying idiomatic to Moonlift’s typed region model.
- **Avoid**: **Approach B** for now. It is architecturally clean in theory but too large and risky before oracle gaps, decode loss, and current runtime discrepancies are resolved.

## Documenter Output — 2026-06-02 10:12:01

```markdown
# SpongeJIT LuaCompile/MoonOut Typed Region Target Blueprint

**Status:** Selected architecture blueprint; design reset in effect; implementation frozen until the open design questions in this document are resolved.  
**Workflow ID:** `wf-b7b79a56`

## Goal

Enable SpongeJIT `LuaCompile` to emit honest Moonlift kernels for Lua bytecode windows: successful compilation must mean a flat, typed MoonOut command stream that emits compiled Moonlift regions, with no Lua interpreter fallback, no host protocol handoff, and no rejection counted as success.

## Problem / Trust Reset

This reset exists because the previous green tests did not prove compiled Lua semantics. Several dynamic Lua behaviors were treated as “compiled” by emitting protocol exits such as `call`, `close`, `generic_for`, `setlist`, and `getvarg`, which required some external host/interpreter continuation to finish the operation. Other tests treated structured rejection as acceptable coverage for valid Lua behavior. This produced dishonest confidence: the pipeline could appear successful while either punting semantics to a protocol boundary or rejecting valid Lua cases.

The selected design rejects that model. A MoonOut success must be self-contained compiled control, expressed through typed Moonlift regions and continuations, not integer out-tags or mutable pointer out-params.

## Incentives

This matters because the current pipeline has multiple trust failures:

- `MoonOut.Kernel` still carries `LuaNF.Program` and `LuaContract.Contract`, so MoonOut is not yet a true terminal flat backend layer.
- Protocol exits originate in `LuaSem`, survive through `LuaNF`, affect `LuaContract`, are accepted by `MoonOut` validation, emitted by `moon_out_emit.lua`, and asserted by tests.
- The `out_tag` ABI is effectively a continuation protocol, not compiled semantics.
- Tests currently encode rejected assumptions, especially that protocol exits are valid success cases.
- The completion gate is red for valid Lua behavior such as generic `ADD`, `GETTABLE`, `SETTABLE`, `LEN`, `CONCAT`, variable-count `VARARG`, multivalue `RETURN`, and `ERRNNIL`.
- Current opcode “coverage” only proves that handlers exist; rejection now happens inside semantic handlers.
- Source decoding drops information needed for exact semantics, including `RETURN C/k`, `SETLIST k/EXTRAARG`, and `ERRNNIL Bx`.

The reset’s purpose is not to patch individual opcodes until green. It is to restore a trustworthy definition of compilation success.

## PVM_GUIDE Grounding

The design is grounded in the PVM guide’s ASDL and phase discipline.

### Immutable, interned ASDL values

Compilation state must remain explicit ASDL data. Meaningful compiler state must not hide in strings, callbacks, side tables, or runtime-only conventions. Existing layers already follow this principle structurally:

- `LuaSrc` answers what PUC encoded.
- `LuaEvidence` answers what runtime/foundry proved.
- `LuaSem` answers semantic meaning under evidence.
- `LuaNF` answers normalized semantic computation.
- `LuaContract` answers obligations and transferred facts.
- `MoonOut` must become the terminal compiled output layer.

The reset requires MoonOut to stop being a wrapper around earlier IR and become explicit flat output data.

### Named `pvm.phase` boundaries

The current LuaCompile phases are scalar `pvm.phase(name, fn)` boundaries used with `pvm.one(...)`. This is valid PVM usage. The problem is not scalar phases themselves.

Current scalar boundaries include:

- `lua_src_to_lua_sem_lower.lua`
- `lua_sem_to_lua_nf_normalize.lua`
- `lua_nf_to_lua_contract_derive.lua`
- `lua_nf_to_moon_out_lower.lua`
- `lua_compile_to_normal_form.lua`
- `lua_compile_to_moon_kernel.lua`

These boundaries may remain scalar if their outputs are single ASDL values. The reset does not require converting them to handler-form phases merely for method installation.

### Method-installation meaning

Handler-form `pvm.phase(name, handlers)` installs `:name(...)` methods only on the handled ASDL types. Scalar function-form phases do not imply such methods. Existing tests around scalar phase caching are therefore not invalid simply because they do not use installed ASDL methods.

### Flatten early, uniform command/product layer

The PVM guide’s stronger target is:

- uniform `Cmd` product shape,
- containment via push/pop markers where needed,
- for-loop execution over flat commands,
- state represented explicitly, not via recursive dispatch or nested IR trees.

The selected architecture applies this to MoonOut: the final kernel representation must be a flat list of uniform MoonOut commands. Emission should operate by iterating over `kernel.cmds`, not by recursively interpreting `LuaNF` variants.

## Current State

### ASDL structure

The relevant schema is in:

`experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/ssa_asdl/spongejit_lua_ssa.asdl`

The current ASDL stack includes `LuaSrc`, `LuaEvidence`, `LuaSem`, `LuaNF`, `LuaContract`, `LuaPlace`, and `MoonOut`.

Current `LuaNF.Exit` includes normal exits such as guards, returns, jumps, conditional jumps, and loop-region exits, but also protocol exits:

- `CallProtocolExit`
- `CloseProtocolExit`
- `GenericForProtocolExit`
- `SetListProtocolExit`
- `GetVargProtocolExit`

Current `MoonOut.Kernel` is:

```asdl
Kernel = (MoonOut.KernelKind kind,
          MoonOut.Param* params,
          LuaNF.Program normal_form,
          LuaContract.Contract contract,
          MoonOut.Projection* projections) unique
```

This means MoonOut still contains the normalized Lua program and contract directly. It is not yet a flattened terminal command layer.

### Current data flow

The current pipeline is:

```text
PUC event tables
  -> lua_src_from_puc_decode.decode
  -> LuaSrc.Window
  -> LuaCompile.Unit(source, evidence)
  -> lua_src_to_lua_sem_lower.lower(window, evidence)
       returns LuaSem.Accepted(program) or LuaSem.Rejected(rejection)
  -> lua_sem_to_lua_nf_normalize.normalize(program)
       turns observations into LuaNF steps/exits
  -> lua_nf_to_lua_contract_derive.derive(nf)
       derives obligations and dependencies
  -> lua_compile_to_normal_form.compile(unit)
       returns LuaCompile.Ok(NormalForm(nf, contract)) or Reject
  -> lua_nf_to_moon_out_lower.lower(nf, contract)
       wraps NF + contract into MoonOut.Kernel
  -> moon_out_emit.emit(kernel)
       emits Moonlift source using out_* protocol parameters
```

The foundry path dedupes representatives by `LuaNF + LuaContract`, so protocol exits currently affect artifact identity.

### Current protocol output ABI

`experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/moon_out_abi.lua` defines integer output tags:

```lua
ok = 0
return_ = 1
guard = 2
jump = 3
loop_region = 4
branch = 5
call = 6
close = 7
generic_for = 8
setlist = 9
getvarg = 10
```

It also defines pointer out-params such as:

- `out_tag`
- `out_value_kind`
- `out_pc`
- `out_slot`
- `out_narray`
- `out_start`
- `out_bool`
- `out_event_kind`
- `out_event_count`

`moon_out_emit.lua` writes those tags for protocol exits. For example, `CallProtocolExit` becomes `out_tag = call`; `SetListProtocolExit` becomes `out_tag = setlist`.

This is the old rejected boundary: it is typed as Moonlift output, but semantically it says “someone else must continue Lua execution.”

### Current semantic limitations

`lua_src_to_lua_sem_lower.lua` handles many opcode families but often only for specialized evidence-backed cases:

- arithmetic requires primitive type facts;
- `GETTABLE`/`SETTABLE` handle limited array/field paths;
- `LEN` requires table shape and no metatable;
- `CONCAT` requires all operands already strings;
- fixed-count `VARARG` works, open-count does not;
- one-value and zero-value returns work, multivalue/open returns do not;
- `CALL`, `TAILCALL`, `CLOSE`, `TBC`, `TFOR*`, `SETLIST`, and `GETVARG` become protocol observations.

The completion tests expose that valid generic Lua behavior remains unimplemented.

### Current test tension

Some tests already enforce “no fake helper” behavior for guards and truthiness, but other tests bless protocol exits as success. This is inconsistent.

The main suite must stop treating these as green:

- protocol out-tags as compiled success,
- structured rejection of valid behavior as success,
- absence of `LuaSrc.Op` inside `MoonOut.Kernel` as sufficient proof of semantic lowering.

## Rejected Old Assumptions

The reset explicitly rejects these assumptions:

1. **Protocol out-tags are not success.**  
   `call`, `close`, `generic_for`, `setlist`, and `getvarg` out-tags are host/interpreter continuation protocols, not compiled semantics.

2. **Host/interpreter handoff is not MoonOut compilation.**  
   A compiled kernel may not rely on a Lua interpreter, opcode helper, resume protocol, or external dispatcher to finish Lua semantics.

3. **Rejection is not success for valid Lua behavior.**  
   Unsupported valid behavior may remain unimplemented, but tests must not count rejection as a positive compiled result.

4. **Primitive opcode patches are frozen until design is settled.**  
   Individual fixes to `ADD`, `GETTABLE`, `SETLIST`, `VARARG`, etc. must not proceed without the flat region-command target and continuation policy.

5. **MoonOut may not remain a wrapper around `LuaNF.Program`.**  
   The output layer must become a terminal command layer.

## Chosen Target

### Approach

The selected design is the **Typed Moonlift Region Target**.

MoonOut becomes a flat list of commands. Each command emits or references a typed Moonlift semantic region. Generic Lua behavior is implemented inside compiled Moonlift regions, not by returning protocol tags to the host.

This choice preserves the Moonlift philosophy: typed control edges, explicit continuations, zero-cost region splicing via `emit`, and no integer continuation protocol.

### Architecture

#### Layer shape

MoonOut must be reshaped around a flat command product.

The exact ASDL syntax remains to be finalized before coding, but the required shape is:

```asdl
module MoonOut {
    Kernel = (
        MoonOut.KernelKind kind,
        MoonOut.Param* params,
        MoonOut.Cmd* cmds,
        ...
    ) unique

    Cmd = (
        MoonOut.CmdKind kind,
        MoonOut.RegionRef region,
        MoonOut.Operand* args,
        MoonOut.ContBinding* continuations,
        MoonOut.Obligation* obligations
    ) unique
}
```

The important invariant is not the exact field names; it is that `Kernel` carries flat `Cmd*`, not `LuaNF.Program`.

`Cmd` must be one uniform product shape. Semantic variation belongs in ASDL-visible fields such as `kind`, `region`, operands, continuation bindings, and obligations, not in hidden Lua closures or opaque string protocols.

#### Meaning of a MoonOut flat command

A `MoonOut.Cmd` means:

> Emit this typed Moonlift semantic region with these operands and these typed continuations.

It is not:

- a PUC opcode,
- a Lua interpreter instruction,
- a host callback request,
- a protocol exit record,
- a string of Moonlift source carrying hidden semantics.

A command is valid only if the referenced region fully implements the semantic operation it claims to represent, or if it represents a legitimate typed kernel boundary such as a return/error/guard boundary according to the continuation rules.

#### Typed region requirements

A Moonlift region used by MoonOut must satisfy:

- It is a compiled Moonlift `region` or equivalent typed fragment.
- Its parameters are typed data parameters.
- Its exits are typed continuations.
- All continuation edges are explicit at the `emit` site.
- Its contract is represented in ASDL-visible data.
- It does not call back into the Lua interpreter to complete semantics.
- It does not encode control as integer tags plus mutable out-params.
- It may be reusable, but reuse must be through typed region composition, not opaque helper dispatch.

Examples of region families that may eventually exist under this model include table get/set, arithmetic metamethod handling, concat, len, call preparation, vararg adjustment, close chains, and generic-for behavior. They are legal only when they fully implement the relevant Lua semantics for their claimed domain.

#### Continuation rules

Continuations such as `ok`, `error`, `yield`, `guard`, branch, return, or other semantic exits must be typed Moonlift continuations and resolved inside the compiled kernel boundary.

They must not become:

```text
out_tag = call
out_tag = setlist
out_tag = getvarg
out_tag = generic_for
```

or any equivalent host protocol under another name.

If a kernel exposes a boundary result, that boundary must be typed and explicit in Moonlift control/data terms. It must not be an untyped integer tag protocol requiring an external interpreter dispatcher.

#### Legal helpers

Legal helper-like reuse is limited to compiled, typed Moonlift composition:

- `region` definitions emitted or referenced by MoonOut;
- `emit` sites with explicit continuation bindings;
- typed fragments whose semantics and obligations are ASDL-visible;
- primitive operations that are truly primitive for the backend and not hidden Lua semantic interpreters.

#### Illegal helpers

The following are illegal in accepted MoonOut kernels:

- Lua interpreter handoff;
- opcode helper calls such as old `OpcodeHelper`/`HelperCall` patterns;
- host callbacks that implement Lua semantics outside the compiled kernel;
- integer `out_tag` protocol exits;
- mutable `out_*` pointer protocols as semantic continuation ABI;
- side tables that carry semantic meaning not represented in ASDL;
- tests that assert rejection or protocol handoff as success.

### Data flow after reset

The intended data flow becomes:

```text
LuaSrc.Window + LuaEvidence
  -> LuaSem / semantic lowering
  -> LuaNF / normalized semantics where still useful
  -> LuaContract
  -> MoonOut lowering
       produces MoonOut.Kernel(cmds = flat Cmd*)
  -> MoonOut validation
       proves command/region/continuation closure
  -> MoonOut emission
       for _, cmd in ipairs(kernel.cmds) do
           emit typed Moonlift region usage
       end
```

The final boundary is `MoonOut.Cmd*`, not `LuaNF.Program`.

### Tradeoffs acknowledged

This design sacrifices some transparency compared with a primitive microcode model: generic Lua semantics may live inside reusable typed regions rather than being expanded into tiny primitive commands.

That is acceptable because Moonlift’s native abstraction is typed region composition. The critical requirement is that regions are compiled semantic splices with typed continuations, not opaque helpers or interpreter protocols.

This design is more invasive than merely banning protocol exits because it requires replacing the pointer/tag ABI and defining region contracts. It is still preferred because it supports fuller Lua semantics without building a second hand-written Lua VM microcode language.

### Risks acknowledged

Known risks from critique:

- Typed regions can become disguised helpers if their contracts and continuation edges are not explicit and validated.
- MoonOut may become coupled to a semantic region library.
- Proving that a region fully implements Lua semantics is harder than structurally banning protocol tags.
- Migration cost is higher than the minimal honest-partial reset.
- Existing runtime modules contain useful semantic fragments but also known discrepancies; importing them blindly could reintroduce interpreter machinery or wrong semantics.

The design therefore requires strict validation and design-first implementation discipline.

## Required ASDL Layer Shape

Before coding, the ASDL must be revised so that MoonOut has a true terminal flat layer.

Required properties:

- `MoonOut.Kernel` must contain `MoonOut.Cmd*`.
- `MoonOut.Kernel` must not contain `LuaNF.Program` as executable payload.
- `MoonOut.Cmd` must be one uniform product shape.
- Region identity, operands, continuations, and obligations must be ASDL-visible.
- Protocol exits must not appear as successful terminal commands.
- Any remaining projections or obligations must describe typed command/region requirements, not host continuation protocols.

Existing protocol exit constructors may be removed, quarantined, or made non-successful, but they must no longer be accepted as compiled MoonOut success.

## Test Policy

The main test suite must contain positive intended behavior tests only.

Allowed main-suite tests:

- accepted kernels contain flat `MoonOut.Cmd*`;
- accepted kernels contain no protocol exits;
- accepted kernels contain no `out_tag` continuation ABI;
- accepted kernels emit typed Moonlift regions with resolved continuations;
- implemented Lua behavior runs or validates as intended;
- invariant violations fail loudly.

Disallowed main-suite success patterns:

- “valid Lua behavior rejects” as a passing test;
- “protocol exit emitted” as a passing test;
- “no `LuaSrc.Op` appears” as sufficient proof of semantic compilation;
- primitive opcode patch tests that bypass the selected architecture.

Valid but unimplemented Lua behavior should naturally fail until implemented. It should not be represented as green coverage.

## Migration Implications

The reset affects the whole LuaCompile/MoonOut stack:

- `ssa_asdl/spongejit_lua_ssa.asdl` must gain the flat MoonOut command/region shape.
- `LuaSem` and `LuaNF` protocol observations/exits must stop flowing into successful MoonOut kernels.
- `lua_sem_to_lua_nf_normalize.lua` must no longer normalize protocol observations into accepted terminal protocol exits.
- `lua_nf_to_lua_contract_derive.lua` must stop deriving success obligations around protocol handoffs.
- `lua_nf_to_moon_out_lower.lua` must lower into flat `MoonOut.Cmd*`.
- `moon_out_validate.lua` must validate command/region/continuation closure.
- `moon_out_emit.lua` must emit typed Moonlift region usage, not pointer out-tag protocol writes.
- `moon_out_abi.lua` must lose the semantic protocol tag role.
- Foundry representative keys must no longer dedupe partial protocol behaviors as compiled kernels.
- Tests asserting old protocol behavior must be rewritten or removed.
- Decode information loss must be addressed before exact semantics for affected opcodes can be implemented.

## Open Questions Before Coding

These must be decided before implementation begins:

1. What is the exact ASDL schema for `MoonOut.Cmd`, `RegionRef`, operands, continuation bindings, and obligations?
2. What typed kernel boundary replaces the old `out_tag` ABI for return/error/guard/yield-style outcomes?
3. Which continuation kinds are legal in the first version?
4. Which semantic regions are in scope for the first migration slice?
5. How is “region fully implements this Lua semantic case” validated?
6. How will foundry representative keys be computed from flat commands and contracts?
7. How will source decode preserve missing fields for `RETURN C/k`, `SETLIST k/EXTRAARG`, and `ERRNNIL Bx`?
8. Which oracle resolves discrepancies between `.vendor/Lua` and current runtime modules, especially `ERRNNIL`, `TFOR`, `CONCAT`, metamethod lookup, and close behavior?
9. Can existing `regions_*` runtime code be reused as Moonlift region source, or must it be re-authored to avoid interpreter/resume machinery?
10. What tests move out of the main suite because they only assert rejection/protocol handoff?

## Implementation Freeze / Design-First Rule

No opcode-by-opcode patches, protocol-exit renames, ABI tweaks, or test-green changes should be implemented until the above design questions are answered.

The reset is architectural. The first implementation work must establish the flat MoonOut command layer, typed region continuation rules, and validation boundary. Only then should individual Lua semantic families be migrated.
```

## Documenter Output — 2026-06-02 10:16:54

```markdown
# SpongeJIT LuaCompile/MoonOut CFG-ASDL Blueprint

**Workflow ID:** `wf-b7b79a56`  
**Status:** Architecture decision blueprint. This revises the earlier MoonOut typed-region direction into a sharper requirement: the compiled control-flow graph itself must be an explicit ASDL model. Moonlift source emission is a mechanical rendering step, not a semantic lowering step.

## Goal

Enable SpongeJIT `LuaCompile` to compile Lua bytecode windows into a self-contained ASDL-described Moonlift CFG, so successful compilation means `LuaSrc/LuaSem/LuaNF -> MoonCFG ASDL -> Moonlift source` with no Lua interpreter dependency, no host protocol handoff, and no rejection counted as successful coverage.

## Problem / Trust Reset

The current pipeline can report success without proving compiled Lua semantics. Dynamic Lua operations such as `CALL`, `TAILCALL`, `CLOSE`, `TFOR*`, `SETLIST`, and `GETVARG` are currently lowered into protocol observations, normalized into `LuaNF.*ProtocolExit` variants, accepted by `MoonOut`, and emitted as integer `out_tag` results. That is not compiled semantics; it is a request for some external host/interpreter protocol to continue Lua execution.

The reset rejects that model. A successful MoonOut kernel must contain an explicit compiled CFG. Every semantic choice must be represented by ASDL enums/sum types. Typed Moonlift regions are not opaque helper strings; they are ASDL CFG/region fragments made of blocks, operations, expressions, places, continuations, and terminators. `moon_out_emit.lua` must only render this ASDL CFG into Moonlift source mechanically.

## Incentives

This matters because the existing architecture creates false confidence:

- `MoonOut.Kernel` currently carries `LuaNF.Program` and `LuaContract.Contract`, so MoonOut is a wrapper around earlier IR rather than a terminal compiled representation.
- The pointer/tag ABI in `moon_out_abi.lua` exposes tags such as `call`, `close`, `generic_for`, `setlist`, and `getvarg`, which encode external continuation protocols.
- Protocol exits are vertical assumptions: they originate in `LuaSem`, flow through `LuaNF`, affect `LuaContract`, influence foundry dedupe keys, pass validation, and are asserted by tests.
- Completion tests are red for valid Lua behavior including generic `ADD`, `GETTABLE`, `SETTABLE`, `LEN`, `CONCAT`, variable-count `VARARG`, multivalue `RETURN`, and `ERRNNIL`.
- Existing opcode “semantic coverage” only proves that handlers exist; many valid cases still reject internally due to missing facts or unsupported semantic cases.
- Current source decoding loses fields required for exact semantics: `RETURN C/k`, `SETLIST k/EXTRAARG`, and `ERRNNIL Bx`.
- The old “no `LuaSrc.Op` inside MoonOut” test is too weak: NF protocol exits can still encode opcode-shaped semantic handoffs.

The reset restores a strict definition: compiled success means an ASDL CFG that fully describes the compiled computation and its typed exits.

## PVM Grounding

The current LuaCompile phases are scalar `pvm.phase(name, fn)` boundaries used with `pvm.one(...)`. This is valid PVM usage. The problem is not scalar phases.

Relevant current scalar phases include:

- `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/lua_src_to_lua_sem_lower.lua`
- `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/lua_sem_to_lua_nf_normalize.lua`
- `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/lua_nf_to_lua_contract_derive.lua`
- `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/lua_nf_to_moon_out_lower.lua`
- `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/lua_compile_to_normal_form.lua`
- `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/lua_compile_to_moon_kernel.lua`

PVM’s stronger requirement is the final representation shape: flatten early, use uniform command/product structures, avoid recursive dispatch over nested IR trees, and keep meaningful state in ASDL. The chosen design satisfies this by introducing a terminal `MoonCFG` ASDL layer. PVM phase boundaries may remain scalar if they return one interned ASDL value, but the final returned value must be an explicit flat/structured CFG, not `LuaNF.Program` plus ad hoc emitter logic.

## Current State

### ASDL Layers

The main schema is:

`experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/ssa_asdl/spongejit_lua_ssa.asdl`

It currently defines:

- `LuaSrc`: decoded PUC bytecode operations.
- `LuaEvidence`: runtime/foundry facts.
- `LuaSem`: semantic effects/observations under evidence.
- `LuaNF`: normalized semantic computation.
- `LuaContract`: facts, payload uses, projection obligations, dependencies.
- `MoonOut`: emitted Moonlift-level kernel boundary.

Current `LuaNF.Exit` includes normal exits and protocol exits:

- `GuardExit`
- `ReturnExit`
- `Return0Exit`
- `JumpExit`
- `ConditionalJumpExit`
- `TestSetExit`
- `LoopRegionExit`
- `CallProtocolExit`
- `CloseProtocolExit`
- `GenericForProtocolExit`
- `SetListProtocolExit`
- `GetVargProtocolExit`

Current `MoonOut.Kernel` is structurally still tied to LuaNF:

```asdl
Kernel = (MoonOut.KernelKind kind,
          MoonOut.Param* params,
          LuaNF.Program normal_form,
          LuaContract.Contract contract,
          MoonOut.Projection* projections) unique
```

That is the central design tension: the final layer is not final.

### Current Data Flow

```text
PUC event tables
  -> lua_src_from_puc_decode.decode
  -> LuaSrc.Window
  -> LuaCompile.Unit(source, evidence)
  -> lua_src_to_lua_sem_lower.lower(window, evidence)
       returns LuaSem.Accepted(program) or LuaSem.Rejected(rejection)
  -> lua_sem_to_lua_nf_normalize.normalize(program)
       turns observations into LuaNF steps/exits
  -> lua_nf_to_lua_contract_derive.derive(nf)
       derives facts, payload uses, projections, deps
  -> lua_compile_to_normal_form.compile(unit)
       returns LuaCompile.Ok(NormalForm(nf, contract)) or Reject
  -> lua_nf_to_moon_out_lower.lower(nf, contract)
       wraps NF + contract into MoonOut.Kernel
  -> moon_out_emit.emit(kernel)
       emits Moonlift source using pointer out-params and integer tags
```

The foundry path dedupes by `LuaNF + LuaContract`, so protocol exits currently affect representative identity.

### Current ABI Problem

`experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/moon_out_abi.lua` defines an integer tag protocol:

```lua
M.TAG = {
  ok = 0,
  return_ = 1,
  guard = 2,
  jump = 3,
  loop_region = 4,
  branch = 5,
  call = 6,
  close = 7,
  generic_for = 8,
  setlist = 9,
  getvarg = 10,
}
```

`moon_out_emit.lua` writes these through mutable pointer parameters such as `out_tag`, `out_slot`, `out_narray`, `out_start`, and `out_event_kind`.

That ABI externalizes Lua control as integer tags. Under the reset, this is forbidden for semantic continuation.

## Chosen Target

The chosen target is:

```text
LuaSrc / LuaSem / LuaNF
  -> MoonCFG ASDL
  -> Moonlift source
```

`MoonCFG` is the terminal compiled representation. It fully describes the compiled CFG that Moonlift will receive. It is not a string template layer and not a wrapper around `LuaNF.Program`.

Moonlift regions are represented as ASDL CFG fragments:

- regions,
- blocks,
- params,
- operations,
- expressions,
- places,
- values,
- typed continuations,
- terminators,
- typed exit protocols.

Emission is mechanical: traverse `MoonCFG.Module`, render declarations, render regions/kernels, render blocks, render operations, render terminators. Emission must not decide Lua semantics.

## MoonCFG ASDL Vocabulary Sketch

Exact field names may change during implementation, but the required shape is below.

```asdl
module MoonCFG {
  Module = (
    MoonCFG.Region* regions,
    MoonCFG.Kernel* kernels
  ) unique

  Kernel = (
    MoonCFG.KernelId id,
    MoonCFG.KernelKind kind,
    MoonCFG.Param* params,
    MoonCFG.Region body,
    LuaContract.Contract contract
  ) unique

  Region = (
    MoonCFG.RegionId id,
    MoonCFG.Param* params,
    MoonCFG.Continuation* continuations,
    MoonCFG.BlockId entry,
    MoonCFG.Block* blocks
  ) unique

  Block = (
    MoonCFG.BlockId id,
    MoonCFG.Param* params,
    MoonCFG.Op* ops,
    MoonCFG.Terminator terminator
  ) unique

  Param = (
    MoonCFG.Name name,
    MoonCFG.TypeRef type,
    MoonCFG.ParamMode mode
  ) unique

  Continuation = (
    MoonCFG.ContId id,
    MoonCFG.Param* params,
    MoonCFG.ContinuationKind kind
  ) unique

  Op =
      Let(MoonCFG.Place dst, MoonCFG.Expr expr)
    | Assign(MoonCFG.Place dst, MoonCFG.Value src)
    | Store(MoonCFG.Place dst, MoonCFG.Value src)
    | EmitRegion(MoonCFG.RegionRef region,
                 MoonCFG.Arg* args,
                 MoonCFG.ContBinding* continuations)
    | Project(MoonCFG.Place dst,
              MoonCFG.Value src,
              MoonCFG.Projection projection)
    | Assert(MoonCFG.Expr condition,
             MoonCFG.ExitProtocol on_fail)

  Terminator =
      Jump(MoonCFG.BlockRef target, MoonCFG.Arg* args)
    | Branch(MoonCFG.Choice choice,
             MoonCFG.BlockRef if_true,
             MoonCFG.BlockRef if_false)
    | Switch(MoonCFG.Choice choice,
             MoonCFG.SwitchArm* arms,
             MoonCFG.BlockRef default)
    | Continue(MoonCFG.ContRef continuation, MoonCFG.Arg* args)
    | Return(MoonCFG.Value* values)
    | Exit(MoonCFG.ExitProtocol protocol, MoonCFG.Arg* args)
    | Unreachable

  Expr =
      ValueExpr(MoonCFG.Value value)
    | Primitive(MoonCFG.PrimOp op, MoonCFG.Value* args)
    | Load(MoonCFG.Place place)
    | AddressOf(MoonCFG.Place place)
    | Convert(MoonCFG.TypeRef type, MoonCFG.Value value)
    | Select(MoonCFG.Choice choice,
             MoonCFG.Value if_true,
             MoonCFG.Value if_false)

  Value =
      PlaceValue(MoonCFG.Place place)
    | ConstValue(MoonCFG.Const const)
    | ParamValue(MoonCFG.Name name)
    | UnitValue

  Place =
      StackSlot(int index)
    | ConstSlot(int index)
    | UpvalueSlot(int index)
    | VarargSlot(int index)
    | Temp(MoonCFG.Name name)
    | FrameTop
    | ExecCtx
    | TableField(MoonCFG.Value table, MoonCFG.Value key)
    | ArrayElement(MoonCFG.Value table, MoonCFG.Value index)

  Choice =
      BoolChoice(MoonCFG.Value value)
    | NilChoice(MoonCFG.Value value)
    | TypeChoice(MoonCFG.Value value, MoonCFG.TypeTest test)
    | NumericChoice(MoonCFG.NumericTest test,
                    MoonCFG.Value left,
                    MoonCFG.Value right)
    | EqualityChoice(MoonCFG.Value left, MoonCFG.Value right)
    | MetamethodPresentChoice(MoonCFG.Value value,
                              MoonCFG.Metamethod metamethod)
    | GuardChoice(LuaContract.Guard guard)

  ExitProtocol =
      ReturnExit
    | ErrorExit
    | GuardDeoptExit
    | YieldExit
    | UnsupportedExit

  KernelKind =
      InlineSpan
    | FunctionFastPath

  ContinuationKind =
      LocalContinuation
    | RegionOk
    | RegionError
    | RegionYield
    | RegionGuardFail
    | KernelExit

  ParamMode =
      ValueParam
    | ReadonlyPtr
    | WriteonlyPtr
    | NoaliasPtr

  PrimOp =
      AddI64 | SubI64 | MulI64 | DivF64 | ModI64 | IDivI64
    | Eq | Lt | Le
    | Not | Truthy
    | LoadTag | LoadArrayLen
    | RawGet | RawSet
    | CheckNil | CheckNonNil
    | StringLen | StringConcatPrimitive

  TypeTest =
      IsNil | IsBool | IsI64 | IsF64 | IsString | IsTable
    | IsClosure | IsFunction | IsThread | IsUserdata

  Metamethod =
      Add | Sub | Mul | Mod | Pow | Div | IDiv | Band | Bor | Bxor
    | Shl | Shr | Unm | Bnot | Eq | Lt | Le | Index | NewIndex
    | Call | Len | Concat | Close

  Projection =
      ValueKind
    | Payload
    | ArrayLength
    | Shape
    | Metatable
}
```

### Required Properties

- `MoonCFG.Module` is the terminal compiled output model.
- `MoonCFG.Kernel` must not contain executable `LuaNF.Program`.
- Semantic variants must be ASDL choices, not strings.
- Moonlift region bodies must be represented as `MoonCFG.Region` / `Block` / `Op` / `Terminator`.
- Emitter logic must not inspect Lua opcodes to decide semantics.
- Emitter logic may only render the already-decided CFG.

Names may be strings when they are identifiers. Strings must not encode semantic choices, protocol tags, operation kinds, or hidden contracts.

## Forbidden Patterns

Accepted kernels must not contain or depend on:

1. **Stringly semantic tags**  
   No `"call"`, `"setlist"`, `"generic_for"`, `"getvarg"`, etc. as semantic control tags. These must be ASDL enum/sum constructors if they are legitimate internal choices.

2. **Integer `out_tag` protocol ABI**  
   No semantic continuation through `out_tag`, `out_event_kind`, or equivalent mutable integer protocol fields.

3. **Host/interpreter handoff**  
   No successful kernel may require a Lua interpreter, opcode dispatcher, resume protocol, or host callback to finish Lua semantics.

4. **Protocol exits as success**  
   `CallProtocolExit`, `CloseProtocolExit`, `GenericForProtocolExit`, `SetListProtocolExit`, and `GetVargProtocolExit` are not compiled success.

5. **Opaque helpers**  
   Reusable code is allowed only as ASDL-described CFG regions/fragments. Helpers that hide Lua semantics outside `MoonCFG` are forbidden.

6. **Rejection-as-success**  
   Rejecting valid Lua behavior may be the current implementation limitation, but tests must not count it as successful compilation.

7. **MoonOut wrapping LuaNF**  
   `MoonOut.Kernel` / `MoonCFG.Kernel` must not carry `LuaNF.Program` as the executable payload.

## How Generic Lua Operations Compile

Generic Lua operations must become CFG regions/fragments, not protocol exits.

### Arithmetic / MMBIN

Generic arithmetic must model the PUC arithmetic + `MMBIN*` pair as one semantic unit when necessary.

Compiled CFG may include:

- primitive numeric fast path blocks,
- type-choice branches,
- metamethod lookup blocks,
- metamethod-call region,
- result projection blocks,
- error exits.

The `MMBIN*` marker must not become a standalone no-op unless the primitive-specialized arithmetic window proves that the marker is unreachable semantically.

### GETTABLE / SETTABLE

Generic table access must become CFG regions for:

- table raw get/set,
- array/index fast paths,
- field/const-key paths,
- `__index` / `__newindex` lookup,
- table-chain continuation,
- function metamethod call,
- loop-limit/type-error exits.

It must not become `out_tag = gettable` or any equivalent host request.

### LEN

Generic `LEN` must become CFG covering:

- string byte length,
- table raw length when no `__len`,
- `__len` metamethod lookup/call,
- type-error exit.

Current table-shape-only lowering remains a specialization, not full generic coverage.

### CONCAT

Generic `CONCAT` must become CFG covering:

- string operands,
- numeric-to-string conversion where valid,
- `__concat` lookup/call,
- continuation after metamethod result,
- error paths.

Current all-operands-string lowering remains a specialization.

### CALL / TAILCALL

Generic call behavior must become CFG covering:

- function classification,
- `__call` metamethod retry,
- argument/result count handling,
- tailcall behavior,
- upvalue close behavior when required,
- typed return/error/yield continuations.

It must not become `CallProtocolExit`.

### RETURN

Return semantics must preserve and compile the relevant PUC fields:

- fixed count,
- open count via `top`,
- `C`,
- `k` close behavior,
- hidden vararg behavior where applicable.

Multivalue/open returns are valid Lua behavior and must not be counted green by rejection.

### VARARG / GETVARG

Vararg behavior must become CFG over explicit frame/vararg places:

- fixed-count copy,
- open-count copy and `top` update,
- vararg table behavior,
- `GETVARG` lookup semantics.

It must not become `GetVargProtocolExit`.

### SETLIST

`SETLIST` must become CFG covering:

- fixed value count,
- open count from `top`,
- `k` / `EXTRAARG` extension,
- array write loop,
- table/barrier semantics as required by the chosen runtime model.

It must not become `SetListProtocolExit`.

### CLOSE / TBC

Close behavior must become CFG covering:

- close-chain traversal,
- `__close` lookup,
- close-call sequencing,
- error/unwind behavior.

It must not become `CloseProtocolExit`.

### Generic For

`TFORPREP`, `TFORCALL`, and `TFORLOOP` must become CFG covering:

- iterator/state/control layout,
- iterator call,
- result placement,
- nil test,
- loop continuation,
- close behavior where applicable.

It must not become `GenericForProtocolExit`.

## Emission Rules

`moon_out_emit.lua` must become a renderer from `MoonCFG` to Moonlift source.

Allowed emitter responsibilities:

- assign stable source names for ASDL identifiers;
- render types, params, blocks, regions, expressions, operations, and terminators;
- render `emit` sites for ASDL-described regions;
- render typed continuations exactly as represented in ASDL;
- preserve deterministic output.

Forbidden emitter responsibilities:

- inspect `LuaSrc.Op` to choose semantics;
- interpret `LuaNF.Exit` as executable behavior;
- lower protocol exits into tags;
- synthesize hidden helper calls;
- encode semantic choices as strings or integer tags;
- decide metamethod/table/call semantics during printing.

The semantic lowering decision must already be present in `MoonCFG`.

## Test Policy

The main test suite must assert intended compiled behavior and structural honesty.

### Required Positive Tests

- Accepted compile result contains `MoonCFG.Module` / `MoonCFG.Kernel`.
- Accepted kernel body contains `MoonCFG.Region` / `Block` / `Op` / `Terminator`.
- Accepted kernel does not contain executable `LuaNF.Program`.
- Accepted kernel does not contain protocol exits.
- Accepted emitted source has no integer `out_tag` semantic continuation ABI.
- Accepted emitted source uses typed Moonlift regions/continuations.
- Emitter is mechanical: given a fixed `MoonCFG`, output is deterministic.
- Generic operation tests become green only when the corresponding CFG semantics exist.

### Required Negative Tests

- `CallProtocolExit`, `CloseProtocolExit`, `GenericForProtocolExit`, `SetListProtocolExit`, and `GetVargProtocolExit` cannot pass MoonCFG/MoonOut validation as compiled success.
- Stringly semantic tags are rejected.
- Unknown enum/sum choices fail validation.
- Hidden helper/protocol calls fail validation.
- Rejection of valid Lua behavior is not asserted as success.

### Tests to Rewrite or Remove

Tests that currently bless protocol exits as success must be rewritten. Tests that only prove absence of `LuaSrc.Op` inside MoonOut are insufficient and must be replaced with assertions over `MoonCFG` structure.

## Migration Steps

1. **Add `MoonCFG` ASDL vocabulary**  
   Extend `spongejit_lua_ssa.asdl` or add a new schema module for `MoonCFG.Module`, `Kernel`, `Region`, `Block`, `Op`, `Terminator`, `Expr`, `Value`, `Place`, `Continuation`, `ExitProtocol`, and choice enums.

2. **Change final compile target**  
   Replace `LuaCompile.MoonKernel` / `MoonOut.Kernel` payloads so successful output carries `MoonCFG.Kernel` or `MoonCFG.Module`, not executable `LuaNF.Program`.

3. **Quarantine protocol exits**  
   Stop treating `CallProtocolExit`, `CloseProtocolExit`, `GenericForProtocolExit`, `SetListProtocolExit`, and `GetVargProtocolExit` as valid compiled terminal results.

4. **Introduce MoonCFG validation**  
   Add validation that checks:
   - all choices are ASDL constructors,
   - continuations are typed and resolved,
   - region references resolve,
   - no forbidden protocol exits appear,
   - no stringly semantic tags appear,
   - no hidden host/interpreter handoff appears.

5. **Rewrite MoonOut lowering**  
   Change `lua_nf_to_moon_out_lower.lua` or replace it with `lua_nf_to_moon_cfg_lower.lua`, lowering accepted NF/contract data into explicit CFG regions.

6. **Rewrite MoonOut emission**  
   Change `moon_out_emit.lua` so it renders `MoonCFG` mechanically. Remove semantic `out_tag` emission.

7. **Adjust ABI module**  
   Remove or quarantine semantic tag definitions in `moon_out_abi.lua`. Any remaining ABI must describe typed kernel data boundaries, not semantic continuation protocols.

8. **Update foundry keys**  
   Foundry representatives must dedupe by `MoonCFG` plus relevant contract data, not by protocol-exit-containing `LuaNF`.

9. **Fix source decode information loss**  
   Preserve fields required for exact semantics:
   - `RETURN C/k`,
   - `SETLIST k/EXTRAARG`,
   - `ERRNNIL Bx`.

10. **Rewrite tests**  
    Remove old green assertions for protocol exits and rejection-as-success. Add structural `MoonCFG` validation tests before expanding generic semantic coverage.

11. **Migrate operations incrementally**  
    Each generic Lua operation becomes accepted only when its semantics are represented as CFG regions/fragments. Until then, unsupported cases may reject, but rejection is not success.

## Open Questions Before Coding

These must be answered before implementation begins:

1. Should `MoonCFG` live inside `spongejit_lua_ssa.asdl` or in a separate ASDL schema file?
2. What is the exact boundary between `LuaNF` and `MoonCFG`?
3. Which existing `LuaNF.Exit` variants remain legitimate inputs to CFG lowering?
4. What exact typed `ExitProtocol` variants are allowed for compiled kernels?
5. How are Moonlift types represented in ASDL: reuse existing type refs or define `MoonCFG.TypeRef`?
6. How are region identifiers, block identifiers, and continuation identifiers interned?
7. What is the first minimal accepted CFG slice?
8. How should `LuaContract.Contract` attach to `MoonCFG`: kernel-level, region-level, op-level, or obligation-level?
9. What validation proves a region is not an opaque helper?
10. How should generic metamethod calls be represented without reintroducing interpreter resume protocols?
11. How should `top` be modeled for `CALL`, `RETURN`, `VARARG`, and `SETLIST`?
12. What source event data is available for preserving `RETURN C/k`, `SETLIST k/EXTRAARG`, and `ERRNNIL Bx`?
13. Which oracle resolves discrepancies between `.vendor/Lua` and current runtime modules, especially `ERRNNIL`, `TFOR`, `CONCAT`, metamethod lookup, and close behavior?
14. What old tests move out of the main suite because they only asserted protocol handoff or rejection?

## Summary

The selected architecture is a full CFG-ASDL target:

```text
LuaSrc / LuaSem / LuaNF
  -> MoonCFG ASDL
  -> mechanical Moonlift source rendering
```

The compiled CFG is the product. Moonlift source is only its textual rendering. Protocol tags, stringly semantic choices, hidden helpers, interpreter handoff, and rejection-as-success are forbidden in accepted kernels.
```

   - Add constructors:
     ```asdl
     module MoonCFG {
         Name = (string text) unique
         TypeRef = (string moon_type) unique
         KernelId = (MoonCFG.Name name) unique
         RegionId = (MoonCFG.Name name) unique
         BlockId = (MoonCFG.Name name) unique
         ContId = (MoonCFG.Name name) unique

         KernelKind = InlineSpan | FunctionFastPath

         ParamMode = ValueParam | ReadonlyPtr | WriteonlyPtr | NoaliasPtr
         Param = (MoonCFG.Name name, MoonCFG.TypeRef type, MoonCFG.ParamMode mode) unique

         ContinuationKind = LocalContinuation | RegionOk | RegionError | RegionYield | RegionGuardFail | KernelExit
         Continuation = (MoonCFG.ContId id, MoonCFG.Param* params, MoonCFG.ContinuationKind kind) unique

         RegionRef = (MoonCFG.RegionId id) unique
         BlockRef = (MoonCFG.BlockId id) unique
         ContRef = (MoonCFG.ContId id) unique

         Const = I64Const(number value) unique
               | F64Const(number value) unique
               | BoolConst(boolean value) unique
               | StringConst(string value) unique

         Place = StackSlot(number index) unique
               | ConstSlot(number index) unique
               | UpvalueSlot(number index) unique
               | VarargSlot(number index) unique
               | Temp(MoonCFG.Name name) unique
               | FrameTop unique
               | ExecCtx unique
               | TableField(MoonCFG.Value table, MoonCFG.Value key) unique
               | ArrayElement(MoonCFG.Value table, MoonCFG.Value index) unique

         Value = PlaceValue(MoonCFG.Place place) unique
               | ConstValue(MoonCFG.Const const) unique
               | ParamValue(MoonCFG.Name name) unique
               | UnitValue unique

         PrimOp = AddI64 | SubI64 | MulI64 | DivF64 | ModI64 | IDivI64
                | Eq | Lt | Le | Not | Truthy
                | LoadTag | LoadArrayLen | RawGet | RawSet
                | CheckNil | CheckNonNil
                | StringLen | StringConcatPrimitive

         Expr = ValueExpr(MoonCFG.Value value) unique
              | Primitive(MoonCFG.PrimOp op, MoonCFG.Value* args) unique
              | Load(MoonCFG.Place place) unique
              | AddressOf(MoonCFG.Place place) unique
              | Convert(MoonCFG.TypeRef type, MoonCFG.Value value) unique

         Arg = (MoonCFG.Name name, MoonCFG.Value value) unique

         TypeTest = IsNil | IsBool | IsI64 | IsF64 | IsString | IsTable
                  | IsClosure | IsFunction | IsThread | IsUserdata

         NumericTest = NumEq | NumLt | NumLe | NumGt | NumGe | NumNonZero

         Metamethod = Add | Sub | Mul | Mod | Pow | Div | IDiv | Band | Bor | Bxor
                    | Shl | Shr | Unm | Bnot | Eq | Lt | Le | Index | NewIndex
                    | Call | Len | Concat | Close

         Choice = BoolChoice(MoonCFG.Value value) unique
                | NilChoice(MoonCFG.Value value) unique
                | TypeChoice(MoonCFG.Value value, MoonCFG.TypeTest test) unique
                | NumericChoice(MoonCFG.NumericTest test, MoonCFG.Value left, MoonCFG.Value right) unique
                | EqualityChoice(MoonCFG.Value left, MoonCFG.Value right) unique
                | MetamethodPresentChoice(MoonCFG.Value value, MoonCFG.Metamethod metamethod) unique
                | GuardChoice(LuaContract.FactUse* facts) unique

         ExitProtocol = ReturnExit | ErrorExit | GuardDeoptExit | YieldExit | UnsupportedExit

         Projection = ValueKind | Payload | ArrayLength | Shape | Metatable

         ContBinding = (MoonCFG.ContRef continuation, MoonCFG.BlockRef target) unique

         Op = Let(MoonCFG.Place dst, MoonCFG.Expr expr) unique
            | Assign(MoonCFG.Place dst, MoonCFG.Value src) unique
            | Store(MoonCFG.Place dst, MoonCFG.Value src) unique
            | EmitRegion(MoonCFG.RegionRef region, MoonCFG.Arg* args, MoonCFG.ContBinding* continuations) unique
            | Project(MoonCFG.Place dst, MoonCFG.Value src, MoonCFG.Projection projection) unique
            | Assert(MoonCFG.Expr condition, MoonCFG.ExitProtocol on_fail) unique

         SwitchArm = (MoonCFG.Const match, MoonCFG.BlockRef target) unique

         Terminator = Jump(MoonCFG.BlockRef target, MoonCFG.Arg* args) unique
                    | Branch(MoonCFG.Choice choice, MoonCFG.BlockRef if_true, MoonCFG.BlockRef if_false) unique
                    | Switch(MoonCFG.Value value, MoonCFG.SwitchArm* arms, MoonCFG.BlockRef default) unique
                    | Continue(MoonCFG.ContRef continuation, MoonCFG.Arg* args) unique
                    | Return(MoonCFG.Value* values) unique
                    | Exit(MoonCFG.ExitProtocol protocol, MoonCFG.Value* args) unique
                    | Unreachable unique

         Block = (MoonCFG.BlockId id, MoonCFG.Param* params, MoonCFG.Op* ops, MoonCFG.Terminator terminator) unique

         Region = (MoonCFG.RegionId id,
                   MoonCFG.Param* params,
                   MoonCFG.Continuation* continuations,
                   MoonCFG.BlockId entry,
                   MoonCFG.Block* blocks) unique

         Kernel = (MoonCFG.KernelId id,
                   MoonCFG.KernelKind kind,
                   MoonCFG.Param* params,
                   MoonCFG.TypeRef* returns,
                   MoonCFG.Region body,
                   LuaContract.Contract contract) unique

         Module = (MoonCFG.Region* regions, MoonCFG.Kernel* kernels) unique
     }

  ```

  local function name(s) return CFG.Name(s) end

  ```

  - `ConstI64` -> `const_N_i64: i64`
  - `ToF64(SrcSlotTValue)` -> `slot_N_f64: f64`
  - `ConstF64` -> `const_N_f64: f64`

**Danger zones**

#### `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/moon_cfg_validate.lua`

**Purpose**: Validate MoonCFG structural honesty before emission.

**Contents sketch**
- Imports:
  ```lua
  local pvm = require("moonlift.pvm")
  local Validate = require("lua_compile.validate")
  local B = require("lua_compile.builders")
  local T = B.T
  local CFG, NF = T.MoonCFG, T.LuaNF
  ```
- Implement generic ASDL walk.
- `FORBIDDEN_PARAM_NAMES`:
  - reject names matching `^out_`
  - reject exact `out_tag`, `out_event_kind`
- `FORBIDDEN_PROTOCOL_EXITS`:
  ```lua
  NF.CallProtocolExit,
  NF.CloseProtocolExit,
  NF.GenericForProtocolExit,
  NF.SetListProtocolExit,
  NF.GetVargProtocolExit
  ```
- Validate:
  - kernel is `MoonCFG.Kernel`
  - no `LuaNF.Program` appears recursively
  - no forbidden protocol exit appears recursively, including inside attached `LuaContract.Contract`
  - no string semantic tags: reject strings equal to `"call"`, `"close"`, `"generic_for"`, `"setlist"`, `"getvarg"`, `"out_tag"`
  - region entry block exists
  - all block ids in a region are unique
  - all `Jump`/`Branch`/`Switch` targets resolve
  - first migration slice: require exactly one block unless support for multi-block rendering is added
- Export:
  ```lua
  function M.validate(kernel) ... end
  ```

**Danger zones**
- Validator must fail closed. Unknown node shapes should produce errors, not silently pass.
- Do not whitelist protocol exits.

  local pvm = require("moonlift.pvm")

  - single-block kernel body

  - `Expr.Primitive(AddI64/SubI64/MulI64/IDivI64/ModI64/DivF64)`
  - `Terminator.Return`
- `M.emit(kernel, opts)`:
  - validate first
  - render:
    ```moonlift
    local <name> = func(<params>) -> <return-type>
        ...
        return <value>
    end

    return <name>
    ```
- Deterministic output: no table-pair iteration without sorted keys.

**Danger zones**
- Emitter must never inspect `LuaSrc` or `LuaNF` to decide semantics.
- Emitter must not output `out_tag`, protocol params, or helper calls.

#### `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/lua_nf_to_moon_cfg_lower.lua`

**Purpose**: Lower supported `LuaNF.Program + LuaContract.Contract` into `MoonCFG.Kernel`.

**Contents sketch**
- Imports:
  ```lua
  local pvm = require("moonlift.pvm")
  local B = require("lua_compile.builders")
  local T = B.T
  local NF, CFG = T.LuaNF, T.MoonCFG
  local Abi = require("lua_compile.moon_cfg_abi")
  ```
- Phase name:
  ```lua
  pvm.phase("spongejit_lua_nf_to_moon_cfg_lower", function(nf, contract) ...)
  ```
- Initial helpers:
  - `new_state()`: temp counter, ops array.
  - `temp(state, prefix)`
  - `lower_i64(state, nf_i64)`: support `CanonAffineI64`, `CanonMulI64`, `CanonIDivI64`, `CanonModI64`.
  - `lower_f64(state, nf_f64)`: support `ToF64(SrcSlotTValue)`, `ConstF64`, `DivF64`.
  - `lower_tvalue_for_return(state, value)`: initially support `BoxI64TValue`, `BoxF64TValue`, maybe `BoolTValue`.
  - `terminal_exit(nf)`: find first `StepExit`; reject unsupported exit kinds.
- Build:
  ```lua
  CFG.Kernel(
    CFG.KernelId(CFG.Name("lua_compile_kernel")),
    CFG.InlineSpan,
    Abi.params_for_nf(nf),
    { CFG.TypeRef("i64") }, -- or f64/bool/void depending terminal
    body_region,
    contract
  )
  ```
- Reject/unsupported behavior:
  - If NF contains `CallProtocolExit`, `CloseProtocolExit`, `GenericForProtocolExit`, `SetListProtocolExit`, `GetVargProtocolExit`, return `nil, { "forbidden_protocol_exit:..." }` or error with clear message.
  - First slice may only lower terminal `ReturnExit` with scalar i64/f64/bool.

**Danger zones**
- Do not lower protocol exits into `Exit(UnsupportedExit)` and call it success.
- Do not carry `nf` into the kernel.

**Contents sketch**

- Skip fields named `contract` so foundry can explicitly combine `MoonCFG + LuaContract`.
- Export `M.key(kernel)`.

#### `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/moon_out_abi.lua`
