#### `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/lua_compile_to_moon_kernel.lua`

**Goal**: Compile to `MoonCFG.Kernel` and return `Reject` if CFG lowering is unsupported.

**Edit blocks**

1. **Lines 4-6**:
   - Change require:
     ```lua
     local MoonLower = require("lua_compile.lua_nf_to_moon_cfg_lower")
     ```

2. **Lines 11-16**: Handle lowering failure.
   - Before:
     ```lua
     local kernel = MoonLower.lower(product.nf, product.contract)
     return T.LuaCompile.Ok(T.LuaCompile.MoonKernel(kernel))
     ```
   - After:
     ```lua
     local kernel, lower_errors = MoonLower.lower(product.nf, product.contract)
     if not kernel then
       return T.LuaCompile.Reject(MoonLower.rejection_for(product.nf, lower_errors))
     end
     return T.LuaCompile.Ok(T.LuaCompile.MoonKernel(kernel))
     ```
   - Add `rejection_for` helper in `lua_nf_to_moon_cfg_lower.lua` that creates `LuaSem.Rejection` with:
     - pc `0` if no source pc recoverable,
     - reason `UnsupportedSemanticCase`,
     - source op `LuaSrc.UnsupportedOpcode(Pc(0), "moon_cfg_lower")`.

**Danger zones**
- Do not throw for normal unsupported CFG lowering through public compile path; return `Reject`.
- Throw only for internal invariants.

---

#### `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/lua_src_to_lua_sem_lower.lua`

**Goal**: Stop protocol-only operations from becoming accepted semantic observations.

**Edit blocks**

1. **Lines 482-501**: Replace `CALL`, `TAILCALL`, `CLOSE`, `TBC`, `TFORPREP`, `TFORCALL`, `TFORLOOP` protocol observations with explicit unsupported rejection.
   - Example:
     ```lua
     add_decision("CALL", "semantic", function(_ctx, op)
       return reject(op, "unsupported_semantic_case")
     end)
     ```
   - Add comment:
     ```lua
     -- CFG reset: these are valid Lua operations but not accepted compiled
     -- success until represented as MoonCFG regions. Do not emit protocol observations.
     ```

2. **Lines 513-527**: Replace `SETLIST` and `GETVARG` protocol observations with unsupported rejection.

3. **Lines 529-535 comment for `VARARGPREP`**:
   - Remove language saying `GETVARG` is a “dynamic-index protocol exit”.
   - Replace with:
     ```lua
     -- GETVARG and open VARARG require MoonCFG region semantics before success.
     ```

**Danger zones**
- This is not a success test for rejection. It is a safety gate preventing fake success.
- Leave fixed-count `VARARG` behavior as-is if already semantic.

#### `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/lua_sem_to_lua_nf_normalize.lua`

**Goal**: Prevent protocol observations from normalizing into accepted NF exits.

**Edit blocks**

1. **Lines 194-212**: Replace all protocol-observation branches with hard internal failure:
   ```lua
   elseif obs.kind == "CallProtocolObservation"
       or obs.kind == "CloseProtocolObservation"
       or obs.kind == "GenericForProtocolObservation"
       or obs.kind == "SetListProtocolObservation"
       or obs.kind == "GetVargProtocolObservation" then
     error("forbidden protocol observation reached LuaNF normalization: " .. tostring(obs.kind))
   end
   ```

**Danger zones**
- Do not silently drop observations.
- Do not convert them to `UnsupportedExit`.

#### `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/tests/test_spongejit_lua_compile_moon_out.lua`

**Goal**: Replace old tag/protocol runtime test with MoonCFG structural/mechanical-renderer tests.

**Edit blocks**

1. **Replace entire file.**

**New test contents outline**
- Imports:
  ```lua
  local moon = require("moonlift")
  local C = require("lua_compile")
  local Validate = require("lua_compile.moon_cfg_validate")
  local Emit = require("lua_compile.moon_cfg_emit")
  local Schema = require("lua_compile.schema")
  local pvm = require("moonlift.pvm")
  local T = Schema.get()
  ```
- Helpers:
  - `kernel_from(events, evidence)`
  - recursive `contains_class_member(v, member_table)`
  - recursive string search for forbidden strings.
- Positive structural test:
  ```lua
  local kernel = kernel_from({ {op="LOADI",pc=1,a=1,b=42}, {op="RETURN1",pc=2,a=1} }, {})
  assert(pvm.classof(kernel) == T.MoonCFG.Kernel)
  assert(kernel.normal_form == nil)
  assert(kernel.body and kernel.body.blocks and #kernel.body.blocks == 1)
  assert(kernel.body.blocks[1].terminator.kind == "Return")
  assert(not contains LuaNF.Program)
  ```
- Validation:
  ```lua
  local ok, errs = Validate.validate(kernel)
  assert(ok, table.concat(errs, "\n"))
  ```
- Emission:
  ```lua
  local src = Emit.emit(kernel, { name = "test_moon_cfg_loadi" })
  assert(src:match("local test_moon_cfg_loadi = func"))
  assert(not src:match("out_tag"))
  assert(not src:match("out_event_kind"))
  assert(not src:match("generic_for") and not src:match("getvarg") and not src:match("setlist"))
  assert(src == Emit.emit(kernel, { name = "test_moon_cfg_loadi" }))
  ```
- Compile/run simple scalar:
  ```lua
  local fn = assert(moon.loadstring(src, "=(test_moon_cfg_loadi)"))()
  local native = assert(fn:compile())
  assert(native() == 42)
  native:free()
  ```
- ADDI scalar test:
  - Compile `{ ADDI, RETURN1 }` with `is_i64`.
  - Assert param `slot_1_i64`.
  - Compile and call with `41`, expect `42`.
- Negative protocol success tests:
  ```lua
  for _, op in ipairs({ "CALL", "TAILCALL", "CLOSE", "TBC", "TFORPREP", "TFORCALL", "TFORLOOP", "SETLIST", "GETVARG" }) do
    local r = C.compile_to_moon_kernel(C.unit_from_events({ sample_event(op) }, {}))
    assert(r.kind == "Reject", op .. " must not compile as protocol success")
  end
  ```
- Direct validator negative:
  - Construct a minimal `MoonCFG.Kernel` with a param named `out_tag`; assert validation fails with `forbidden_param`.
  - Construct a contract containing `LuaNF.CallProtocolExit`; assert validation fails with `forbidden_protocol_exit`.

**Danger zones**
- Do not assert rejection as semantic coverage. Negative tests only assert forbidden protocol success is blocked.
- Do not keep old protocol buffer/FFI helpers.

---

---

### Order of Operations

1. **ASDL first**: add `MoonCFG`, change `LuaCompile.MoonKernel`.
2. **Builders/validate next**: expose `MoonCFG`, add base `moon_cfg_kernel`.
3. **Create MoonCFG ABI/validator/emitter/key/lowerer**.
4. **Replace old MoonOut modules with wrappers** so old require paths do not resurrect tag ABI.
5. **Update compile path** to use `lua_nf_to_moon_cfg_lower`.
6. **Quarantine protocol observations** in semantic lowerer and NF normalizer.
7. **Rewrite MoonOut test into MoonCFG test**.
8. **Update pipeline/foundry/corpus tests and Makefile**.
9. **Run tests for the small implemented slice**.
10. **Only after this is green**, do decode-preservation edits.
11. **Only after decode fields are preserved**, begin adding real generic MoonCFG regions.

---

### Testing Strategy

Run incrementally:

1. After ASDL/builders:
   ```sh
   luajit experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/tests/test_spongejit_lua_compile_schema.lua
   ```

2. After MoonCFG validator/emitter/lowerer:
   ```sh
   luajit experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/tests/test_spongejit_lua_compile_moon_out.lua
   ```

3. After compile path update:
   ```sh
   luajit experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/tests/test_spongejit_lua_compile_pipeline.lua
   ```

4. After foundry update:
   ```sh
   luajit experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/tests/test_spongejit_lua_compile_foundry.lua
   ```

5. Main suite:
   ```sh
   cd experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit && make test-lua-compile
   ```

6. Structural grep checks:
   ```sh
   rg -n "out_tag|out_event_kind|TAG\\.call|TAG\\.setlist|TAG\\.getvarg" experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile
   rg -n "CallProtocolExit|CloseProtocolExit|GenericForProtocolExit|SetListProtocolExit|GetVargProtocolExit" experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile
   ```
   Expected:
   - protocol constructors may remain in ASDL/tests as negative fixtures;
   - accepted lowering/emission must not use them.

---

### Pattern Memo

- Accepted compile product is `MoonCFG.Kernel`, not `MoonOut.Kernel`.
- `MoonCFG.Kernel` must not contain `LuaNF.Program`.
- No accepted kernel may contain protocol exits.
- No emitted source may contain `out_tag` or semantic `out_*` continuation ABI.
- Emitter is mechanical: render MoonCFG only; do not inspect LuaSrc/LuaNF semantics.
- Unsupported generic Lua behavior may reject for now, but tests must not count that as success.
- Do not add opcode-by-opcode generic patches until CFG region semantics exist.

## Completed

- Extended `MoonCFG` validation/emission beyond the one-block scalar slice.
- Emitter now mechanically renders:
  - multi-block `return region -> T ... end`
  - `entry` / `block` syntax

  - bool branch returning different `i64` values
  - jump through block param and return it
  - numeric branch over `i64`

## Completed
Implemented the first bounded closed bytecode-window control lowering slice.

What it does:
- Adds `lua_src_to_moon_cfg_closed.lua`.
- Recognizes source windows with internal-only `JMP` / comparison+`JMP` control and terminal returns.
- Builds PC-based `MoonCFG` blocks.
- Lowers:
  - straight-line fallthrough to internal `MoonCFG.Jump`
  - in-window `JMP` to internal `MoonCFG.Jump`
  - `EQI`/numeric comparison + following `JMP` to internal `MoonCFG.Branch`
  - `RETURN0` / `RETURN1` / simple `RETURN` to `MoonCFG.Return`
- Carries simple live i64 values through jump block params.
- Rejects/declines out-of-window targets; no external exits or `out_tag`.

## Critique Output — 2026-06-02 13:59:51

## Design critique: complete generic Lua semantics ASDL → MoonCFG

The emerging direction is architecturally sound **only if MoonCFG becomes the semantic product**, not merely a prettier backend wrapper. The biggest danger is recreating the rejected interpreter/protocol model under new names: “regions,” “helpers,” “ExecCtx,” “runtime calls,” or “typed exits” can all become disguised handoff points if their semantics are not ASDL-visible and internally closed.

## Main risks

### 1. Hidden interpreter semantics inside “regions”

Typed Moonlift regions are a good fit, but they are also the highest-risk abstraction. A region that says “do table get” but internally calls an opaque runtime helper is not materially different from `out_tag = gettable`.

A legal region must be a compiled CFG fragment whose semantic branches are visible as ASDL:

- table vs non-table,
- raw hit vs miss,
- metatable present/absent,
- `__index` table chain vs function call,
- loop-limit/type-error path,
- yield/error/return continuation behavior.

If those choices are hidden in Lua strings, C helpers, host callbacks, or an `ExecCtx` method, the reset has failed.

### 2. Opcode dispatch can reappear as semantic dispatch

A complete generic Lua compiler must not become:

```text
MoonCFG.Cmd(kind = "OP_GETTABLE")
MoonCFG.EmitRegion(region = "execute_opcode")
MoonCFG.Switch(opcode)
```

That is an interpreter in ASDL clothing. The compiled CFG may be derived from opcodes, but its final representation must be semantic: table access, metamethod call, vararg adjustment, close chain, etc. The emitter must never recover opcode meaning.

### 3. `TValue` can become an escape hatch

Generic Lua semantics require a dynamic value model, but `TValue` must not become a black box where all semantics live behind helper calls.

Non-negotiable: value representation must expose enough ASDL-visible operations and choices for:

- type/tag tests,
- payload projection,
- nil/false truthiness,
- number/string/table/function/userdata distinctions,
- boxing/unboxing,
- equality/order semantics,
- GC/barrier-relevant table mutation if in scope.

If MoonCFG only has `ExecCtx` plus opaque `TValue*` operations, semantic explicitness is lost.

### 4. Calls, metamethods, yield, error, and close are inseparable

Generic Lua semantics are not just data transformations. They are control semantics.

The dangerous simplification is to model metamethod/call as “invoke something and resume later.” That is exactly the old continuation protocol unless the call path has typed continuations represented in MoonCFG:

- normal return,
- multivalue return,
- error,
- yield,
- tailcall,
- close/error interaction,
- result adjustment,
- open `top` propagation.

If these are externalized to a host dispatcher, the design violates no-interpreter.

### 5. Varargs and multivalue semantics need first-class representation

Lua’s `top`, open counts, vararg windows, return adjustment, `CALL B/C == 0`, `RETURN B == 0`, `SETLIST B == 0`, and `VARARG C == 0` cannot be papered over with scalar return values.

A complete design needs ASDL-visible concepts for:

- dynamic result sequences,
- stack windows,
- frame top,
- fixed vs open counts,
- adjustment/truncation/fill-with-nil,
- vararg source storage,
- vararg table behavior where applicable.

Without these, “generic CALL/RETURN/VARARG” will either reject or smuggle interpreter behavior.

### 6. Close/error/yield semantics are especially prone to fake success

`CLOSE`, `TBC`, tailcall close, return close, and error unwind need explicit sequencing. They cannot be represented as a single “close protocol” region unless the region’s internal CFG describes:

- close-chain traversal,
- `__close` lookup,
- call ordering,
- error replacement/propagation,
- yield legality,
- continuation after close.

This area should be treated as a high-risk semantic boundary.

## Can the runtime constructs be represented without interpreter handoff?

Yes, but only under strict conditions.

| Construct | Representable in MoonCFG? | Critical requirement |
|---|---:|---|
| `TValue` | Yes | Tags, payloads, projections, boxing, truthiness must be ASDL-visible. |
| Tables | Yes | Raw get/set, array/hash distinction, miss handling, metatable lookup, barriers must be explicit or consciously scoped. |
| Metamethods | Yes | Lookup, call, retry/table-chain behavior, errors/yields must be typed CFG control. |
| Varargs | Yes | Frame vararg storage and open/fixed count behavior must be modeled directly. |
| Multivalue returns | Yes | Dynamic value sequences and adjustment must be first-class. |
| Calls | Hard but possible | Arbitrary Lua call must not become host dispatch; it needs typed callable semantics or a clearly illegal unsupported boundary. |
| Close/TBC | Hard | Must model unwind and `__close` sequencing, not emit close handoff. |
| Error/yield | Hard | Must be typed kernel/control exits, not integer tags or host resume protocols. |

## Non-negotiable guardrails before implementation

1. **MoonCFG is the executable semantic product.**  
   Moonlift source emission must be mechanical rendering only.

2. **No opaque Lua semantic helpers.**  
   Helpers/regions are legal only when represented as ASDL CFG fragments with typed continuations.

3. **No opcode-shaped final IR.**  
   Final commands must describe semantics, not PUC opcode execution.

4. **Every semantic branch is an ASDL enum/sum choice.**  
   No string tags, integer event codes, or side-table meaning.

5. **Typed continuations only.**  
   Return, error, yield, guard fail, normal continuation, metamethod result, call result, and close continuation must be typed control edges.

6. **No host/interpreter completion boundary.**  
   Accepted kernels must not require an external Lua interpreter, resume dispatcher, opcode helper, or protocol loop.

7. **`ExecCtx` must not become semantic magic.**  
   It may carry state, but operations over it must be explicit MoonCFG operations/regions.

8. **Dynamic stack/top/multivalue state must be first-class.**  
   Open-count Lua behavior cannot be lowered honestly without this.

9. **Contracts cannot substitute for semantics.**  
   `LuaContract` may state obligations/facts, but it must not hide execution behavior.

10. **Unsupported valid Lua behavior may reject, but never pass as success.**  
   Rejection is an implementation limitation, not coverage.

11. **Runtime reuse must be audited as semantic import.**  
   Existing runtime modules contain useful knowledge but also interpreter/resume machinery and known mismatches. Reuse is only safe if converted into explicit MoonCFG semantics.

12. **PUC is the oracle.**  
   Current runtime discrepancies, especially around `ERRNNIL`, TFOR, concat, metamethods, and close behavior, must not leak into the compiler as accidental semantics.

## Bottom line

The ASDL → MoonCFG direction is the right philosophical trajectory, but its success depends on refusing all “almost explicit” shortcuts. The danger is not lack of expressiveness; MoonCFG can express the needed control. The danger is allowing dynamic Lua semantics to hide behind region names, runtime helpers, `ExecCtx`, or typed-looking continuation protocols that still require an external interpreter to finish the job.

## Key Code

### PUC opcode fields and pairing facts

`lopcodes.h` defines important fields:

```c
OP_CALL,      /* A B C R[A], ... := R[A](...) */
OP_TAILCALL,  /* A B C k return R[A](...) */
OP_RETURN,    /* A B C k return R[A], ... */
OP_SETLIST,   /* A vB vC k R[A][vC+i] := R[A+i] */
OP_VARARG,    /* A B C k R[A], ..., R[A+C-2] = varargs */
OP_GETVARG,   /* A B C R[A] := R[B][R[C]], R[B] is vararg parameter */
OP_ERRNNIL,   /* A Bx raise error if R[A] ~= nil */
```

Opcode notes require preservation of:

- `CALL`: `B == 0` consumes previous `top`; `C == 0` sets `top`.
- `VARARG`: `C == 0` copies all varargs and sets `top`; `k` means vararg table in `R[B]`.
- `RETURN`: `B == 0` returns up to `top`.
- `SETLIST`: `B == 0` uses `top`; `k` means following `EXTRAARG` extends `C`.
- `RETURN/TAILCALL`: `k` closes upvalues; `C > 0` corrects hidden-vararg `func`.
- `MMBINI/MMBINK`: `k` means operands were flipped.
- Comparisons/tests assume following instruction is `JMP`.

### TValue and tag facts

`lobject.h` establishes PUC value identity:

```c
typedef union Value { GCObject *gc; void *p; lua_CFunction f;
  lua_Integer i; lua_Number n; lu_byte ub; } Value;

typedef struct TValue { Value value_; lu_byte tt_; } TValue;
```

Tags use:

- bits 0-3: base `LUA_T*`
- bits 4-5: variant
- bit 6: collectable

Important variants:

- nil: `LUA_VNIL`, `LUA_VEMPTY`, `LUA_VABSTKEY`, `LUA_VNOTABLE`
- booleans: `LUA_VFALSE`, `LUA_VTRUE`; falsey is only false or nil
- numbers: `LUA_VNUMINT`, `LUA_VNUMFLT`
- strings: short/long
- functions: Lua closure, light C function, C closure
- tables: `LUA_VTABLE`

Current runtime `products.lua` uses a different Moonlift ABI:

```lua
struct Value tag: u32; aux: u32; bits: u64 end
struct ResumeState kind: u16; a: u16; b: u16; c: u16; pc: index; ...
```

So PUC layout is an oracle, not directly imported storage.

### Metamethod facts

`ltm.h` metamethod order is fixed:

```c
TM_INDEX, TM_NEWINDEX, TM_GC, TM_MODE, TM_LEN, TM_EQ,
TM_ADD, TM_SUB, TM_MUL, TM_MOD, TM_POW, TM_DIV, TM_IDIV,
TM_BAND, TM_BOR, TM_BXOR, TM_SHL, TM_SHR, TM_UNM, TM_BNOT,
TM_LT, TM_LE, TM_CONCAT, TM_CALL, TM_CLOSE
```

`luaT_gettmbyobj` checks:

- table metatable
- userdata metatable
- global type metatable for other types

`luaT_callTMres` pushes metamethod + args, calls yieldably only from Lua code, moves one result to destination, returns result tag.

Binary metamethod lookup tries first operand, then second operand. Missing bitwise metamethod on numeric operands can produce integer-conversion errors; otherwise type operation errors.

### Table get/set facts

PUC `GETTABLE` fast path:

```c
if (ttisinteger(rc))
  luaV_fastgeti(rb, ivalue(rc), s2v(ra), tag);
else
  luaV_fastget(rb, rc, s2v(ra), luaH_get, tag);
if (tagisempty(tag))
  Protect(luaV_finishget(L, rb, rc, ra, tag));
```

`luaV_finishget` facts:

- non-table checks `__index` via `luaT_gettmbyobj`
- table miss checks table metatable `__index`
- no `__index` on table miss returns nil
- function `__index` is called with `(t,key)`
- table `__index` repeats lookup
- chain capped by `MAXTAGLOOP`

`luaV_finishset` facts:

- table existing slot can be raw-updated
- absent table key with no `__newindex` inserts raw key/value
- non-table checks `__newindex`
- function `__newindex` called with `(t,key,val)`
- table `__newindex` repeats assignment
- chain capped by `MAXTAGLOOP`

`ltable.c` facts:

- integer and integral-float keys canonicalize to integer lookup.
- setting nil key errors: `"table index is nil"`.
- setting NaN float key errors: `"table index is NaN"`.
- `luaH_getn` finds a border using array hint, binary search, and hash search.

Current runtime divergence:

- `regions_table.lua` `table_get/table_set` immediately type-error on non-table; PUC allows non-table `__index`/`__newindex` through global type metatables.
- `regions_metamethod.lua` `get_metamethod` currently handles tables only.

### Arithmetic/MMBIN facts

PUC codegen always emits arithmetic plus following MMBIN companion:

```c
int pc = luaK_codeABCk(fs, op, 0, v1, v2, 0);
luaK_codeABCk(fs, mmop, v1, v2, event, flip);
```

PUC VM fast arithmetic increments `pc` on primitive success. If primitive path fails, execution falls through to companion MMBIN.

`OP_MMBIN` reads previous arithmetic instruction and writes metamethod result into that original result register.

Raw arithmetic facts:

- ADD/SUB/MUL/MOD/IDIV use integer result when both operands are integers; otherwise numeric float when convertible without string conversion in fast path.
- DIV/POW operate as float operations.
- bitwise ops require integer conversion without string coercion.
- `luaV_idiv` and `luaV_mod` have special zero and `-1` cases.
- string-to-number coercion exists via `luaV_tonumber`/`luaV_tointeger`, but fast macros often use no-string-conversion variants.

Current runtime divergence:

- arithmetic fast paths skip companion with `pc + 2`;
- MMBIN regions currently jump runtime error, not metamethod implementation.

### Comparison/test facts

PUC comparison/test control:

```c
#define docondjump() if (cond != GETARG_k(i)) pc++; else donextjump(ci);
```

Facts:

- comparison/test op condition true edge executes following `JMP`; false edge skips it.
- `k` is accepted condition polarity.
- `EQ` can call `__eq` for tables/userdata with different identities.
- `EQK` uses raw equality; no `__eq`.
- `EQI` non-number is false.
- `LT`/`LE` compare numbers, strings, or call order metamethods.
- immediate order comparison has `C` flag indicating whether original operand was float for metamethod correction.

Current `LuaSrc` does not preserve immediate comparison `C`/isfloat.

### LEN/CONCAT facts

`luaV_objlen`:

- table: if `__len`, call it; else `luaH_getn`
- short/long string: byte length
- otherwise: `__len` or type error

`luaV_concat`:

- works over stack range ending at `L->top`
- number operands can be converted to strings via `luaO_tostring`
- non-string/non-convertible pair calls `__concat`
- empty strings optimize away
- concat metamethod may yield; `luaV_finishOp` resumes and continues concat

Current runtime divergence:

- `op/misc.lua` LEN supports strings/table raw length/table `__len`, but non-table metatable support depends on table-only `get_metamethod`.
- `regions_string.lua` `string_concat_range` accepts only already-string values; non-string conversion and `__concat` are not implemented.

### CALL/RETURN/VARARG facts

PUC `OP_CALL`:

```c
if (b != 0) L->top.p = ra + b;
if ((newci = luaD_precall(L, ra, nresults)) == NULL) ...
else goto startfunc;
```

`luaD_precall`:

- C closure/light C function: call C, move results
- Lua closure: push CallInfo, fill missing fixed params with nil
- non-function: find `__call`, shift original function/args right, retry
- `__call` chain is capped by status bits

`OP_TAILCALL`:

- `B == 0` uses previous top
- computes `delta` for hidden varargs using `C`
- `k` closes upvalues before tailcall
- Lua tailcall reuses caller frame; C tailcall returns to caller via `luaD_poscall`

`OP_RETURN`:

- `B == 0` returns up to `top`
- `k` closes upvalues/TBC before return; close may yield
- `C > 0` adjusts `func` for hidden varargs before returning
- results are moved/filled/truncated by `luaD_poscall`/`moveresults`

Vararg facts:

- `VARARGPREP` calls `luaT_adjustvarargs`.
- hidden varargs store `nextraargs` and move fixed params after hidden args.
- vararg-table mode creates table with numeric elements and `"n"` field.
- `VARARG` with `wanted < 0` copies all and sets top.
- `GETVARG`:
  - integer key in range copies hidden arg
  - key string `"n"` returns extra count
  - else nil

Current `LuaSrc` preserves `RETURN C/k`, but currently drops:

- `TAILCALL k`
- `TAILCALL C` meaning hidden-vararg fixed-param count; field currently named `nresults`
- `VARARG B/k` vararg-table source
- immediate comparison `C` isfloat
- MMBINI/MMBINK flip `k`
- NEWTABLE `k`/EXTRAARG extension

### Numeric for facts

PUC `forprep`:

Before:

- `ra`: initial
- `ra+1`: limit
- `ra+2`: step

After integer prep:

- `ra`: loop count
- `ra+1`: step
- `ra+2`: control variable/init

After float prep:

- `ra`: limit
- `ra+1`: step
- `ra+2`: control variable/init

Errors/coercions:

- step zero errors
- limit/init/step are converted with precise integer/float rules
- integer limit conversion clips or skips according to step direction

`FORLOOP`:

- integer loop decrements count, updates control variable, jumps back if count > 0
- float loop updates control variable and compares with step direction
- current external loop variable in PUC layout is `ra+2` after prep; current LuaCompile uses `base+3` in places, so numeric-for state layout needs oracle reconciliation.

Current runtime divergence:

- `op/loop.lua` implements a simpler numeric for layout (`idx=a`, `limit=a+1`, `step=a+2`, external `a+3`) and does not match PUC’s integer count prep layout.

### Generic for facts

Parser creates generic-for internals:

- `base`: iterator function
- `base+1`: state
- `base+2`: closing variable after TFORPREP swap
- `base+3`: control variable / first result slot
- declared loop variables start at `base+3`

PUC `TFORPREP`:

- swaps control and closing variables
- marks closing variable TBC if not false/nil
- jumps to TFORCALL

PUC `TFORCALL`:

- copies iterator/state/control into call slots starting at `ra+3`
- calls iterator with two args and `C` wanted results
- first result overwrites `ra+3`

PUC `TFORLOOP`:

- checks `ra+3` for non-nil
- if non-nil, jumps back

There is a discrepancy between `lopcodes.h` comment saying `R[A+2]` and `lvm.c` code checking `R[A+3]`; `lvm.c` is the executing oracle.

Current runtime divergence:

- `op/loop.lua` `TFORCALL` is runtime error.
- `op/loop.lua` `TFORLOOP` checks `a+2`, not PUC `a+3`.

### SETLIST facts

PUC `OP_SETLIST`:

```c
n = GETARG_vB(i);
last = GETARG_vC(i);
if (n == 0) n = L->top.p - ra - 1;
last += n;
if (k) { last += GETARG_Ax(*pc) * (MAXARG_vC + 1); pc++; }
for (; n > 0; n--) obj2arr(h, last - 1, val);
```

Facts:

- table is assumed table (`hvalue(ra)`) after validation/codegen.
- no `__newindex`; constructor array fill writes raw array part.
- `B == 0` uses top.
- `k` consumes following EXTRAARG.
- writes values from `R[A+n]` down to `R[A+1]`.
- array index is 1-based in Lua, `obj2arr` uses C index `last-1`.
- may resize array only for variable-count case.

Current `LuaSrc.SETLIST` now preserves `uses_extraarg` and `extraarg`.

### CLOSE/TBC facts

`luaF_newtbcupval`:

- nil/false values do not need close (`l_isfalse`)
- otherwise value must have `__close`, or error
- TBC list uses deltas and dummy nodes

`luaF_close`:

- first closes open upvalues
- then traverses TBC variables down to level
- calls `__close(self[, err])`
- `yy` controls whether close call may yield

Return/call result movement can also close TBC variables.

Current runtime divergence:

- `regions_error.lua` finds `__close` but errors instead of invoking it.
- `op_tbc` only stores `L.tbc_head = slot`, not PUC delta list semantics.
- `op_close` closes upvalues only.

### Errors/yield facts

PUC `Protect` saves `pc` and `top` before operations that may error/yield/reallocate. `luaV_finishOp` handles yielded operations including MMBIN, table access, comparisons, CONCAT, CLOSE, RETURN, TFORCALL, CALL, TAILCALL, SET*.

`lua_yieldk` facts:

- cannot yield across non-yieldable C boundary
- yields store result count in `ci->u2.nyield`
- C continuation saved in `ci->u.c.k/ctx`
- Lua hook yields cannot yield values or continue

ASDL for full semantics needs explicit error/yield continuation facts if kernels can cross yieldable Lua calls/metamethods.

### Moonlift control facts

Moonlift control model:

- regions are typed control fragments with continuation protocols
- blocks are typed state points with named params
- `emit` splices a region CFG; it is not a runtime function call
- every declared continuation exit must be filled; extra/missing fills reject
- `jump` args are named, match target block param names and types
- `jump` terminates current path
- `yield` exits nearest control region; `return` exits enclosing function
- no implicit fallthrough between blocks
- every block path must explicitly terminate

These facts constrain MoonCFG emission: block params/continuations must be typed and all edges explicit.

## Relationships

Current factual data flow:

```text
PUC event table
  -> lua_src_from_puc_decode.decode
  -> LuaSrc.Window
  -> compile_to_moon_kernel
       if closed control candidate:
          lua_src_to_moon_cfg_closed.lower
          -> MoonCFG.Kernel
       else:
          lua_src_to_lua_sem_lower.lower
          -> LuaSem.Accepted/Rejected
          -> lua_sem_to_lua_nf_normalize.normalize
          -> LuaNF.Program
          -> lua_nf_to_lua_contract_derive
          -> lua_nf_to_moon_cfg_lower
          -> MoonCFG.Kernel
  -> moon_cfg_validate
  -> moon_cfg_emit
```

Current protocol reset facts:

- `LuaNF` still contains old protocol exit constructors.
- `lua_src_to_lua_sem_lower.lua` now rejects CALL/TAILCALL/CLOSE/TBC/TFOR*/SETLIST/GETVARG instead of producing protocol observations.
- `lua_sem_to_lua_nf_normalize.lua` errors if old protocol observations reach normalization.
- `moon_cfg_validate.lua` rejects `LuaNF.Program`, protocol exits, `out_*` params, and string protocol tags inside accepted kernels.
- `moon_cfg_emit.lua` renders only MoonCFG and does not inspect LuaSrc/LuaNF.

## Fields ASDL Must Preserve for Full Generic Semantics

From the oracle/code facts above, these source/semantic fields are mandatory facts to preserve:

- All opcodes: `pc`, raw operand modes, register windows, following-op pairing where semantically required.
- CALL: `A`, `B`, `C`, open `B==0`, open-result `C==0`, previous/next `top`.
- TAILCALL: `A`, `B`, `C`, `k`; `C` is hidden-vararg fixed-param count, not ordinary result count.
- RETURN: `A`, `B`, `C`, `k`, open `B==0`, close behavior, hidden-vararg correction.
- VARARG: `A`, `B`, `C`, `k`; open `C==0`; vararg-table mode via `k`/`B`.
- GETVARG: destination, vararg base/table slot, dynamic key slot.
- SETLIST: `A`, `vB`, `vC`, `k`, following `EXTRAARG Ax`, open `vB==0` and `top`.
- NEWTABLE: `A`, `vB`, `vC`, `k`, following `EXTRAARG Ax` for array size.
- LOADKX: following `EXTRAARG Ax`.
- ERRNNIL: `A`, `Bx/name_index`.
- MMBIN/MMBINI/MMBINK: previous arithmetic op, event/TMS, operands, immediate/constant operand, flip `k`.
- Immediate comparisons: `C` float-origin flag for metamethod correction.
- Comparisons/tests: `k` polarity and mandatory following `JMP`.
- Numeric for: base, offset, integer-vs-float prepared state, count/limit/step/control layout, skip/body/continue targets.
- Generic for: base, `TFORPREP` offset, `TFORCALL C`, `TFORLOOP Bx`, swapped closing/control layout, TBC state.
- CLOSE/TBC: close level, TBC list ordering, false/nil non-closeable shortcut, close metamethod/error/yield state.
- Errors/yield: error object/status, saved pc/top, resumable opcode kind, result locations, continuation signatures.

Current `LuaSrc` already preserves `RETURN C/k`, `SETLIST k/EXTRAARG`, and `ERRNNIL Bx`, but still drops or misnames some fields listed above.

## Observations

- `.vendor/Lua/lvm.c` is the strongest semantic oracle. Existing runtime modules are useful but have documented divergences and incomplete paths.
- Current MoonCFG supports honest scalar/closed-control slices only. It has no full generic TValue/table/call/top/TBC/yield semantic vocabulary yet.
- Current completion gate correctly lists valid Lua behavior still rejecting: generic ADD, GETTABLE, SETTABLE, LEN, CONCAT, open VARARG, multivalue RETURN, ERRNNIL.
- Current runtime `op_errnnil` errors on nil, while PUC errors on non-nil; PUC opcode comment and `lvm.c`/`ldebug.c` agree that ERRNNIL raises when `R[A] ~= nil`.
- Current runtime generic-for and numeric-for layouts diverge from PUC in important places.
- Any ASDL for full generic semantics must model Lua `top`, frame/result adjustment, metamethod calls, error/yield continuations, and PUC companion-op invariants explicitly; these are semantic facts, not optional backend details.

## Knowledge-builder Output — 2026-06-02 14:10:21

### What Matters Most for This Problem

- **Semantic state completeness**: Lua semantics require explicit ASDL for dynamic values, stack/top, call frames, multivalue sequences, varargs, errors, yields, and close chains.
- **No hidden execution**: MoonCFG regions/helpers must be ASDL-visible CFG, not opaque runtime calls, opcode dispatch, or `ExecCtx` magic.
- **Oracle fidelity**: `.vendor/Lua/lvm.c`/PUC behavior must dominate current runtime modules where they diverge.
- **Window correctness**: opcode companion and following-instruction invariants must be preserved before semantics can be correct.
- **Contracts vs semantics separation**: facts may justify specialization, but may not substitute for execution behavior.

### Non-Obvious Observations

- The current `MoonCFG` vocabulary is honest for scalar/closed-control slices, but far too shallow for full Lua semantics. `StackSlot`, `FrameTop`, `ExecCtx`, `LoadTag`, `Payload`, and `RawGet` are useful atoms, but without ASDL-visible Lua value/state operations they become exactly the kind of semantic escape hatches the reset rejected.

- `TValue` cannot be modeled as just “tag + payload.” PUC distinguishes ordinary nil, empty table slots, absent keys, booleans, integer/float numbers, short/long strings, closures, C functions, userdata, tables, threads, and collectable variants. Some of those distinctions are not user-visible as values but are semantically crucial for table lookup, equality, truthiness, and metamethod dispatch.

- Truthiness is deceptively small: only nil and false are falsey. But correctness requires separating **nil as a value** from **empty/absent table lookup sentinel**. If ASDL collapses those, table miss, `GETTABLE`, `__index`, `SETTABLE`, and `EQ` semantics become wrong.

- Payload projection must not silently imply validity. A `Payload` projection is only meaningful after an ASDL-visible tag/type proof or a typed control branch. Otherwise `Project(Payload)` becomes hidden unchecked unboxing.

- Backend `TypeRef("i64")` / `TypeRef("ptr(...)")` is not a Lua semantic type system. Full semantics need a separate Lua-level value/tag model; Moonlift types are only representation choices.

- `UnknownTValue(reason)` is safe only as a rejection/debug artifact. If accepted MoonCFG can carry unknown dynamic values whose operations are later “handled” by helper regions, that reintroduces interpreter dispatch under a different name.

- `FrameTop` is not just a mutable field. Lua `top` is a temporal protocol between opcodes: `CALL C==0`, `RETURN B==0`, `VARARG C==0`, and `SETLIST B==0` consume or produce it. A correct ASDL boundary must distinguish fixed count, open count, known dynamic count, and saved top across yield/error.

- Stack slots alone are insufficient. Lua operations act on **stack windows**: call windows, return windows, vararg windows, constructor windows, iterator windows. Full correctness needs those windows as first-class semantic objects, not inferred from raw slot integers during emission.

- Multivalue is not `TValue*`. Lua result sequences have dynamic length, origin, adjustment rules, nil-fill/truncation, open-tail propagation, and special interaction with assignment, return, call, vararg, and table constructors. Treating them as ordinary arrays loses the semantics of “open” values.

- Varargs have two distinct semantic identities: hidden frame varargs and vararg table behavior. `GETVARG` is not just indexed stack access; string key `"n"` and out-of-range/nil behavior matter.

- Generic table get/set requires representing the **empty-result sentinel** from raw lookup separately from returned nil. Table miss without `__index` returns nil; table miss with `__index` continues through table/function metamethod logic. Those are different semantic paths.

- Current runtime table/metamethod helpers are not a safe oracle because they only handle table metatables in places where PUC also checks userdata/global type metatables. Reusing them opaquely would bake in known divergence.

- Metamethod lookup is operation-specific, ordered, and sometimes asymmetric. Binary arithmetic tries first operand then second; order comparisons have different fallback rules; `EQK` is raw while `EQ` may call `__eq`; concat may repeatedly resume after metamethod calls. A single “call metamethod” region name would hide too much unless its internal CFG exposes these distinctions.

- Arithmetic and `MMBIN*` form one semantic unit for generic behavior. The arithmetic opcode writes the primitive result only when the fast path succeeds; otherwise control falls through to the companion. Modeling `MMBIN` as an independent no-op is correct only for proven primitive-success windows.

- Comparison/test opcodes are also paired with following `JMP`. The branch direction is encoded by `k/polarity`, and the true edge executes the following jump. A window that splits the comparison from its companion jump does not contain enough semantics for honest lowering.

- `SETLIST`, `LOADKX`, `NEWTABLE`, and some constructor/codegen forms depend on following `EXTRAARG`. Preserving `SETLIST` is only one part of the pairing problem; full correctness needs a general source-window invariant for companion instructions.

- Calls are not merely control transfers. Lua call semantics include `__call` retry, C vs Lua closure behavior, argument shifting, result adjustment, frame creation/reuse, yieldability, and possible tailcall frame replacement. A typed `Call` continuation without these details is indistinguishable from the old protocol handoff.

- Tailcall correctness depends on frame identity, not just “return callee results.” `TAILCALL` can use open argument count, hidden-vararg correction via `C`, and close-upvalue behavior via `k`. Those facts must survive past `LuaSrc`.

- Yield and error cannot be generic integer exits. PUC saves `pc` and `top` around yieldable/erroring operations and resumes through opcode-specific continuations. If MoonCFG supports yield inside metamethod/call/close/concat/table access, the continuation state must be ASDL-visible.

- `ExitProtocol.UnsupportedExit` is dangerous. In accepted kernels, it can become rejection-as-success in CFG form unless its meaning is restricted to non-semantic impossible/unreachable paths, not valid-but-unimplemented Lua behavior.

- `Return` in MoonCFG currently means native Moonlift function return. Lua `RETURN` means Lua-frame return with multivalue adjustment, close/TBC sequencing, hidden-vararg correction, and caller result movement. Those are not the same boundary.

- Close/TBC semantics are a high-risk hidden-helper zone. Correctness requires ordering: close open upvalues, traverse TBC variables, detect false/nil non-closeable values, require `__close`, call it with error context when unwinding, and handle error replacement/yield legality. A single `CloseRegion` without visible internal CFG would recreate `CloseProtocolExit`.

- Numeric `for` cannot use the current runtime’s simplified slot layout as design truth. PUC rewrites loop state differently for integer and float loops; integer mode stores count/step/control, while float mode stores limit/step/control. The ASDL must distinguish prepared loop-state variants.

- Generic `for` is inseparable from call and close semantics. `TFORPREP` mutates closing/control layout and may create TBC state; `TFORCALL` is a real call; `TFORLOOP` tests `R[A+3]` in `lvm.c`. Treating `TFOR*` as a loop opcode family hides cross-cutting call/TBC behavior.

- `LuaContract` can justify specialization but cannot execute Lua. A fact like `MetatableAbsent` can permit skipping metamethod paths only if guarded and invalidatable; it cannot replace the generic metatable lookup semantics for unconstrained values.

- Existing `LuaContract.ProjectionObligation` still references `LuaNF.Exit`, including old protocol exits. That ties contracts to the old “exit as semantic boundary” model. Full MoonCFG semantics need contracts to describe obligations on CFG-visible values/regions, not obligations to resume host protocols.

- `RegionRef` by name is not enough to avoid helpers. A region is honest only if the referenced body is part of the ASDL module and all continuations are resolved by typed CFG edges. An unresolved named region is semantically equivalent to an opaque helper call.

- `ExecCtx` is the most likely place for hidden interpreter semantics to reappear. It may carry state, but any operation that mutates or queries it must be an ASDL-visible operation with explicit effects, choices, and continuations.

- Complete generic semantics and window compilation are in tension. If kernels cover only bytecode windows, any boundary exit must carry a complete, typed Lua machine state snapshot. Otherwise exiting a window becomes an implicit interpreter handoff.

### Knowledge Gaps

- Exact legal boundary for Lua/C calls, allocator/GC barriers, errors, and yields: which external effects are semantic runtime effects versus forbidden interpreter helpers?
- Final Lua value ABI: logical PUC-compatible tag model vs current `products.lua` representation.
- Remaining dropped source fields: `TAILCALL k/C`, `VARARG B/k`, `MMBINI/MMBINK flip k`, immediate-comparison `C`, `NEWTABLE/LOADKX EXTRAARG`.
- How full MoonCFG contracts should attach to regions/ops without referencing old `LuaNF.Exit`.
- Whether accepted kernels are intended to be whole-function closed CFGs or window CFGs with typed deopt/state exits.

## Documenter Output — 2026-06-02 14:13:43

# SpongeJIT Full Generic Lua Semantics ASDL -> MoonCFG Design

**Workflow ID:** `wf-b7b79a56`

## 1. Design Goal and Non-Negotiables

The goal is to make SpongeJIT compile full generic Lua bytecode semantics into an explicit ASDL-described semantic CFG that feeds `MoonCFG`, so successful compilation means the Lua computation is represented as typed, closed, mechanically-emittable Moonlift control/data structure with no Lua interpreter dependency, no host protocol handoff, and no rejection counted as success.

Non-negotiables:

1. **PUC Lua semantics are the oracle.**
2. **Every semantic choice is represented as ASDL data.**
3. **MoonCFG emission is mechanical rendering only.**
4. **No opaque helpers, protocol exits, integer `out_tag`s, or host resume dispatch.**
5. **No opcode-shaped final IR.**
6. **Contracts and evidence may justify specialization, but cannot execute semantics.**
7. **Unsupported valid Lua behavior may reject during implementation, but rejection is never coverage.**
8. **Typed continuations are required for calls, returns, errors, yields, close chains, and guard/deopt exits.**
9. **Dynamic Lua state — stack, top, multivalue results, varargs, frame state, close state — must be first-class ASDL.**

---

## 2. Oracle / Fidelity Rule

The semantic oracle is `.vendor/Lua`, especially:

- `.vendor/Lua/lvm.c`
- `.vendor/Lua/lopcodes.h`
- `.vendor/Lua/lopcodes.c`
- `.vendor/Lua/lobject.h`
- `.vendor/Lua/ltm.h`
- `.vendor/Lua/ltm.c`
- `.vendor/Lua/ldo.c`
- `.vendor/Lua/lfunc.c`
- `.vendor/Lua/ltable.c`
- `.vendor/Lua/lcode.c`
- `.vendor/Lua/lparser.c`

Current runtime modules under `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/src/` are useful references, but they do **not** dominate PUC. Known divergences include:

- `ERRNNIL`: PUC raises when `R[A] ~= nil`; current runtime/compiler behavior previously treated nil as failing.
- Generic-for layout: PUC `TFORLOOP` checks `R[A+3]`; current runtime checks a different slot.
- Numeric-for layout: PUC rewrites integer loop state into count/step/control, not the runtime’s simplified slot layout.
- Metamethod lookup: PUC checks table, userdata, and global type metatables; current runtime often handles table metatables only.
- `CONCAT`: PUC supports numeric-to-string conversion and `__concat`; current runtime string region only accepts already-string values.
- `__close`: PUC calls `__close`; current runtime close chain is incomplete.

Where current runtime disagrees with PUC, PUC wins.

---

## 3. Full Layer Architecture

The full architecture is:

```text
PUC bytecode / trace events
  -> LuaSrc
       preserves exact opcode operands, companion instructions, top-sensitive fields
  -> LuaSem / LuaRT
       ASDL semantic domain for Lua values, stack, frames, tables, calls, errors, yields
  -> LuaExec
       ASDL semantic CFG over LuaRT values and typed continuations
  -> MoonCFG
       terminal compiled CFG model
  -> moon_cfg_emit.lua
       mechanical Moonlift source rendering
```

### Layer Responsibilities

| Layer | Responsibility |
|---|---|
| `LuaSrc` | Preserve what PUC encoded: opcode identity, operands, flags, companion `JMP`, `MMBIN`, `EXTRAARG`, open counts, `top` effects. |
| `LuaSem` | Interpret source operations into semantic operations under evidence, without losing generic paths. |
| `LuaRT` | Define Lua runtime semantic objects: `TValue`, sentinels, stack windows, multivalue sequences, varargs, tables, metatables, calls, errors, yields, close state. |
| `LuaExec` | Define typed semantic CFG fragments/regions over `LuaRT` objects. |
| `MoonCFG` | Terminal compiled CFG rendered into Moonlift. It must not carry executable `LuaNF.Program`. |
| `moon_cfg_emit.lua` | Print already-decided CFG. It must not infer Lua semantics. |

---

## 4. Complete ASDL Module Sketches

The following sketches specify the required semantic vocabulary. Exact field names may change, but the semantic distinctions must remain ASDL-visible.

### 4.1 `LuaRT`: Runtime Semantic Domain

```asdl
module LuaRT {
  Name = (string text) unique
  Pc = (number value) unique
  Slot = (number index) unique
  Count = (number value) unique
  Ax = (number value) unique

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Lua value tags and sentinel distinctions
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------

  ValueTag =
      NilTag
    | EmptySlotTag
    | AbsentKeyTag
    | NoTableTag
    | FalseTag
    | TrueTag
    | IntegerTag
    | FloatTag
    | ShortStringTag
    | LongStringTag
    | TableTag
    | LuaClosureTag
    | CClosureTag
    | LightCFunctionTag
    | UserdataTag
    | LightUserdataTag
    | ThreadTag

  NilKind =
      OrdinaryNil
    | EmptySlotSentinel
    | AbsentKeySentinel
    | NoTableSentinel

  BoolKind = LuaFalse | LuaTrue

  NumberKind = IntegerNumber | FloatNumber

  StringKind = ShortString | LongString

  GCColor = White | Gray | Black

  ValueRef =
      StackValue(LuaRT.FrameRef frame, LuaRT.Slot slot) unique
    | ConstValue(LuaRT.ConstRef const) unique
    | UpvalueValue(LuaRT.UpvalueRef upvalue) unique
    | VarargValue(LuaRT.VarargRef vararg, LuaRT.Count index) unique
    | TempValue(LuaRT.Name name) unique
    | TableValue(LuaRT.TableRef table) unique
    | ClosureValue(LuaRT.ClosureRef closure) unique
    | UserdataValue(LuaRT.UserdataRef userdata) unique
    | ThreadValue(LuaRT.ThreadRef thread) unique

  TValue =
      NilValue(LuaRT.NilKind kind) unique
    | BoolValue(LuaRT.BoolKind kind) unique
    | IntValue(number value) unique
    | FloatValue(number value) unique
    | StringValue(LuaRT.StringRef string, LuaRT.StringKind kind) unique
    | TableValueNode(LuaRT.TableRef table) unique
    | LuaClosureValue(LuaRT.ClosureRef closure) unique
    | CClosureValue(LuaRT.ClosureRef closure) unique
    | LightCFunctionValue(LuaRT.FunctionRef function) unique
    | UserdataValueNode(LuaRT.UserdataRef userdata) unique
    | LightUserdataValue(LuaRT.PointerRef pointer) unique
    | ThreadValueNode(LuaRT.ThreadRef thread) unique

  ValueProjection =
      ProjectTag
    | ProjectNilKind
    | ProjectBool
    | ProjectInteger
    | ProjectFloat
    | ProjectStringRef
    | ProjectTableRef
    | ProjectClosureRef
    | ProjectUserdataRef
    | ProjectThreadRef
    | ProjectPayloadBits

  TypeTest =
      IsNil
    | IsOrdinaryNil
    | IsFalse
    | IsFalsey
    | IsTruthy
    | IsBoolean
    | IsInteger
    | IsFloat
    | IsNumber
    | IsString
    | IsTable
    | IsLuaClosure
    | IsCClosure
    | IsFunction
    | IsUserdata
    | IsThread
    | IsCollectable
    | IsAbsentKey
    | IsEmptySlot

  Truthiness =
      FalseyNil
    | FalseyFalse
    | TruthyValue

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- References
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------

  FrameRef = (LuaRT.Name name) unique
  StackRef = (LuaRT.FrameRef frame) unique
  ConstRef = (number index) unique
  UpvalueRef = (number index) unique
  VarargRef = (LuaRT.FrameRef frame) unique
  TableRef = (LuaRT.Name name) unique
  StringRef = (LuaRT.Name name) unique
  ClosureRef = (LuaRT.Name name) unique
  FunctionRef = (LuaRT.Name name) unique
  UserdataRef = (LuaRT.Name name) unique
  ThreadRef = (LuaRT.Name name) unique
  PointerRef = (LuaRT.Name name) unique

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Stack, windows, frame top, multivalue
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------

  CountSpec =
      FixedCount(number count) unique
    | OpenFromTop(LuaRT.TopRef top) unique
    | DynamicCount(LuaRT.ValueRef count_value) unique
    | UnknownCount(string reason) unique

  TopRef = (LuaRT.FrameRef frame) unique

  StackWindowKind =
      CallWindow
    | ReturnWindow
    | VarargWindow
    | ConstructorWindow
    | IteratorWindow
    | AssignmentWindow

  StackWindow = (
    LuaRT.StackWindowKind kind,
    LuaRT.FrameRef frame,
    LuaRT.Slot base,
    LuaRT.CountSpec count
  ) unique

  ValueSeqKind =
      FixedSeq
    | OpenSeq
    | AdjustedSeq
    | VarargSeq
    | CallResultSeq

  ValueSeq = (
    LuaRT.ValueSeqKind kind,
    LuaRT.ValueRef* values,
    LuaRT.CountSpec count,
    LuaRT.SequenceOrigin origin
  ) unique

  SequenceOrigin =
      FromStackWindow(LuaRT.StackWindow window) unique
    | FromCallResult(LuaRT.CallRef call) unique
    | FromVarargs(LuaRT.VarargSource source) unique
    | FromLiteralValues unique
    | FromAdjusted(LuaRT.ValueSeq source) unique

  ResultAdjustment =
      ExactCount(LuaRT.Count count) unique
    | OpenResult unique
    | FillNilTo(LuaRT.Count count) unique
    | TruncateTo(LuaRT.Count count) unique
    | PropagateOpenTail unique

  Frame = (
    LuaRT.FrameRef id,
    LuaRT.StackRef stack,
    LuaRT.TopRef top,
    LuaRT.VarargSource varargs,
    LuaRT.CloseChain close_chain,
    LuaRT.Pc pc
  ) unique

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Varargs
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------

  VarargSource =
      NoVarargs unique
    | HiddenFrameVarargs(LuaRT.FrameRef frame, LuaRT.Count count) unique
    | VarargTableSource(LuaRT.TableRef table, LuaRT.Count count) unique

  VarargAccess =
      VarargIndex(LuaRT.VarargSource source, LuaRT.ValueRef key) unique
    | VarargFixedCopy(LuaRT.VarargSource source, LuaRT.Count count) unique
    | VarargOpenCopy(LuaRT.VarargSource source) unique
    | VarargNField(LuaRT.VarargSource source) unique

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Tables, raw lookup, miss sentinels, metatables
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------

  TableShape =
      ArrayOnly
    | HashOnly
    | MixedArrayHash
    | UnknownShape

  TableRefState = (
    LuaRT.TableRef table,
    LuaRT.TableShape shape,
    LuaRT.MetatableRef metatable
  ) unique

  MetatableRef =
      NoMetatable unique
    | TableMetatable(LuaRT.TableRef table) unique
    | UserdataMetatable(LuaRT.UserdataRef userdata) unique
    | TypeMetatable(LuaRT.ValueTag tag) unique
    | UnknownMetatable unique

  RawGetResult =
      RawHit(LuaRT.ValueRef value) unique
    | RawMiss(LuaRT.NilKind absent_sentinel) unique

  RawSetResult =
      RawUpdated unique
    | RawInserted unique
    | RawSetNilKeyError unique
    | RawSetNaNKeyError unique
    | RawSetBarrierRequired unique

  TableLookupState =
      LookupStart(LuaRT.ValueRef table, LuaRT.ValueRef key) unique
    | LookupRawTable(LuaRT.TableRef table, LuaRT.ValueRef key) unique
    | LookupMetatable(LuaRT.ValueRef receiver, LuaRT.Metamethod method) unique
    | LookupIndexTableChain(LuaRT.TableRef next_table, LuaRT.Count depth) unique
    | LookupIndexFunctionCall(LuaRT.ValueRef function, LuaRT.ValueRef receiver, LuaRT.ValueRef key) unique
    | LookupComplete(LuaRT.ValueRef value) unique
    | LookupTypeError(LuaRT.ValueRef receiver, LuaRT.ValueRef key) unique
    | LookupLoopLimitExceeded unique

  TableSetState =
      SetStart(LuaRT.ValueRef table, LuaRT.ValueRef key, LuaRT.ValueRef value) unique
    | SetRawTable(LuaRT.TableRef table, LuaRT.ValueRef key, LuaRT.ValueRef value) unique
    | SetMetatable(LuaRT.ValueRef receiver, LuaRT.Metamethod method) unique
    | SetNewIndexTableChain(LuaRT.TableRef next_table, LuaRT.Count depth) unique
    | SetNewIndexFunctionCall(LuaRT.ValueRef function, LuaRT.ValueRef receiver, LuaRT.ValueRef key, LuaRT.ValueRef value) unique
    | SetComplete unique
    | SetTypeError(LuaRT.ValueRef receiver, LuaRT.ValueRef key) unique
    | SetLoopLimitExceeded unique

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Metamethods in PUC order
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------

  Metamethod =
      TM_INDEX
    | TM_NEWINDEX
    | TM_GC
    | TM_MODE
    | TM_LEN
    | TM_EQ
    | TM_ADD
    | TM_SUB
    | TM_MUL
    | TM_MOD
    | TM_POW
    | TM_DIV
    | TM_IDIV
    | TM_BAND
    | TM_BOR
    | TM_BXOR
    | TM_SHL
    | TM_SHR
    | TM_UNM
    | TM_BNOT
    | TM_LT
    | TM_LE
    | TM_CONCAT
    | TM_CALL
    | TM_CLOSE

  MetamethodLookup =
      LookupFirstOperand(LuaRT.ValueRef left, LuaRT.Metamethod method) unique
    | LookupSecondOperand(LuaRT.ValueRef right, LuaRT.Metamethod method) unique
    | LookupReceiver(LuaRT.ValueRef receiver, LuaRT.Metamethod method) unique
    | MetamethodFound(LuaRT.ValueRef function) unique
    | MetamethodMissing unique

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Calls, callable classification, continuations
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------

  CallRef = (LuaRT.Name name) unique

  CallableKind =
      CallableLuaClosure
    | CallableCClosure
    | CallableLightCFunction
    | CallableViaCallMetamethod
    | NotCallable

  CallShape = (
    LuaRT.ValueRef callee,
    LuaRT.StackWindow args,
    LuaRT.CountSpec wanted_results,
    boolean is_tailcall,
    boolean may_yield
  ) unique

  CallContinuationKind =
      CallReturn
    | CallError
    | CallYield
    | TailCallReplaceFrame
    | CallMetamethodRetry

  CallResult = (
    LuaRT.CallRef call,
    LuaRT.ValueSeq results,
    LuaRT.CallContinuationKind continuation
  ) unique

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Errors, yields, resume state
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------

  ErrorKind =
      TypeError
    | ArithmeticError
    | CompareError
    | TableIndexNilError
    | TableIndexNaNError
    | NotCallableError
    | CloseError
    | RuntimeError
    | ErrNnilError

  ErrorState = (
    LuaRT.ErrorKind kind,
    LuaRT.ValueRef error_object,
    LuaRT.Pc saved_pc,
    LuaRT.TopRef saved_top
  ) unique

  YieldState = (
    LuaRT.Pc saved_pc,
    LuaRT.TopRef saved_top,
    LuaRT.ValueSeq yielded_values,
    LuaRT.ResumePoint resume_point
  ) unique

  ResumePoint =
      ResumeCall
    | ResumeMetamethod
    | ResumeTableGet
    | ResumeTableSet
    | ResumeArithmetic
    | ResumeComparison
    | ResumeConcat
    | ResumeClose
    | ResumeReturn
    | ResumeTForCall

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Close / TBC
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------

  CloseChain = (
    LuaRT.FrameRef frame,
    LuaRT.CloseItem* items
  ) unique

  CloseItem = (
    LuaRT.Slot slot,
    LuaRT.ValueRef value,
    LuaRT.CloseState state
  ) unique

  CloseState =
      ClosePending
    | CloseSkippedFalsey
    | CloseMethodLookup
    | CloseMethodFound(LuaRT.ValueRef method) unique
    | CloseCallRunning
    | CloseComplete
    | CloseErrorState(LuaRT.ErrorState error) unique
    | CloseYieldState(LuaRT.YieldState yield) unique

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Loop state
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------

  NumericForState =
      IntegerForState(
        LuaRT.Slot base,
        LuaRT.ValueRef count,
        LuaRT.ValueRef step,
        LuaRT.ValueRef control
      ) unique
    | FloatForState(
        LuaRT.Slot base,
        LuaRT.ValueRef limit,
        LuaRT.ValueRef step,
        LuaRT.ValueRef control
      ) unique

  GenericForState = (
    LuaRT.Slot base,
    LuaRT.ValueRef iterator,
    LuaRT.ValueRef state,
    LuaRT.ValueRef control,
    LuaRT.ValueRef closing,
    LuaRT.Count wanted_results
  ) unique

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- SETLIST / constructor state
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------

  SetListState = (
    LuaRT.TableRef table,
    LuaRT.StackWindow values,
    LuaRT.CountSpec value_count,
    LuaRT.Count start_index,
    boolean uses_extraarg,
    LuaRT.Ax extraarg
  ) unique

  ----------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Guards and contracts tied to CFG-visible values
  ----------------------------------------------------------------------

  Guard =
      TypeGuard(LuaRT.ValueRef value, LuaRT.TypeTest test) unique
    | TagGuard(LuaRT.ValueRef value, LuaRT.ValueTag tag) unique
    | ShapeGuard(LuaRT.TableRef table, LuaRT.TableShape shape) unique
    | MetatableGuard(LuaRT.ValueRef value, LuaRT.MetatableRef metatable) unique
    | NonZeroGuard(LuaRT.ValueRef value) unique
    | BoundsGuard(LuaRT.StackWindow window) unique
    | CompanionGuard(LuaRT.Pc pc, LuaRT.CompanionKind kind) unique

  CompanionKind =
      FollowingJmp
    | FollowingMMBIN
    | FollowingExtraArg
}
```

---

### 4.2 `LuaExec`: Semantic CFG over LuaRT

```asdl
module LuaExec {
  Name = (string text) unique

  Module = (
    LuaExec.Region* regions,
    LuaExec.Kernel* kernels
  ) unique

  Kernel = (
    LuaExec.Name id,
    LuaRT.Frame frame,
    LuaExec.Region body,
    LuaExec.Contract contract
  ) unique

  Region = (
    LuaExec.Name id,
    LuaExec.RegionKind kind,
    LuaExec.Param* params,
    LuaExec.Continuation* continuations,
    LuaExec.BlockId entry,
    LuaExec.Block* blocks
  ) unique

  RegionKind =
      ArithmeticRegion
    | TableGetRegion
    | TableSetRegion
    | LenRegion
    | ConcatRegion
    | CallRegion
    | TailCallRegion
    | ReturnRegion
    | VarargRegion
    | SetListRegion
    | CloseRegion
    | NumericForRegion
    | GenericForRegion
    | ErrorRegion
    | YieldRegion
    | GuardRegion

  BlockId = (LuaExec.Name name) unique
  BlockRef = (LuaExec.BlockId id) unique

  Param = (
    LuaExec.Name name,
    LuaExec.Type type
  ) unique

  Type =
      LuaValueType
    | LuaValueSeqType
    | LuaFrameType
    | LuaTableType
    | LuaStringType
    | LuaClosureType
    | LuaErrorType
    | LuaYieldType
    | LuaCountType
    | LuaBoolType
    | LuaNumberType
    | MoonType(string moon_type)

  ContinuationKind =
      OkCont
    | ErrorCont
    | YieldCont
    | ReturnCont
    | GuardFailCont
    | TailCallCont
    | CloseCont
    | LocalCont

  Continuation = (
    LuaExec.Name id,
    LuaExec.ContinuationKind kind,
    LuaExec.Param* params
  ) unique

  ContRef = (LuaExec.Name id) unique

  ContBinding = (
    LuaExec.ContRef continuation,
    LuaExec.BlockRef target,
    LuaExec.Arg* args
  ) unique

  Arg = (
    LuaExec.Name name,
    LuaExec.Value value
  ) unique

  Value =
      RuntimeValue(LuaRT.ValueRef value) unique
    | RuntimeSeq(LuaRT.ValueSeq seq) unique
    | RuntimeFrame(LuaRT.FrameRef frame) unique
    | ConstTValue(LuaRT.TValue value) unique
    | TempValue(LuaExec.Name name) unique
    | UnitValue unique

  Expr =
      ValueExpr(LuaExec.Value value) unique
    | TypeTestExpr(LuaRT.ValueRef value, LuaRT.TypeTest test) unique
    | TruthinessExpr(LuaRT.ValueRef value) unique
    | ProjectExpr(LuaRT.ValueRef value, LuaRT.ValueProjection projection) unique
    | RawGetExpr(LuaRT.TableRef table, LuaRT.ValueRef key) unique
    | RawSetExpr(LuaRT.TableRef table, LuaRT.ValueRef key, LuaRT.ValueRef value) unique
    | MetamethodLookupExpr(LuaRT.MetamethodLookup lookup) unique
    | AdjustResultsExpr(LuaRT.ValueSeq seq, LuaRT.ResultAdjustment adjustment) unique
    | NumberOpExpr(LuaExec.NumberOp op, LuaRT.ValueRef left, LuaRT.ValueRef right) unique
    | StringConcatExpr(LuaRT.ValueSeq values) unique

  NumberOp =
      Add
    | Sub
    | Mul
    | Mod
    | Pow
    | Div
    | IDiv
    | Band
    | Bor
    | Bxor
    | Shl
    | Shr
    | Unm
    | Bnot

  Choice =
      BoolChoice(LuaExec.Value value) unique
    | TypeChoice(LuaRT.ValueRef value, LuaRT.TypeTest test) unique
    | TruthinessChoice(LuaRT.ValueRef value) unique
    | NumericChoice(LuaExec.NumericTest test, LuaRT.ValueRef left, LuaRT.ValueRef right) unique
    | EqualityChoice(LuaRT.ValueRef left, LuaRT.ValueRef right) unique
    | RawGetHitChoice(LuaRT.RawGetResult result) unique
    | MetamethodPresentChoice(LuaRT.MetamethodLookup lookup) unique
    | CountChoice(LuaRT.CountSpec count) unique
    | GuardChoice(LuaRT.Guard guard) unique

  NumericTest =
      Eq
    | Lt
    | Le
    | Gt
    | Ge
    | NonZero

  Op =
      Let(LuaExec.Name dst, LuaExec.Expr expr) unique
    | AssignValue(LuaRT.ValueRef dst, LuaExec.Value src) unique
    | AssignSeq(LuaRT.StackWindow dst, LuaRT.ValueSeq src, LuaRT.ResultAdjustment adjustment) unique
    | SetTop(LuaRT.TopRef top, LuaRT.CountSpec count) unique
    | Project(LuaExec.Name dst, LuaRT.ValueRef src, LuaRT.ValueProjection projection) unique
    | Guard(LuaRT.Guard guard, LuaExec.ContRef on_fail) unique
    | EmitRegion(LuaExec.Name region, LuaExec.Arg* args, LuaExec.ContBinding* continuations) unique

  Terminator =
      Jump(LuaExec.BlockRef target, LuaExec.Arg* args) unique
    | Branch(LuaExec.Choice choice, LuaExec.BlockRef if_true, LuaExec.BlockRef if_false) unique
    | Continue(LuaExec.ContRef continuation, LuaExec.Arg* args) unique
    | Return(LuaRT.ValueSeq values) unique
    | Error(LuaRT.ErrorState error) unique
    | Yield(LuaRT.YieldState yield) unique
    | Unreachable unique

  Block = (
    LuaExec.BlockId id,
    LuaExec.Param* params,
    LuaExec.Op* ops,
    LuaExec.Terminator terminator
  ) unique

  Contract = (
    LuaExec.Obligation* obligations,
    LuaExec.Guarantee* guarantees
  ) unique

  Obligation =
      RequiresGuard(LuaRT.Guard guard) unique
    | RequiresResolvedRegion(LuaExec.Name region) unique
    | RequiresContinuation(LuaExec.ContRef continuation) unique
    | RequiresCompanion(LuaRT.Pc pc, LuaRT.CompanionKind kind) unique

  Guarantee =
      ProducesValue(LuaRT.ValueRef value) unique
    | PreservesFrame(LuaRT.FrameRef frame) unique
    | UpdatesTop(LuaRT.TopRef top) unique
    | ClosesChain(LuaRT.CloseChain chain) unique
}
```

Important: `EmitRegion` is legal only when the referenced region body is present in the same ASDL module or otherwise resolved as an ASDL CFG fragment. A region name alone is not enough.

---

## 5. Generic Opcode Family Mapping

### 5.1 Arithmetic + `MMBIN*`

PUC arithmetic plus following `MMBIN`, `MMBINI`, or `MMBINK` is one semantic unit for generic behavior.

Mapping:

```text
Arithmetic opcode + companion MMBIN*
  -> LuaExec.ArithmeticRegion
       primitive numeric path
       integer/float conversion path
       bitwise integer conversion path
       non-primitive path
       ordered metamethod lookup
       metamethod call
       result placement
       error/yield continuations
```

Required ASDL choices:

- operand type tests,
- integer vs float operation,
- conversion success/failure,
- division/modulo zero cases,
- companion presence guard,
- metamethod lookup first operand then second operand,
- `MMBINI/MMBINK` flip flag,
- destination is original arithmetic result register, not the `MMBIN` register.

`MMBIN*` may be treated as no-op only when CFG proves primitive success makes it unreachable.

---

### 5.2 Comparisons + Following `JMP`

PUC comparison/test opcodes depend on the following `JMP`.

Mapping:

```text
EQ/LT/LE/EQI/EQK/LTI/LEI/GTI/GEI/TEST/TESTSET + following JMP
  -> LuaExec comparison/test CFG
       compute condition
       apply k/polarity
       true edge executes following JMP target
       false edge skips following JMP
```

Required ASDL choices:

- raw equality vs metamethod equality,
- number comparison,
- string comparison,
- order metamethod lookup/call,
- immediate comparison float-origin flag,
- `k` polarity,
- following-`JMP` companion guard.

---

### 5.3 `GETTABLE`

Mapping:

```text
GETTABLE A B C
  -> LuaExec.TableGetRegion
       classify receiver
       raw table get
       hit -> assign result
       miss -> __index lookup
       non-table -> type/userdata/global metatable __index lookup
       __index absent -> nil or type error
       __index table -> repeat chain
       __index function -> call
       loop cap/error/yield continuations
```

Required ASDL choices:

- integer key fast path,
- generic key raw lookup,
- `RawHit` vs `RawMiss`,
- absent sentinel distinct from ordinary nil,
- table metatable,
- userdata metatable,
- global type metatable,
- `__index` absent/table/function,
- chain depth cap.

---

### 5.4 `SETTABLE`

Mapping:

```text
SETTABLE A B C
  -> LuaExec.TableSetRegion
       classify receiver
       raw table update/insert
       absent path -> __newindex lookup
       non-table -> type/userdata/global metatable __newindex lookup
       __newindex table -> repeat chain
       __newindex function -> call
       nil/NaN key errors
       write barrier path
```

Required ASDL choices:

- existing table slot update,
- absent slot insert,
- nil key error,
- NaN key error,
- `__newindex` absent/table/function,
- metatable lookup sources,
- loop cap,
- barrier obligation.

---

### 5.5 `LEN`

Mapping:

```text
LEN A B
  -> LuaExec.LenRegion
       string byte length
       table: __len present -> call
       table: __len absent -> raw table length
       non-table: metatable __len lookup
       missing __len -> type error
```

Required ASDL choices:

- string vs table vs other type,
- table raw border length,
- metatable `TM_LEN`,
- metamethod call,
- error/yield continuations.

---

### 5.6 `CONCAT`

Mapping:

```text
CONCAT A B
  -> LuaExec.ConcatRegion
       operate over stack range ending at top
       pairwise/string sequence concatenation
       numeric-to-string conversion
       __concat lookup/call
       continuation after yielded metamethod
```

Required ASDL choices:

- already-string operands,
- numeric convertible operands,
- non-convertible operands,
- `TM_CONCAT` lookup,
- repeated concat state,
- yield resume state.

---

### 5.7 `CALL`

Mapping:

```text
CALL A B C
  -> LuaExec.CallRegion
       compute argument window
       B==0 consumes previous top
       C-1 fixed wanted results or C==0 open results
       classify callee
       Lua closure frame setup
       C closure call path
       __call retry path for non-functions
       result adjustment
       top update for open result
       error/yield continuations
```

Required ASDL choices:

- fixed vs open argument count,
- fixed vs open result count,
- Lua closure,
- C closure,
- light C function,
- non-function with `__call`,
- non-callable error,
- argument shift for `__call`,
- frame creation,
- result movement/fill/truncate,
- yield legality.

---

### 5.8 `TAILCALL`

Mapping:

```text
TAILCALL A B C k
  -> LuaExec.TailCallRegion
       B==0 consumes previous top
       C hidden-vararg correction
       k close-upvalue/TBC sequencing
       callable classification
       Lua tailcall frame replacement
       C tailcall result path
       error/yield continuations
```

Required ASDL choices:

- open argument count,
- hidden-vararg fixed-param correction,
- close-before-tailcall path,
- Lua tailcall frame reuse,
- C tailcall return path,
- `__call` retry.

---

### 5.9 `RETURN`

Mapping:

```text
RETURN A B C k
  -> LuaExec.ReturnRegion
       B==0 returns up to top
       fixed result window otherwise
       C hidden-vararg correction
       k close-upvalue/TBC sequencing
       caller result adjustment
       Lua frame return
```

Required ASDL choices:

- fixed vs open return count,
- hidden-vararg correction,
- close chain,
- close may error/yield,
- final caller result adjustment.

MoonCFG native `return` is not equivalent to Lua `RETURN` unless the kernel boundary is a whole Lua-frame boundary with matching result semantics.

---

### 5.10 `VARARG` / `GETVARG`

Mapping:

```text
VARARG A B C k
  -> LuaExec.VarargRegion
       fixed copy
       open copy and top update
       vararg table behavior when k/B indicates table source

GETVARG A B C
  -> LuaExec.VarargRegion
       dynamic key lookup into vararg source/table
       integer in range -> hidden arg
       string "n" -> count
       otherwise nil
```

Required ASDL choices:

- hidden frame varargs,
- vararg table source,
- fixed count,
- open count,
- top update,
- integer key,
- `"n"` key,
- out-of-range nil.

---

### 5.11 `SETLIST`

Mapping:

```text
SETLIST A vB vC k [EXTRAARG]
  -> LuaExec.SetListRegion
       table constructor array fill
       vB==0 consumes top
       k consumes following EXTRAARG
       compute start/last
       raw array writes from R[A+1..A+n]
       resize/barrier path as required
```

Required ASDL choices:

- fixed vs open value count,
- extraarg extension,
- raw array fill loop,
- table identity,
- 1-based Lua array index,
- no `__newindex` path for constructor fill.

---

### 5.12 `CLOSE` / `TBC`

Mapping:

```text
TBC A
  -> update frame close chain / require __close unless falsey

CLOSE A
  -> LuaExec.CloseRegion
       close open upvalues
       traverse TBC chain
       skip nil/false
       lookup __close
       call __close(self[, err])
       sequence errors/yields
       propagate or replace error during unwind
```

Required ASDL choices:

- false/nil close skip,
- missing `__close` error for TBC creation,
- close item ordering,
- close while returning,
- close while error-unwinding,
- close call result/error/yield.

---

### 5.13 `FORPREP` / `FORLOOP`

Mapping:

```text
FORPREP / FORLOOP
  -> LuaExec.NumericForRegion
       integer-prepared state variant
       float-prepared state variant
       init/limit/step conversion
       zero-step error
       skip/body decision
       loop update
```

Required ASDL choices:

- integer vs float prepared state,
- integer count/step/control layout,
- float limit/step/control layout,
- conversion success/error,
- positive vs negative step,
- loop continuation target.

Current runtime numeric-for layout must not be used as oracle.

---

### 5.14 `TFORPREP` / `TFORCALL` / `TFORLOOP`

Mapping:

```text
TFORPREP
  -> swap control/closing variables
  -> create TBC close state if closing value is not falsey

TFORCALL
  -> call iterator(state, control)
  -> place wanted results at R[A+3...]

TFORLOOP
  -> test R[A+3] for non-nil
  -> continue loop if non-nil
```

Required ASDL choices:

- iterator/state/control slots,
- closing variable slot,
- TBC creation,
- iterator call,
- wanted result count,
- first result nil/non-nil test,
- loop target,
- close behavior.

`lvm.c` is the oracle for `R[A+3]`.

---

## 6. Guardrails

### Forbidden

- Opaque helper calls.
- Opaque region names without ASDL region bodies.
- Opcode-shaped final IR.
- `ExecCtx` operations that hide Lua semantics.
- Integer `out_tag` / `out_event_kind` protocols.
- Host interpreter dispatch.
- Resume protocol handoff.
- `CallProtocolExit`, `CloseProtocolExit`, `GenericForProtocolExit`, `SetListProtocolExit`, `GetVargProtocolExit` as success.
- Rejection-as-success.
- Contracts used as execution behavior.
- Strings used as semantic tags.

### Required

- Every semantic branch is an ASDL sum/enum.
- Every continuation is typed and resolved.
- Every region used by `EmitRegion` is present as ASDL CFG.
- Every payload projection is dominated by a type/tag proof.
- Every open count/top dependency is explicit.
- Every yield/error path carries typed saved state.

---

## 7. Source Field Preservation Checklist

Already preserved:

- `RETURN C/k`
- `SETLIST k/EXTRAARG`
- `ERRNNIL Bx/name_index`

Remaining fields to preserve before full semantics:

- `CALL A/B/C`, including `B==0`, `C==0`, previous/next `top`.
- `TAILCALL A/B/C/k`, with `C` as hidden-vararg correction.
- `VARARG A/B/C/k`, including vararg table mode.
- `GETVARG A/B/C`.
- `MMBINI/MMBINK k` flip flag.
- Immediate comparison `C` float-origin flag.
- Comparison/test following-`JMP` pairing.
- `NEWTABLE vB/vC/k/EXTRAARG`.
- `LOADKX` following `EXTRAARG`.
- Generic companion-instruction invariants for `MMBIN`, `JMP`, `EXTRAARG`.
- Numeric-for prepared-state layout facts.
- Generic-for `TFORPREP/TFORCALL/TFORLOOP` slot layout and close state.
- Close/TBC ordering and error/yield state.

---

## 8. Boundary Question: Whole-Function vs Window Kernels

The design supports full correctness only if kernel boundaries are explicit.

### Whole-function kernels

A whole-function kernel can model Lua frame lifecycle internally:

- calls,
- returns,
- top,
- varargs,
- close chains,
- yields,
- errors,
- loop state.

This is the cleanest semantic boundary because no partial Lua machine state must be exported mid-operation.

### Window kernels

If bytecode windows remain the compilation unit, every window exit must carry a complete typed state snapshot:

```text
TypedDeoptExit {
  pc,
  frame,
  stack window values,
  top,
  varargs,
  open result sequence,
  close chain,
  pending call/yield/error state,
  loop state,
  contract/guard failure reason
}
```

A window exit must not mean “resume interpreter protocol.” It must be a typed state boundary whose meaning is ASDL-visible and whose consumer is explicitly defined.

Open decision: whether accepted full-generic kernels are whole-function CFGs or window CFGs with typed state/deopt exits.

---

## 9. Validation Invariants

Validators must fail closed.

Required invariants:

1. No executable `LuaNF.Program` inside accepted kernels.
2. No old protocol exits inside accepted kernels.
3. No `out_*` semantic ABI.
4. No string semantic tags.
5. All `RegionRef`s resolve to ASDL region bodies.
6. All continuations are filled exactly once with matching names/types.
7. All blocks terminate explicitly.
8. No implicit fallthrough.
9. All branch targets resolve.
10. All jump args match block params by name and type.
11. Payload projections require dominating type/tag proof.
12. Sentinels cannot be returned as ordinary Lua nil unless explicitly converted.
13. Table miss sentinel is distinct from ordinary nil.
14. `top` producers/consumers are explicit.
15. Open counts are not silently converted to fixed counts.
16. Companion opcode requirements are validated.
17. Metamethod enum order matches PUC.
18. Call/yield/error/close continuations carry saved `pc`/`top` where PUC requires it.
19. Contracts reference CFG-visible values/guards only.
20. `UnsupportedExit` cannot represent valid-but-unimplemented Lua behavior in an accepted kernel.

---

## 10. Test Policy

Main tests must assert semantic honesty and oracle fidelity.

Required tests:

- ASDL schema contains `LuaRT`, `LuaExec`, and `MoonCFG` semantic structures.
- Accepted kernels contain no `LuaNF.Program`.
- Accepted kernels contain no protocol exits.
- Emitted Moonlift contains no `out_tag` or equivalent protocol ABI.
- Region references resolve to ASDL CFG bodies.
- Payload projection without type proof is rejected.
- Table miss and nil are distinct.
- `ERRNNIL` follows PUC semantics.
- Arithmetic+`MMBIN` pairing is enforced.
- Comparison+`JMP` pairing is enforced.
- `SETLIST`/`EXTRAARG` pairing is enforced.
- Generic table/metamethod/call/return/vararg/close/yield paths match PUC fixtures.
- Existing runtime divergences are tested against PUC, not current runtime shortcuts.

Disallowed tests:

- Rejection as positive coverage.
- Protocol exit emission as success.
- Absence of `LuaSrc.Op` as sufficient proof.
- Opaque helper invocation as semantic success.
- Runtime module behavior used as oracle when it conflicts with PUC.

---

## 11. Open Decisions

These must be answered without weakening the design:

1. Are full-generic accepted kernels whole-function CFGs or window CFGs with typed deopt/state exits?
2. What exact Lua value ABI backs `LuaRT.TValue` in Moonlift?
3. How are GC barriers and allocator effects represented without opaque helpers?
4. How are C calls represented while avoiding host interpreter handoff?
5. What yield boundaries are legal for compiled kernels?
6. How are protected calls, errors, and unwind state represented?
7. How do contracts attach to LuaExec regions and MoonCFG blocks?
8. Which runtime modules can be audited and converted into ASDL CFG fragments?
9. How are type metatables for non-table/non-userdata values represented?
10. How are Lua closure frames represented for nested compiled calls?
11. How are stale guards invalidated?
12. What is the exact typed state snapshot for window exits, if windows remain?

These are open design decisions, not excuses for hidden mechanisms.

## Documenter Output — 2026-06-02 15:48:11

# SpongeJIT Full Generic Lua Semantics ASDL -> MoonCFG -> Copy-and-Patch Stencils Design

**Workflow ID:** `wf-b7b79a56`  
**Status:** Architecture update incorporating copy-and-patch stencil backend clarification.

## Goal

Enable SpongeJIT to compile full generic Lua bytecode semantics into explicit ASDL semantic CFGs, lower those CFGs into ASDL-described copy-and-patch stencil templates, and materialize executable code by copying binary stencil bytes and patching typed holes, with no Lua interpreter dependency, no protocol handoff, and no recovery of semantics from backend stencil descriptors.

## Incentives

The earlier ASDL/MoonCFG plan restored semantic honesty by requiring Lua behavior to be represented in ASDL-visible `LuaRT`, `LuaExec`, and `MoonCFG` structures before emission. That was necessary but incomplete: the final SpongeJIT goal is not only mechanical Moonlift source rendering. The final goal remains **copy-and-patch stencil execution**: prebuilt binary implementations with holes for constants, stack offsets, branch targets, call targets, and ABI-specific placements, copied and patched at runtime.
