The clarification matters because the old native stencil path was retired for architectural reasons, not because copy-and-patch itself was rejected. `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/SPONJIT_COPY_LINK_PATCH.md` retires the old Copy-Link-Patch ABI — old descriptors, `sponbank` selector tables, byte stencil banks, relocation metadata conventions, endpoint ABI, linker runtime, and fusion planner — because semantics were being recovered or implied in backend descriptors. That was the failure. The retained goal is a copy-and-patch backend whose stencils are compiled artifacts of explicit ASDL semantic CFG fragments.

## Current State

The current reset has already established the principle that successful compilation must not be a protocol exit or rejection-as-success. The pipeline now treats `MoonCFG` as the terminal semantic CFG representation for accepted kernels:

```text
LuaSrc / LuaSem / LuaNF
  -> MoonCFG ASDL
  -> mechanical Moonlift rendering
```

The ASDL reset added `MoonCFG.Kernel`, `MoonCFG.Region`, `MoonCFG.Block`, `MoonCFG.Op`, `MoonCFG.Terminator`, typed choices, block params, jump/branch validation, and a mechanical emitter. Old `MoonOut` paths are wrappers over MoonCFG. Protocol exits such as `CallProtocolExit`, `CloseProtocolExit`, `GenericForProtocolExit`, `SetListProtocolExit`, and `GetVargProtocolExit` are forbidden as compiled success.

The later full-generic design added the need for semantic ASDL layers:

```text
LuaSrc
  -> LuaRT / LuaExec
  -> MoonCFG
```

where `LuaRT` models Lua values, stack/top, varargs, multivalue sequences, tables, metatables, calls, yields, errors, and close state, and `LuaExec` models semantic CFG regions over those runtime objects.

That plan correctly rejects hidden helpers, protocol tags, opaque region names, opcode-shaped final IR, and backend decisions that infer Lua behavior. However, it stopped at MoonCFG/source rendering. It did not specify how MoonCFG becomes the intended copy-and-patch binary stencil system. This update fills that gap.

## Chosen Target

The chosen target is now:

```text
LuaSrc
  -> LuaRT / LuaExec
  -> MoonCFG
  -> StencilIR / StencilTemplate ASDL
  -> binary stencil bank
  -> runtime copy + patch materialization
```

`MoonCFG` remains the semantic compiled CFG product. `StencilIR` / `StencilTemplate` is a backend artifact layer derived from that CFG. It must not introduce semantics. Its job is to describe binary code templates, typed patch holes, relocations, symbols, linkage, variants, and materialization plans.

## Retired Old ABI vs Retained Copy-and-Patch Goal

### Retired

The old Copy-Link-Patch native stencil ABI is retired:

- old semantic descriptors,
- `sponbank` selector tables,
- byte stencil banks keyed by backend descriptor meaning,
- relocation metadata that implied semantic roles,
- endpoint ABI conventions that encoded control protocol,
- linker runtime that fused or selected semantic behavior,
- fusion planner based on opcode/protocol descriptors.

That system is not allowed to return under new names.

### Retained

The retained goal is copy-and-patch compilation:

- compiled binary code templates,
- holes for constants, offsets, labels, call targets, branch targets, and placement choices,
- library/bank variants,
- runtime materialization by copying bytes and patching typed holes.

The key distinction is that stencil templates are generated from ASDL semantic CFG identity. They do not describe Lua semantics themselves.

## Full Pipeline

```text
PUC bytecode / trace events
  -> LuaSrc
       exact opcode fields and companion-instruction facts

  -> LuaRT / LuaExec
       explicit Lua semantic state and semantic CFG regions

  -> MoonCFG
       typed Moonlift-compatible CFG:
       regions, blocks, ops, choices, continuations, terminators

  -> StencilIR / StencilTemplate ASDL
       backend artifact model:
       templates, patch holes, relocations, symbols, variants, linkage

  -> binary stencil bank
       object-code blobs produced from MoonCFG fragments via Moonlift/Cranelift

  -> runtime copy + patch
       select by ASDL-derived key,
       copy bytes,
       patch typed holes,
       resolve internal branches/calls,
       publish executable code
```

Semantics flow only through `LuaSrc`, `LuaRT`, `LuaExec`, and `MoonCFG`. Stencil layers carry compiled representation and patch metadata only.

## Stencil Backend ASDL Sketch

Exact field names may change, but these distinctions are required.

```asdl
module Stencil {
  Name = (string text) unique

  --------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Module / bank
  --------------------------------------------------------------------

  StencilModule = (
    Stencil.BankIndex bank,
    Stencil.StencilTemplate* templates,
    Stencil.Symbol* symbols,
    Stencil.Linkage linkage
  ) unique

  BankIndex = (
    Stencil.VariantKey* variants,
    Stencil.TemplateIndexEntry* entries
  ) unique

  TemplateIndexEntry = (
    Stencil.VariantKey key,
    Stencil.Name template_name
  ) unique

  --------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Templates
  --------------------------------------------------------------------

  StencilTemplate = (
    Stencil.Name name,
    Stencil.StencilKind kind,
    Stencil.VariantKey variant,
    Stencil.CodeBlobRef code,
    Stencil.PatchHole* holes,
    Stencil.Reloc* relocs,
    Stencil.Symbol* local_symbols,
    Stencil.MaterializationPlan plan
  ) unique

  StencilKind =
      KernelStencil
    | RegionStencil
    | BlockStencil
    | BranchStencil
    | CallStencil
    | GuardStencil
    | RuntimeBoundaryStencil

  VariantKey = (
    MoonCFG.KernelKind kernel_kind,
    LuaExec.RegionKind region_kind,
    LuaContract.Contract contract,
    Stencil.Placement placement,
    Stencil.TargetABI target_abi,
    Stencil.FeatureSet features
  ) unique

  FeatureSet = (
    string arch,
    string os,
    string cpu_features,
    string codegen_version
  ) unique

  TargetABI = (
    string triple,
    string calling_convention,
    string pointer_width,
    string endian
  ) unique

  --------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Code blobs
  --------------------------------------------------------------------

  CodeBlobRef = (
    Stencil.Name symbol,
    number byte_size,
    string content_hash
  ) unique

  Symbol = (
    Stencil.Name name,
    Stencil.SymbolKind kind,
    Stencil.SymbolVisibility visibility,
    number offset
  ) unique

  SymbolKind =
      EntrySymbol
    | LocalLabel
    | ExternalTarget
    | ContinuationTarget
    | PatchAnchor

  SymbolVisibility =
      Local
    | BankExported
    | ExternalImported

  --------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Patch holes
  --------------------------------------------------------------------

  PatchHole = (
    Stencil.Name id,
    Stencil.PatchKind kind,
    number offset,
    number width_bytes,
    Stencil.PatchEncoding encoding,
    Stencil.PatchSource source
  ) unique

  PatchKind =
      ImmediatePatch
    | StackOffsetPatch
    | ConstAddressPatch
    | BranchTargetPatch
    | CallTargetPatch
    | SymbolAddressPatch
    | FrameLayoutPatch
    | RegisterPatch
    | VTablePatch

  PatchEncoding =
      U8
    | U16
    | U32
    | U64
    | I32
    | I64
    | PcRel32
    | PcRel64
    | Abs64
    | TargetSpecific(string encoding)

  PatchSource =
      FromImmediate(Stencil.ImmediateOperand imm) unique
    | FromStack(Stencil.StackOperand stack) unique
    | FromRegister(Stencil.RegisterOperand reg) unique
    | FromSymbol(Stencil.Symbol symbol) unique
    | FromMaterializationValue(Stencil.Name name) unique

  --------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Relocations
  --------------------------------------------------------------------

  Reloc = (
    Stencil.Name id,
    Stencil.RelocKind kind,
    number offset,
    Stencil.Symbol target,
    number addend
  ) unique

  RelocKind =
      AbsAddr
    | PcRel
    | GotRelative
    | PltRelative
    | SectionRelative
    | TargetReloc(string name)

  --------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Operands and placement
  --------------------------------------------------------------------

  RegisterOperand = (
    Stencil.RegisterClass class,
    Stencil.Name register
  ) unique

  RegisterClass =
      GPR
    | FPR
    | Vector
    | Predicate
    | TargetRegisterClass(string name)

  StackOperand = (
    Stencil.Name frame,
    number slot,
    number byte_offset,
    number width_bytes
  ) unique

  ImmediateOperand =
      ImmI64(number value) unique
    | ImmF64(number value) unique
    | ImmBool(boolean value) unique
    | ImmSymbol(Stencil.Symbol symbol) unique
    | ImmBytes(string hash, number byte_size) unique

  Operand =
      RegisterOp(Stencil.RegisterOperand reg) unique
    | StackOp(Stencil.StackOperand stack) unique
    | ImmediateOp(Stencil.ImmediateOperand imm) unique
    | SymbolOp(Stencil.Symbol symbol) unique

  Placement = (
    Stencil.RegisterOperand* fixed_registers,
    Stencil.StackOperand* stack_slots,
    Stencil.Operand* operands
  ) unique

  --------------------------------------------------------------------
  -- Materialization
  --------------------------------------------------------------------

  MaterializationPlan = (
    Stencil.PatchSite* patch_sites,
    Stencil.LinkStep* link_steps,
    Stencil.EntryPoint entry
  ) unique

  PatchSite = (
    Stencil.PatchHole hole,
    Stencil.PatchValue value
  ) unique

  PatchValue =
      PatchImmediate(Stencil.ImmediateOperand imm) unique
    | PatchStack(Stencil.StackOperand stack) unique
    | PatchRegister(Stencil.RegisterOperand reg) unique
    | PatchSymbol(Stencil.Symbol symbol) unique
    | PatchComputed(Stencil.Name name) unique

  LinkStep =
      ResolveInternalBranch(Stencil.Symbol from, Stencil.Symbol to) unique
    | ResolveInternalCall(Stencil.Symbol from, Stencil.Symbol to) unique
    | ResolveExternalSymbol(Stencil.Symbol symbol) unique
    | ApplyReloc(Stencil.Reloc reloc) unique

  EntryPoint = (
    Stencil.Symbol symbol,
    Stencil.TargetABI abi
  ) unique

  Linkage = (
    Stencil.Symbol* exported,
    Stencil.Symbol* imported,
    Stencil.Reloc* required_relocs
  ) unique
}
```

## How Semantic Region Templates Become Stencils

A stencil template is generated from ASDL structural identity:

```text
LuaExec.Region / MoonCFG.Region
  + LuaContract.Contract
  + placement / ABI / target choices
  -> VariantKey
  -> Moonlift / Cranelift object generation
  -> CodeBlobRef + PatchHole* + Reloc*
  -> StencilTemplate
```

The foundry enumerates semantic region shapes and variant choices from ASDL, not from opcode descriptors. For each shape:

1. The semantic CFG is already explicit in `LuaExec` / `MoonCFG`.
2. Moonlift renders or builds the CFG mechanically.
3. Cranelift produces object bytes.
4. Object extraction records code bytes and relocation information.
5. The stencil generator converts relocations and parameterized locations into typed `PatchHole` and `Reloc` ASDL nodes.
6. The binary bytes are stored as a `CodeBlobRef`.
7. The resulting `StencilTemplate` is indexed by a `VariantKey`.

Patch holes are typed backend facts. They can represent “patch this immediate,” “patch this stack offset,” or “patch this branch target.” They cannot mean “this is a GETTABLE fast path” or “resume CALL protocol.”

## Semantics Stay Out of Stencils

Stencil templates are compiled artifacts of semantic CFG fragments. They are not a semantic IR.

Allowed stencil facts:

- code byte identity,
- object symbol identity,
- target ABI,
- register/stack placement,
- immediate patch sites,
- relocation sites,
- branch/call target holes,
- materialization ordering,
- bank indexing.

Forbidden stencil facts:

- opcode names as semantic keys,
- protocol tags,
- Lua operation descriptors,
- hidden “helper kind” selectors,
- interpreter resume states,
- backend decisions that choose Lua semantics,
- descriptor fields from which Lua semantics are reconstructed.

If a stencil must differ for table hit vs metatable path, that distinction must already exist in `LuaExec` / `MoonCFG`; the stencil variant only records the compiled artifact for that ASDL branch/region shape.

## Foundry and Dedupe

Foundry representative keys must change from old descriptor-oriented identity to ASDL-derived identity:

```text
RepresentativeKey =
  structural_key(LuaExec.Region or MoonCFG.Region)
  + structural_key(LuaContract.Contract)
  + structural_key(Stencil.VariantKey)
```

The key must not include old stencil descriptors, opcode names, protocol exit classes, `sponbank` selectors, or backend semantic labels.

Dedupe rules:

- Two stencils may dedupe only if they arise from the same ASDL semantic CFG shape, compatible contracts, and identical variant choices.
- Backend byte equality alone is not semantic equivalence.
- Opcode-family equivalence is not enough.
- Protocol-exit equivalence is forbidden because protocol exits are not compiled success.
- Placement and ABI choices are part of stencil identity when they affect patching or bytes.

## Runtime Materialization

Runtime materialization is a mechanical copy-and-patch process:

1. Receive or compute an ASDL-derived `VariantKey`.
2. Look up the corresponding `StencilTemplate` in `BankIndex`.
3. Allocate executable destination memory.
4. Copy bytes from `CodeBlobRef`.
5. Apply each `PatchSite`:
   - constants,
   - stack offsets,
   - register encodings if target supports them,
   - frame layout offsets,
   - branch targets,
   - call targets,
   - symbol addresses.
6. Apply relocations and linkage steps.
7. Resolve internal branch and call targets.
8. Publish the entry point.

The runtime materializer must not inspect Lua opcodes, choose Lua semantics, run an interpreter, interpret protocol tags, or recover semantic meaning from stencil metadata.

## Guardrails

Non-negotiable stencil guardrails:

1. **No opcode-shaped stencil keys.**  
   Stencil keys derive from ASDL semantic CFG identity and variant choices, not `OP_GETTABLE`, `OP_CALL`, etc.

2. **No hidden semantic descriptor recovery.**  
   Backend descriptors must not contain enough semantic tags to reconstruct Lua behavior outside ASDL.

3. **No protocol out-tags.**  
   `out_tag`, `out_event_kind`, and equivalent continuation ABIs are forbidden.

4. **No interpreter helper stencils.**  
   A stencil that calls “execute opcode,” “resume Lua,” “run protocol,” or opaque Lua runtime helpers is invalid.

5. **No backend-only semantics.**  
   If behavior is not present in `LuaRT`, `LuaExec`, or `MoonCFG`, it cannot appear in `StencilIR`.

6. **Typed holes only.**  
   Patch holes must have explicit ASDL kind, width, encoding, source, and target ABI meaning.

7. **Resolved region bodies.**  
   A stencil for a semantic region must be tied to an ASDL region body, not just a region name.

8. **Contracts do not execute.**  
   Contracts may constrain or validate stencil variants, but they do not stand in for semantics.

## Validation Invariants

Stencil validation must fail closed.

Required invariants:

- Every `StencilTemplate` has a resolvable `VariantKey`.
- Every `VariantKey` points back to ASDL semantic CFG identity.
- No old protocol exits appear in stencil inputs.
- No old retired descriptor types appear.
- No `sponbank` selector semantics appear.
- No opcode names are used as semantic stencil keys.
- Every `PatchHole` has a known kind, width, encoding, and source.
- Every relocation target resolves through `Symbol` / `Linkage`.
- Every internal branch/call target resolves before publication.
- Every external symbol is explicitly declared.
- Every `CodeBlobRef` hash and size matches stored bytes.
- Target ABI and feature set match the runtime materialization target.
- Register and stack placements match the template’s declared placement.
- Materialization does not require inspecting Lua semantics.
- Stencil templates cannot call interpreter/protocol helpers.
- Runtime copy+patch cannot silently skip required holes or relocations.

## Test Policy Update

Stencil-layer tests must prove both binary materialization correctness and semantic honesty.

Required tests:

- `StencilModule`, `StencilTemplate`, `PatchHole`, `Reloc`, `VariantKey`, `MaterializationPlan`, and `BankIndex` schema validation.
- Stencil keys derive from `LuaExec` / `MoonCFG` structural identity plus contracts and variant choices.
- Old copy-link-patch descriptors are rejected.
- Opcode-shaped stencil keys are rejected.
- Protocol out-tags are absent from generated templates and emitted/materialized code paths.
- Patch holes are typed and fully applied.
- Missing patch values fail validation.
- Unknown relocation kinds fail validation.
- Internal branch/call links resolve deterministically.
- Runtime materialization copies bytes and patches holes without invoking semantic dispatch.
- Foundry dedupes by ASDL semantic CFG + contract + stencil variant key.
- Byte-identical but semantically different CFGs do not dedupe unless ASDL identity permits it.
- Runtime interpreter/helper stencil calls are rejected.

Disallowed tests:

- protocol stencil emission as success,
- rejection as coverage,
- old descriptor compatibility as a green requirement,
- opcode selector table behavior,
- backend descriptor semantics recovery,
- opaque helper stencils treated as compiled Lua semantics.

## Open Decisions

The following remain open design decisions for the stencil layer:

1. **Stencil bank generation timing**  
   When are stencil banks generated: offline foundry, build-time, ahead-of-run cache, or runtime compilation cache?

2. **Target ABI representation**  
   Exact ASDL shape for calling convention, register classes, stack layout, pointer width, endian, platform, and feature set.

3. **Relocation model**  
   Which relocation kinds are supported, how Cranelift/object relocations map to ASDL `Reloc`, and how unsupported target relocations fail.

4. **Register allocation and placement**  
   Whether placement is fixed before stencil generation, chosen as a variant, or patched through typed holes.

5. **Stack/frame layout**  
   How Lua frame slots, varargs, top, close chain, and temporary locations map to patchable stack offsets.

6. **Cranelift object extraction**  
   How Moonlift/Cranelift object bytes, symbols, sections, and relocations are extracted into `CodeBlobRef`, `Symbol`, `Reloc`, and `PatchHole`.

7. **Variant explosion control**  
   How many semantic/placement/ABI variants the foundry enumerates and how bank size is bounded without hiding semantics.

8. **Invalidation**  
   How stale stencil banks are invalidated when ASDL schemas, semantic CFGs, contracts, target ABI, Cranelift version, or runtime layout changes.

9. **External effects**  
   Which external symbols are legal for allocator, GC barriers, C calls, errors, and yields, and how they avoid interpreter handoff.

10. **Executable memory policy**  
    How materialized code memory is allocated, patched, protected, cached, and reclaimed.

11. **Bank indexing format**  
    Exact stable binary/index format for `BankIndex`, `VariantKey`, code blobs, and materialization metadata.

12. **Whole-function vs window stencil boundaries**  
    Whether stencils materialize whole-function CFGs or window CFGs with typed state/deopt exits.

## Summary

The architecture is now:

```text
LuaSrc
  -> LuaRT / LuaExec
  -> MoonCFG
  -> StencilIR / StencilTemplate ASDL
  -> binary stencil bank
  -> runtime copy + patch
```

The previous ASDL-only MoonCFG plan was incomplete because it did not include the retained copy-and-patch backend goal. The old Copy-Link-Patch ABI remains retired because it encoded or recovered semantics in backend descriptors. The new stencil backend keeps copy-and-patch, but makes stencils compiled artifacts of explicit ASDL semantic CFGs, with typed patch holes and mechanical runtime materialization only.

       StackOperand = (
         Stencil.Name frame,
         number slot,
         number byte_offset,
         number width_bytes
       ) unique

       ImmediateOperand =
           ImmI64(number value) unique
         | ImmF64(number value) unique
         | ImmBool(boolean value) unique
         | ImmSymbol(Stencil.Symbol symbol) unique
         | ImmBytes(string hash, number byte_size) unique

       Operand =
           RegisterOp(Stencil.RegisterOperand reg) unique
         | StackOp(Stencil.StackOperand stack) unique
         | ImmediateOp(Stencil.ImmediateOperand imm) unique
         | SymbolOp(Stencil.Symbol symbol) unique

       Placement = (
         Stencil.RegisterOperand* fixed_registers,
         Stencil.StackOperand* stack_slots,
         Stencil.Operand* operands
       ) unique

       MaterializationPlan = (
         Stencil.PatchSite* patch_sites,
         Stencil.LinkStep* link_steps,
         Stencil.EntryPoint entry
       ) unique

       PatchSite = (
         Stencil.PatchHole hole,
         Stencil.PatchValue value
       ) unique

       PatchValue =
           PatchImmediate(Stencil.ImmediateOperand imm) unique
         | PatchStack(Stencil.StackOperand stack) unique
         | PatchRegister(Stencil.RegisterOperand reg) unique
         | PatchSymbol(Stencil.Symbol symbol) unique
         | PatchComputed(Stencil.Name name) unique

       LinkStep =
           ResolveInternalBranch(Stencil.Symbol from, Stencil.Symbol to) unique
         | ResolveInternalCall(Stencil.Symbol from, Stencil.Symbol to) unique
         | ResolveExternalSymbol(Stencil.Symbol symbol) unique
         | ApplyReloc(Stencil.Reloc reloc) unique

       EntryPoint = (
         Stencil.Symbol symbol,
         Stencil.TargetABI abi
       ) unique

       Linkage = (
         Stencil.Symbol* exported,
         Stencil.Symbol* imported,
         Stencil.Reloc* required_relocs
       ) unique
   }
   ```

**Patterns**
- Stencil ASDL is backend artifact metadata only.
- No opcode names, protocol exits, `out_tag`, `sponbank`, or old descriptors.

**Danger zones**
- Do not reference nonexistent `LuaExec` ASDL directly yet. Keying modules can accept LuaExec nodes later when that module exists.
- Do not make `StencilKind` encode Lua opcode semantics.

   function M.stencil_module(module)
     local errors = {}
     if pvm.classof(module) ~= T.Stencil.StencilModule then add(errors, "expected Stencil.StencilModule") end
     return #errors == 0, errors
   end

   function M.stencil_template(template)
     local errors = {}
     if pvm.classof(template) ~= T.Stencil.StencilTemplate then add(errors, "expected Stencil.StencilTemplate") end
     return #errors == 0, errors
   end
   ```

## New Files

### `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/stencil_key.lua`

**Purpose**: Stable structural keys for stencil variants/templates/modules.

**Contents sketch**
- Import `pvm`.
- Structural walker like `moon_cfg_key.lua`.
- Functions:
  ```lua
  M.semantic_key(node) -- accepts MoonCFG now; accepts LuaExec if T.LuaExec later exists
  M.variant_key(variant)
  M.template_key(template)
  M.representative_key(semantic_node, contract_key, variant)
  ```
- Elide object byte hashes from semantic representative key unless explicitly computing template identity.

**Guardrails**
- Reject class names/strings matching opcode/protocol/old ABI tokens:
  `OP_`, `Opcode`, `out_tag`, `sponbank`, `SponStencil`, `SponDesc`.

---

### `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/stencil_validate.lua`

**Purpose**: Validate ASDL stencil artifacts fail-closed.

**Contents sketch**
- Imports `pvm`, `lua_compile.validate`, `builders`.
- Validate:
  - `StencilTemplate`, `StencilModule`, `VariantKey`.
  - No forbidden strings: `out_tag`, `out_event_kind`, `call`, `generic_for`, `setlist`, `getvarg`, `sponbank`, `SponDesc`, `SponStencil`, `OpcodeHelper`, `HelperCall`.
  - No opcode-shaped template/key names: `^OP_`, `opcode`, `CALLProtocol`, etc.
  - `PatchHole.width_bytes > 0`.
  - `PatchHole.offset >= 0`, `Reloc.offset >= 0`, symbol offsets >= 0.
  - `CodeBlobRef.byte_size > 0` and `content_hash` has stable prefix such as `sha256:`.
  - All `PatchSite.hole` values correspond to declared holes.
  - All relocation symbols resolve through local/import/export linkage.
  - `EntryPoint.symbol` resolves.
  - `RuntimeBoundaryStencil` rejected unless caller passes explicit `allow_runtime_boundary = true`.
- Exports:
  ```lua
  M.validate_template(template, opts)
  M.validate_module(module, opts)
  M.validate_variant_key(variant, opts)
  ```

---

### `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/stencil_materialization_plan.lua`

**Purpose**: Build `Stencil.VariantKey`, `MaterializationPlan`, and patch-site maps from validated metadata.

**Contents sketch**
- Helpers:
  ```lua
  M.name(s)
  M.default_target_abi()
  M.default_feature_set()
  M.empty_placement()
  M.variant_for_kernel(kernel, contract, opts)
  M.plan(entry_symbol, holes, patch_values, link_steps)
  M.template(args)
  ```
- `variant_for_kernel` uses:
  - `Stencil.KernelStencil`
  - `kernel.kind`
  - passed `contract`
  - explicit target ABI/features/placement
- Does not generate code bytes.

---

### `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/stencil_object_extract.lua`

**Purpose**: Adapter boundary for future object-byte extraction.

**Contents sketch**
- Accept explicit object metadata table:
  ```lua
  {
    code = { symbol, byte_size, content_hash },
    symbols = {...},
    holes = {...},
    relocs = {...},
  }
  ```
- Build ASDL `CodeBlobRef`, `Symbol`, `PatchHole`, `Reloc`.
- Validate through `stencil_validate`.
- No Cranelift/Moonlift invocation here.
- No dummy code blob generation.

## Order of Operations

1. **Schema first**: add `Stencil` ASDL module; update builders/basic validate/schema test.
2. **Validation/key layer**: add `stencil_key.lua`, `stencil_validate.lua`, `stencil_materialization_plan.lua`; add stencil tests.
3. **Foundry key integration**: add `stencil_foundry.lua`; update `lua_compile_foundry.lua`, worker/build merge, foundry tests.
4. **Facade/pipeline**: expose modules in `init.lua`; update pipeline planned list.
5. **Docs/guardrails**: update Copy-Link-Patch/architecture docs and Makefile messages.
6. **Object extraction adapter**: add adapter and tests using explicit metadata only.
7. **Binary stencil bank/materialization**: defer executable bank generation until real object extraction exists; do not fabricate code blobs.

---

## Testing Strategy

Run after each stage:

1. Schema:
   ```sh
   luajit experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/tests/test_spongejit_lua_compile_schema.lua
   ```

2. Stencil validator/key:
   ```sh
   luajit experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/tests/test_spongejit_lua_compile_stencil.lua
   ```

3. Foundry:
   ```sh
   luajit experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/tests/test_spongejit_lua_compile_foundry.lua
   ```

4. Existing MoonCFG stability:
   ```sh
   luajit experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/tests/test_spongejit_lua_compile_moon_out.lua
   ```

5. Main suite:
   ```sh
   cd experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit && make test
   ```

6. Guardrail greps:
   ```sh
   rg -n "out_tag|out_event_kind|sponbank|SponDesc|SponStencil|OpcodeHelper|HelperCall" experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile
   ```

## Pattern Memo

- Stencils are ASDL backend artifacts, not semantic descriptors.
- Foundry identity is `LuaExec/MoonCFG structural key + LuaContract + Stencil.VariantKey`.
- No opcode-shaped stencil keys.
- No old Copy-Link-Patch ABI compatibility.
- No fake `CodeBlobRef`; object bytes appear only through explicit extraction metadata.
- Current MoonCFG tests must remain green throughout.

## Documenter Output — 2026-06-02 16:05:07

# Addendum: Moonlift Copy-and-Patch Executor Boundary

**Source:** `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/SPONJIT_MOONLIFT_COPY_PATCH_DESIGN.md`  
**Workflow:** `wf-b7b79a56`

## Goal

Clarify the final copy-and-patch execution boundary for SpongeJIT: Lua semantics and MoonCFG remain compiler-side ASDL products, while the runtime bank lookup/materialization executor is Moonlift code over Moonlift structs/unions that copies, patches, protects, and publishes native stencil bytes without interpreting Lua or recovering Lua semantics.

## Incentives

The workflow already established that accepted compilation must not depend on protocol exits, interpreter fallback, or backend descriptors that imply semantics. This addendum clarifies the retained fast-path goal: copy-and-patch stencils are still desired, but the retired C descriptor/bank ABI must not return. The replacement is a typed Moonlift executor and typed bank data layout whose fields describe materialization facts only: keys, byte blobs, patch holes, relocations, offsets, widths, and memory permissions.

## Current State

The reset currently distinguishes semantic compiler products from backend artifacts:

```text
LuaSrc / LuaSem / LuaExec / LuaContract
  -> MoonCFG ASDL
  -> Stencil metadata
  -> binary stencil artifacts
```

The important boundary clarified here is:

| Layer | Representation | Responsibility |
|---|---|---|
| Lua semantics | ASDL | Lua meaning, semantic choices, continuations |
| Facts/contracts | ASDL | specialization evidence, obligations, invalidation |
| MoonCFG | ASDL | executable semantic CFG shape |
| Stencil metadata | ASDL/offline + runtime layout | compiled bytes, holes, relocs, keys |
| Executor | Moonlift structs/unions/functions | lookup, copy, patch, protect, publish |

ASDL remains the source of semantic identity. Moonlift runtime types are the source of truth for materialization layout.

## Chosen Target

The chosen pipeline is:

```text
Offline / foundry side
----------------------
PUC bytecode window + fact combinations
  -> LuaSrc ASDL
  -> LuaFact ASDL
  -> LuaExec / LuaSem ASDL
  -> LuaContract ASDL
  -> MoonCFG ASDL
  -> Moonlift source / Cranelift object code
  -> Stencil metadata
  -> binary BankImage

Runtime side
------------
current bytecode window + observed facts
  -> TileKey + FactSignature
  -> lookup BankIndex
  -> copy CodeBlob bytes
  -> apply PatchHole / Reloc values
  -> protect executable memory
  -> publish MaterializedCode
  -> call native fast path
```

The runtime selector may use opcode-window identity and observed facts as key material through `TileKey` and `FactSignature`, but it must not recover Lua meaning from opcodes. Semantic lowering already happened offline through ASDL.

Runtime Moonlift types include materialization-only structures such as:

- `TileKey`
- `FactSignature`
- `LookupResult`
- `PatchKind`
- `PatchHole`
- `RelocKind`
- `Reloc`
- `CodeBlob`
- `StencilTemplate`
- `BankIndexEntry`
- `BankImage`
- `PatchValues`
- `MaterializedCode`

Executor regions/functions are small typed Moonlift units:

```text
lookup_template(bank, key) -> LookupResult
allocate_rx(template) -> AllocationResult
copy_blob(dst, template)
apply_patch_holes(dst, template, values) -> PatchResult
apply_relocs(dst, template, bank) -> PatchResult
protect_executable(dst) -> PublishResult
materialize(bank, key, values) -> MaterializeResult
```

The executor may use Moonlift externs for OS/libc operations:

```moonlift
extern mmap(...)
extern mprotect(...)
extern munmap(...)
extern memcpy(...)
extern memcmp(...)
```

These externs are platform/materialization operations only. They are not Lua semantic helpers.

`MaterializeResult` and related results should be Moonlift tagged unions, so failures are typed materialization failures such as lookup miss, allocation failure, patch failure, relocation failure, or protection failure. They are not Lua semantic fallback paths.

## Guardrails

- Runtime materializer is semantics-blind.
- No opcode dispatch in executor or stencil metadata.
- No protocol `out_tag` ABI.
- No interpreter/helper stencil calls.
- Lua semantic choices must exist in ASDL/MoonCFG before codegen.
- Facts select specializations; facts do not replace semantics.
- Patch holes are typed materialization sites only.
- Stencil keys derive from ASDL semantic CFG, contracts, and target layout.
- Moonlift structs/unions define runtime bank layout.
- Externs are OS/libc/platform operations, not Lua fallback.

## Open Decisions

- Exact binary serialization format for `BankImage`.
- Whether bank images are memory-mapped directly into Moonlift structs or loaded through a verifier/relocator.
- Exact key hashing strategy and collision handling.
- Exact mapping from MoonCFG regions to stencil template boundaries.
- How executable memory lifetime and cache invalidation are represented.
- Whether materialized code is whole-window, whole-function, or region-level.
- How target-specific relocation support is enumerated and validated.

# Addendum: First-Class LuaJIT-Quality FFI for SpongeJIT

**Workflow ID:** `wf-b7b79a56`  
**Source:** `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/SPONJIT_FFI_DESIGN.md`

## Goal

Make Lua FFI a first-class part of SpongeJIT Lua runtime semantics and stencil generation: `ffi.cdef`, `ffi.load`, `ffi.C`, `ffi.new`, `ffi.cast`, `ffi.typeof`, field/index access, C calls, callbacks, finalizers, and cdata identity must lower through explicit typed semantic data/control into `LuaExec` / `MoonCFG` and then into typed stencil facts and patch holes, with LuaJIT-class ergonomics and performance but no hidden interpreter dispatch.

## Incentives

The existing workflow already rejects protocol exits, opaque helpers, backend semantic descriptors, and rejection-as-success. FFI needs the same discipline because LuaJIT-style FFI can otherwise become a large hidden semantic escape hatch: string declarations, dynamic symbol lookup, untyped `ptr(u8)` calls, runtime field lookup, generic callback dispatch, or C/Rust side tables could smuggle semantics outside ASDL. The design therefore treats FFI not as a side library but as Lua runtime semantics: C declarations become typed data, operations become typed control regions, and hot paths become signature/layout/symbol-specialized `MoonCFG` and stencil artifacts.

## Current State

The workflow target is now:

```text
LuaSrc
  -> LuaRT / LuaExec
  -> MoonCFG
  -> StencilIR / StencilTemplate ASDL
  -> binary stencil bank
  -> runtime copy + patch
```

This addendum inserts FFI as an explicit semantic subsystem inside that pipeline:

```text
Lua ffi API call / cdef source
  -> FFI declaration/type model
  -> FFI registry + symbol table
  -> cdata values and operations
  -> LuaExec / MoonCFG regions
  -> Moonlift / Cranelift calls, loads, stores
  -> stencil templates with symbol/offset/ABI patch holes
```

The Moonlift VM owns the FFI runtime. No FFI operation may be implemented by calling LuaJIT FFI, asking the host interpreter, or using opaque runtime helpers that hide type/layout/call semantics.

## Chosen Target

### Types-first / explicit-programming rule

FFI has two explicit trees:

- **Data tree:** C declarations, types, layouts, libraries, symbols, cdata values, callbacks, ownership/finalizer state, ABI/calling-convention facts, diagnostics.
- **Control tree:** cdef parsing, type interning, layout computation, library loading, symbol resolution, cdata allocation, casts, field/index access, C calls, callback entry, finalizer attach/run, and explicit error continuations.

Every meaningful alternative is represented as a typed union variant or a region continuation. There are no status strings, integer semantic tags, or hidden global side tables.

### Data tree

The FFI runtime data model includes typed handles:

```moonlift
struct CTypeId        id: u64 end
struct CDeclId        id: u64 end
struct CLibId         id: u64 end
struct CSymbolId      id: u64 end
struct CCallbackId    id: u64 end
struct CMetatypeId    id: u64 end
```

Core data concepts:

- `CScalarKind`: C scalar variants such as `c_int`, `c_uint64`, `c_double`, `c_size_t`.
- `CType`: scalar, pointer, array, incomplete array, function, struct, union, enum, typedef, opaque tag.
- `CAbi`: explicit ABI variants such as `system_v_amd64`, `win64`, `aarch64_sysv`, `cdecl`, `stdcall`.
- `CRecordLayout`: fields, bitfields, flexible array members, size, alignment, packed/complete state.
- `CEnumLayout`: enum representation and items.
- `CLib` / `CSymbol`: typed dynamic library and symbol handles; function and data symbols are distinct.
- `CData`: explicit `ctype`, storage kind, finalizer, metatype.
- `CStorageKind`: inline bytes, external pointer, owned heap, borrowed Lua buffer, static symbol.
- `CFinalizer` / `OwnershipState`: typed ownership and finalizer state.
- `CCallback`: signature, Lua callable reference, thunk address, liveness.
- `FFIRegistry`: explicit registry of types, records, enums, names, libraries, symbols, callbacks.

### Control tree

FFI operations lower to typed regions with explicit continuations:

- `ffi_cdef`: parse declarations, intern declarations, compute layout, report parse/unsupported/layout errors.
- `intern_ctype`: intern and resolve C types.
- `ffi_typeof`, `ffi_sizeof`, `ffi_alignof`, `ffi_offsetof`: typed type/layout queries.
- `ffi_load`, `ffi_resolve_symbol`: dynamic library and symbol resolution.
- `ffi_new`, `ffi_cast`: allocation and conversion.
- `ffi_get_field`, `ffi_set_field`, `ffi_index`: field/element access with typed failure paths.
- `ffi_call`: C function call with signature/ABI-specific lowering.
- `ffi_make_callback`, `ffi_callback_enter`: typed callback creation and C-to-Lua entry.
- `ffi_gc_attach`, `ffi_run_finalizer`: finalizer ownership changes and execution.

Hot JIT/stencil lowering must specialize by signature and ABI. A generic source-level `ffi_call` region may exist, but hot stencils must not call an opaque `execute_ffi_call(symbol, args)` helper that hides ABI conversion and argument/result handling.

### LuaJIT-like API surface

The Lua-visible API should feel like LuaJIT FFI:

```lua
local ffi = require("ffi")
ffi.cdef[[ ... ]]
local C = ffi.C
local lib = ffi.load("libc.so.6")
local T = ffi.typeof("struct foo")
local x = ffi.new("struct foo[?]", n)
local p = ffi.cast("uint8_t *", x)
ffi.sizeof(T)
ffi.alignof(T)
ffi.offsetof(T, "field")
ffi.istype(T, x)
ffi.gc(x, finalizer)
ffi.metatype(T, methods)
```

Strings are allowed at the Lua surface for compatibility, but after parsing they must not remain as semantic selectors. Internally, all declarations, types, layouts, fields, symbols, calls, callbacks, and finalizers are typed runtime objects.

### Stencil and fact integration

FFI facts participate in specialization and stencil selection when relevant. Examples include:

```moonlift
ffi_type_eq(value_slot: u32, type_id: CTypeId)
ffi_symbol_resolved(symbol: CSymbolId, address: ptr(u8))
ffi_layout_eq(type_id: CTypeId, layout_hash: u64)
ffi_callback_live(callback: CCallbackId)
```

FFI-specific patch holes include:

```moonlift
ffi_symbol_addr64(symbol: CSymbolId)
ffi_field_offset32(type_id: CTypeId, field: CNameId)
ffi_sizeof_imm32(type_id: CTypeId)
ffi_alignof_imm32(type_id: CTypeId)
ffi_callback_thunk64(callback: CCallbackId)
```

A stencil for `libc.memcpy(dst, src, n)` is keyed by typed function signature, ABI, symbol identity, and target ABI. It is not keyed by the string `"memcpy"` alone and not by Lua opcode shape.

### Performance requirements

LuaJIT-quality FFI requires:

- hot FFI calls specialize by C signature and ABI;
- field offsets and sizes become constants or patch holes;
- symbol addresses resolve once and become typed patch values or relocations;
- cdata loads/stores lower to `MoonCFG` memory operations;
- no generic vararg boxing loop unless the C signature is genuinely variadic;
- callbacks use precompiled typed thunks;
- layout and ABI decisions are visible typed facts, not hidden runtime lookups.

### Forbidden patterns

Accepted FFI semantics and stencils must not use:

- LuaJIT FFI as implementation;
- opaque `ffi_do(op_string, args)` helpers;
- runtime field lookup by string in hot stencil paths;
- C calls through untyped `ptr(u8)` without signature identity;
- cdata represented as black-box Lua tables;
- callback dispatch through a generic interpreter frame without typed thunk;
- ABI decisions encoded as raw integer constants instead of `CAbi`;
- C/Rust side tables that hide layout decisions;
- backend stencil descriptors that recover FFI semantics outside ASDL.

### Moonlift extern vs Lua-visible FFI

Moonlift `extern` and Lua FFI are distinct:

```text
Moonlift extern:
  typed import used by Moonlift code and runtime implementation.

Lua FFI:
  Lua-visible dynamic API that parses C declarations and creates cdata,
  symbol, call, callback, finalizer, and layout semantics for Lua programs.
```

The FFI runtime may use Moonlift externs for platform services such as `dlopen`, `dlsym`, `mmap`, or libc helpers. Those externs are implementation tools, not the Lua FFI semantic model.

## Positive Testing Policy

Main tests should assert intended positive behavior:

- parse `cdef` and query type layout;
- allocate struct cdata and read/write fields;
- cast pointers and index memory;
- load libc and call a typed symbol;
- attach and observe finalizer execution;
- create callback and call through C/function-pointer path;
- generate stencil for an FFI call with no generic FFI helper dispatch;
- verify field-offset stencil uses typed layout facts and patch holes.

Malformed cdefs and invalid casts may have validator/error tests, but they must not be used to claim feature completion.

## Open Questions

- Exact C parser subset and LuaJIT syntax compatibility target.
- Full bitfield behavior across ABIs.
- Variadic C calls and default argument promotions.
- `long double` and complex number support.
- Callback lifetime and GC interaction.
- Metatype/method semantics and interaction with Lua metamethod lookup.
- Cross-platform ABI coverage order.
- Whether the FFI registry is per Lua state, shared immutable plus per-state dynamic, or bank-generated.

# Addendum: First-Class GC Semantic Subsystem for SpongeJIT

**Workflow ID:** `wf-b7b79a56`  
**Source:** `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/SPONJIT_GC_DESIGN.md`

## Goal

Make garbage collection a first-class Lua VM semantic subsystem in SpongeJIT: allocation, tracing, barriers, weak tables, finalization, GC epochs, invalidation, FFI ownership, and stencil specialization must be represented as explicit typed data/control in `LuaExec` / `MoonCFG` and related stencil facts, not hidden behind allocator calls, side tables, opaque helpers, or backend conventions.

## Incentives

The existing workflow already rejects protocol handoffs, interpreter fallback, hidden helpers, stringly semantic tags, and backend descriptors that recover Lua meaning outside ASDL. GC needs the same treatment because Lua-visible behavior depends on GC semantics: object lifetime, finalizers, weak table reachability, write barriers, cdata ownership, callback roots, materialized-code roots, and invalidation epochs can all affect correctness. Treating GC as “just allocation” would recreate the rejected escape-hatch pattern: table writes could omit barriers, finalizers could be untyped callbacks, stencil fast paths could skip GC work without contracts, and fact collection could mutate collector state. The chosen framing is explicit programming: data types first, then control regions, with typed outcomes instead of boolean success returns.

## Current State

The broader SpongeJIT architecture in workflow `wf-b7b79a56` has moved toward:

```text
LuaSrc
  -> LuaRT / LuaExec
  -> MoonCFG
  -> StencilIR / StencilTemplate ASDL
  -> binary stencil bank
  -> runtime copy + patch
```

Within that architecture:

- Lua semantics must be ASDL-visible.
- `MoonCFG` is the mechanical compiled CFG product.
- Stencil metadata is a backend artifact layer, not a semantic descriptor layer.
- FFI is already framed as a first-class semantic subsystem, including cdata, callbacks, finalizers, ABI facts, and typed stencil holes.
- Facts and contracts may specialize paths, but may not execute or replace semantics.

The GC addendum extends this same rule to memory management. GC is not an implementation detail under `Allocator`; it is part of Lua VM behavior. Any accepted semantic path that allocates, mutates collectable references, observes finalizer state, depends on weak table behavior, or embeds GC references in materialized code must expose that behavior through typed GC state, regions, facts, and contracts.

## Chosen Target

### Approach

GC is treated as a first-class Moonlift subsystem owned by the Lua VM and integrated into SpongeJIT semantic lowering, FFI, fact collection, and copy-and-patch stencils.

The one-sentence architecture is:

```text
Lua allocation / mutation / FFI ownership
  -> GC allocation and barrier regions
  -> object graph + epochs + finalizer queues
  -> LuaExec/MoonCFG semantic regions
  -> stencil contracts/facts
  -> runtime invalidation when GC/layout/epoch facts change
```

This preserves the workflow’s core rule: semantics live in typed ASDL/MoonCFG-visible structures; backend/runtime mechanisms only materialize already-decided behavior.

---

## Data Tree

GC data must be explicit typed data.

### Object headers

Every collectable object begins with a typed `GCHeader`:

```moonlift
union GCColor
    white0()
  | white1()
  | gray()
  | black()
  | fixed()
  | dead()
end

union GCObjectKind
    string()
  | table()
  | closure()
  | proto()
  | thread()
  | userdata()
  | cdata()
  | upvalue()
end

struct GCHeader
    next: ptr(GCHeader)
    kind: GCObjectKind
    color: GCColor
    flags: u32
    epoch: u64
end
```

If colors/kinds lower to compact integer tags, the mapping must be generated from typed union variants, not maintained as magic numbers.

### GC state

Collector state is explicit and passed to regions:

```moonlift
union GCPhase
    pause()
  | propagate()
  | atomic()
  | sweep_string()
  | sweep_objects()
  | call_finalizers()
end

struct GCLimits
    pause_debt: i64
    step_multiplier: i32
    emergency_threshold: u64
end

struct GCLists
    all: ptr(GCHeader)
    gray: ptr(GCHeader)
    gray_again: ptr(GCHeader)
    weak_tables: ptr(GCHeader)
    ephemeron_tables: ptr(GCHeader)
    finalizable: ptr(GCHeader)
    to_finalize: ptr(GCHeader)
end

struct GCState
    phase: GCPhase
    current_white: GCColor
    lists: GCLists
    total_bytes: u64
    debt: i64
    limits: GCLimits
    global_epoch: u64
    barrier_epoch: u64
    allocator: Allocator
end
```

There is no hidden global collector state outside typed `GCState`.

### Allocator

Allocation is explicit through an allocator interface:

```moonlift
struct Allocator
    ctx: ptr(u8)
    alloc_fn: func(ptr(u8), u64, u32) -> ptr(u8)
    realloc_fn: func(ptr(u8), ptr(u8), u64, u64, u32) -> ptr(u8)
    free_fn: func(ptr(u8), ptr(u8), u64, u32) -> void
end
```

Raw libc allocation may be wrapped, but allocation sites must not silently bypass GC protocols.

### Collectable objects

Object layouts are typed and GC-headered. Representative sketches include:

- `TString`: hash, length, bytes.
- `Table`: shape, metatable, array/hash parts, table/shape epochs.
- `LClosure`: proto and upvalues.
- `Userdata`: metatable, payload, finalizer.
- `CDataObject`: `CTypeId`, storage, FFI finalizer.

Exact VM layouts remain layout-design work, but they must be built from explicit typed fields.

### `TValue` and `GCRef`

Lua values carry collectability through typed tag/payload contracts:

```moonlift
union TValueTag
    nil()
  | bool()
  | i64()
  | f64()
  | string()
  | table()
  | closure()
  | userdata()
  | cdata()
  | thread()
  | lightuserdata()
end

struct TValue
    tag: TValueTag
    payload: u64
end

union GCRef
    none()
  | object(ptr(GCHeader))
end
```

GC traversal uses typed projection helpers. Ad-hoc tag tests scattered across semantic code are forbidden.

### Roots

Roots are typed:

```moonlift
union RootKind
    stack_slot(thread: ptr(LuaThread), slot: u32)
  | registry()
  | global_table()
  | metatable_cache()
  | open_upvalue(ptr(Upvalue))
  | c_callback(CCallbackId)
  | jit_materialized_code(TemplateId)
end

struct GCRoot
    kind: RootKind
    value: GCRef
end

struct RootSet
    roots: view(GCRoot)
end
```

Materialized JIT code is a root when it owns object references or callback thunks. Patch values that refer to GC-managed objects must also have typed root or invalidation representation.

### Barriers

Barriers are semantic write obligations:

```moonlift
union BarrierKind
    object_to_object(parent: ptr(GCHeader), child: ptr(GCHeader))
  | table_slot(table: ptr(Table), value: TValue)
  | upvalue_write(upvalue: ptr(Upvalue), value: TValue)
  | cdata_ref(owner: ptr(CDataObject), child: ptr(GCHeader))
end

union BarrierAction
    no_action()
  | mark_child(child: ptr(GCHeader))
  | regray_parent(parent: ptr(GCHeader))
  | enqueue_gray_again(parent: ptr(GCHeader))
end
```

A table/upvalue/cdata reference write is incomplete unless its barrier behavior is represented.

### Finalizers

Finalizers are typed GC protocol participants:

```moonlift
union FinalizerKind
    lua_gc_metamethod(method: TValue)
  | ffi_c_finalizer(symbol: CSymbolId)
  | ffi_lua_finalizer(ref: u64)
  | userdata_finalizer(method: TValue)
end

struct FinalizerRef
    kind: FinalizerKind
    attached: bool
end

union FinalizerResult
    completed()
  | yielded()
  | error(code: u32)
end
```

Lua `__gc`, userdata finalizers, and FFI `ffi.gc` finalizers enter the same explicit GC finalization surface.

### GC facts

GC facts may specialize JIT/stencil behavior:

```moonlift
union GCFact
    barrier_clean(subject: FactSubject)
  | object_epoch(object: ptr(GCHeader), epoch: u64)
  | table_epoch(table: ptr(Table), epoch: u64)
  | shape_epoch(shape: u64, epoch: u64)
  | gc_phase(phase: GCPhase)
  | no_finalizer(object: ptr(GCHeader))
  | finalizer_attached(object: ptr(GCHeader))
end
```

These are selection and invalidation facts. They do not replace allocation, barrier, traversal, or finalizer semantics.

---

## Control Tree

GC control is modeled as typed Moonlift regions with explicit continuations.

### Allocation

```moonlift
region gc_alloc(
    gc: ptr(GCState),
    kind: GCObjectKind,
    size: u64,
    align: u32;

    allocated: cont(object: ptr(GCHeader)),
    step_required: cont(debt: i64),
    out_of_memory: cont(size: u64),
    emergency_collect_required: cont())
```

A caller receiving `step_required` must perform or forward GC stepping. It may not silently allocate through raw libc.

### Collector stepping

Collector phases are explicit:

```moonlift
region gc_step(gc: ptr(GCState), budget: u64;
    progressed: cont(remaining_budget: u64),
    completed_cycle: cont(),
    finalizers_pending: cont(count: u64),
    out_of_memory: cont())
```

Phase-specific regions include:

- `gc_mark_roots`
- `gc_propagate_one`
- `gc_atomic`
- `gc_sweep_step`

### Mark traversal

Marking and traversal are typed:

- `mark_value`
- `mark_object`
- `traverse_object`

Object-kind dispatch is a typed branch over `GCObjectKind`, not an opaque helper.

### Write barriers

Generic and specialized barriers are regions:

```moonlift
region gc_write_barrier(
    gc: ptr(GCState),
    barrier: BarrierKind;

    clean: cont(),
    child_marked: cont(child: ptr(GCHeader)),
    parent_regrayed: cont(parent: ptr(GCHeader)),
    barrier_error: cont(code: u32))
```

Specialized forms include `table_write_barrier` and `upvalue_write_barrier`.

### Finalization

Finalizer control is explicit:

- `enqueue_finalizer`
- `run_one_finalizer`
- `run_finalizers`

If finalizers may yield for the targeted Lua semantics, yield is a typed continuation. If they may not yield, yielding is an explicit error continuation.

### Weak tables / ephemerons

Weak-table and ephemeron behavior is typed:

- `process_weak_table`
- `process_ephemeron_table`

Weakness mode is a typed table/metatable fact, not a string checked ad hoc.

---

## Integration with Lua Semantics

Allocation-producing Lua operations must use GC allocation regions:

- string creation and concat;
- table creation;
- closure creation;
- userdata and cdata creation;
- vararg/multivalue storage when heap-backed;
- callback/thunk objects;
- boxed heap values.

Reference-writing Lua operations must include barriers:

- table raw set;
- table `__newindex` paths that eventually write;
- upvalue writes;
- global/environment writes;
- cdata/userdata reference field writes;
- closure/upvalue initialization when it crosses color invariants.

A fast path may use a `barrier_clean` fact only if that fact is tied to a contract and invalidation epoch. The generic path must contain the barrier region.

`__close`, `__gc`, FFI finalizers, and error unwinding are interacting but distinct protocols. They must not collapse into one opaque cleanup helper.

---

## Integration with Facts and Stencils

GC facts may specialize stencils but cannot hide GC behavior.

Allowed stencil facts include:

- object/table/shape epochs;
- barrier-clean proofs;
- GC phase invariants;
- no-finalizer or finalizer-attached facts;
- allocator layout/version hash.

Stencil contracts must invalidate when relevant state changes:

- shape/table/metatable epoch;
- GC barrier protocol version;
- object layout version;
- finalizer state;
- allocator or VM ABI epoch.

Patch holes may include:

- GC state pointer;
- allocator function pointer;
- object layout offsets;
- write-barrier region entry address;
- finalizer queue pointer;
- epoch address and expected value.

Patch holes may not mean “skip GC semantics.”

---

## Integration with FFI / CData / Finalizers

FFI cdata participates in GC through typed ownership and finalizer state:

- cdata allocation uses `gc_alloc`;
- `ffi.gc` attaches a typed `FinalizerRef`;
- live callbacks are roots;
- cdata fields containing GC references require barriers;
- finalizer execution has typed `completed`, `yielded`, and `error` outcomes;
- C-owned external memory is not traced unless represented by an explicit owner object with trace/finalizer protocol.

This aligns the GC design with the prior FFI addendum: FFI is not an escape hatch around Lua semantics or GC lifetime rules.

---

## Fact Collector Implications

The runtime fact collector may observe GC state:

- object kind/color;
- table/shape/metatable epochs;
- barrier-clean state;
- finalizer presence;
- object layout/version;
- GC phase when required by a tile.

It must not perform collection steps, barriers, finalization, or mutations as part of observation. Fact collection observes; GC regions mutate.

---

## Testing Policy

Positive intended behavior tests should cover:

- allocating table/string/cdata produces typed collectable objects;
- table writes invoke or validly specialize write barriers;
- GC step transitions through typed phases;
- object graph marking reaches expected objects;
- weak table processing follows typed weak-mode semantics;
- finalizer queues run finalizers with typed outcomes;
- FFI `ffi.gc` finalizers participate in GC;
- stencil fast paths with `barrier_clean` invalidate when epochs change;
- materialized code containing GC references is rooted or invalidated explicitly.

Tests must not count “rejects allocation” or “missing barrier fact” as completion for valid Lua behavior.

---

## Forbidden Patterns

Forbidden in accepted semantics and stencil paths:

- raw allocation in Lua semantic paths;
- hidden global GC state accessed outside typed regions;
- write barriers as optional comments or side tables;
- finalizers as untyped callbacks;
- weak table mode as a string checked in arbitrary code;
- stencils that skip barriers without contract facts;
- fact collector mutating GC state;
- GC helper that performs opaque Lua cleanup semantics;
- FFI finalizers outside the GC protocol.

---

## Open Decisions

The GC design leaves these decisions open:

1. Exact collector algorithm: incremental tri-color, generational, or hybrid.
2. Exact Lua version semantics for finalizer yield/error behavior.
3. Weak table and ephemeron ordering details.
4. Final object layouts for strings, tables, closures, userdata, and cdata.
5. Write barrier style: forward, backward, or both.
6. Emergency collection behavior under allocation failure.
7. Per-thread versus global GC state for coroutines/threads.
8. Interaction with materialized code cache lifetime.
9. Whether stencil banks invalidate every GC cycle or only on relevant epoch changes.

## Summary

GC is a Lua semantic subsystem, not a backend allocator detail. SpongeJIT’s typed semantic path must include explicit GC data structures for headers, colors, phases, roots, barriers, finalizers, object graphs, and facts, plus explicit control regions for allocation, marking, sweeping, weak processing, barriers, and finalization. Facts and stencils may specialize GC-sensitive paths, but they never replace GC semantics.

## Completed

Implemented typed Lua outcome/error boundary for LuaExec → MoonCFG.

Outcome representation:

```moonlift
struct LuaRTOutcome
  kind: i64
  count: i64
  value0: LuaRTValue
  value1: LuaRTValue
  value_buffer: i64
  error_kind: i64
  error_value: LuaRTValue
  saved_pc: i64
  saved_top: i64
  yield_kind: i64
end
```

- Outcome kind mapping centralized in `lua_rt_outcome_model.lua`:
  - `NormalReturnOutcome = 0`
  - `LuaErrorOutcome = 1`
  - `LuaYieldOutcome = 2`
- Error/yield kind mappings are centralized from ASDL constructor names.
- MoonCFG now has explicit outcome construction/projection expressions.
- LuaExec `Return`, `Error`, and `Yield` lower to typed outcomes in outcome mode.
- Executable tests project outcome fields because Moonlift does not yet support direct struct return ABI.
- No `out_tag`, `out_event_kind`, or protocol ABI introduced.

ERRNNIL behavior:
- Implements PUC semantics: error when `R[A] ~= nil`.
- Nil path falls through to closed in-window continuation.
- Non-nil path returns typed `LuaErrorOutcome` with `ErrNnilError`.
- Standalone/no-terminal ERRNNIL is declined structurally.

## Notes

Blockers remain:
- Function-valued metamethods require the Call subsystem before accepted execution.
- GC barriers for table writes are not executable yet.
- Full hash table lookup/insert/resizing, NaN key handling, non-table type metatables, and real string allocation remain future work.
- CONCAT currently uses a documented deterministic synthetic string handle (`payload_i64 = -byte_len`) rather than allocation.

## Worker Output — 2026-06-02 18:14:47

## Completed

Implemented generic Lua `ADD` arithmetic through LuaRT/LuaExec/MoonCFG.

## Exact Generic ADD Semantics

- `IntegerTag + IntegerTag` → `IntegerTag`, integer payload sum.
- `IntegerTag + FloatTag`, `FloatTag + IntegerTag`, `FloatTag + FloatTag` → `FloatTag`, float payload sum.
- Non-numeric operands → typed `LuaErrorOutcome` with `ArithmeticError`.
- String-to-number conversion is **not implemented yet**; string operands currently take the explicit nonnumeric error path.
- `ADD + MMBIN(Add)` is consumed as one semantic unit; numeric success proceeds internally and does not treat `MMBIN` as no-op coverage.
- Standalone/incorrect `MMBIN` does not compile as success.

## Metamethod / Call Status

No opaque helper/protocol handoff was added. `__add` call lowering is still blocked until executable CallRegion/metatable semantics exist. Current accepted arithmetic slice is numeric + typed arithmetic error path; metatable/call execution remains future work.

## Worker Output — 2026-06-02 18:18:31

## Completed
Implemented standalone `ERRNNIL` runtime-check lowering through LuaRT/LuaExec/MoonCFG.

Semantics:
- Checks `LuaRTValue.tag` at runtime.
- `nil` (`NilTag`) → normal typed `LuaRTOutcome`, count `0`.
- non-nil (`IntegerTag`, `FalseTag`, `ShortStringTag`, etc.) → `LuaErrorOutcome` with `ErrNnilError`.
- Closed continuation windows still continue on nil and error on non-nil.
- No facts/evidence required.
- No `out_tag`, `out_event_kind`, protocol handoff, or opaque helper.

`Bx/name_index` remains preserved in `LuaSrc.ERRNNIL.name_index`; current `LuaRTOutcome` has no dedicated name-index payload field.

## Files Changed
- `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/lua_src_to_lua_exec_lower.lua`
  - Allows standalone `ERRNNIL`.
  - Synthesizes explicit nil-success zero-result block.
  - Keeps non-nil path as typed `ErrNnilError`.

- `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/tests/test_spongejit_lua_compile_lua_exec_pipeline.lua`
  - Added standalone `ERRNNIL` executable tests.
  - Added closed-continuation tests.
  - Added `Bx/name_index` preservation assertion.
  - Added emitted-source checks for explicit tag check and no protocol ABI.

## Tests

## Worker Output — 2026-06-02 18:34:24

## Completed
Implemented the next dumb copy-and-patch materialization layer.

Added:
- `Stencil.MaterializedImage`
- `Stencil.MaterializationRecord`
  - `AppliedPatch`
  - `AppliedReloc`
- `lua_compile.stencil_materialize`
  - verifies caller-supplied code bytes by `CodeBlobRef` size/hash
  - accepts byte blobs keyed by `CodeBlobRef`, symbol name, or content hash
  - copies bytes into a materialized image
  - applies `U8/U16/U32/U64/I32/I64` immediate patches
  - applies `Abs64` symbol address patches
  - applies simple `AbsAddr` and `PcRel` relocations
  - fails closed on missing bytes, hash/size mismatch, out-of-range writes, unsupported encodings, unresolved symbols, overflow, and forbidden metadata strings
- Added materialized-image validation.
- Added positive exact-byte materialization tests and negative failure-mode tests.

## Worker Output — 2026-06-02 18:38:32

## Completed
Implemented the next typed stencil bank selector/materializer layer.

Added `lua_compile.stencil_bank` with:
- `build_index(module)`
- `lookup(index, variant_or_key)`
- `select_template(module_or_index, variant_or_key)`
- `materialize(module_or_index, variant_or_key, code_blobs, opts)`
- `_or_error` variants

It enforces:
- unique variant keys
- unique template names
- no ambiguous duplicate entries
- entries resolve templates exactly
- entry key matches template variant
- declared bank variants have entries
- forbidden opcode/protocol/old-backend strings fail closed

Selection/materialization is dumb and deterministic: it only keys by stable `Stencil.VariantKey`, then delegates byte copying/patching to `stencil_materialize`.

## Files Changed
- `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/stencil_bank.lua` - new bank index/selection/materialization API.
- `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/spongejit/lua_compile/init.lua` - exports `stencil_bank`.
- `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/tests/test_spongejit_lua_compile_stencil.lua` - added positive two-template bank selection/materialization tests and negative bank invariant tests.
- `experiments/lua_interpreter_vm/tests/test_spongejit_lua_compile_pipeline.lua` - planned file list includes `stencil_bank.lua`.
